Here, she shelters other victims and creations of Viktra, showing them the esteem their creator denies them. Those in Elise's care have taken to calling themselves the Children (detailed below).



#### Mordenheim's Masterpiece

The Unbreakable Heart is a nonmagical scientific wonder. Despite being the creator of the Unbreakable Heart, Viktra can't re-create it and is obsessed with reclaiming it and rediscovering its secrets.



#### Unbreakable Heart

This heart-shaped, clockwork device installs itself, fastening into place if positioned where a creature's heart used to be. A creature that contains the device is affected as if by the *Raise Dead* spell. After this, the creature is immune to disease, ceases to age, and doesn't die of old age. The Unbreakable Heart glows, shedding *Bright Light* in a 10-foot radius and *Dim Light* for an additional 10 feet. While inside a creature, the device causes the creature to shed Dim Light in a 10-foot radius.



#### The Children

The Children are discarded creations of Dr. Viktra Mordenheim who have found shelter with Elise. Composed a few dozen Constructs and chemically animated Undead, the Children follow Elise's lead and seek to live peacefully away from those who would misunderstand and harm them.

The exception to this is Adam, a *Mordenheim's Monster* who recently joined the Children. Adam was created by Viktra to capture Elise, but Elise convinced him to join her instead. Unlike Elise, Adam was created from disparate parts and knows no previous life. Although Elise seeks to teach Adam humanity, he shows little respect for the lives of more fragile beings. Moreover, Adam is fascinated by Mordenheim's work and quietly seeks ways to create life that will serve him.

![A desperate crew of Ludendorf whalers runs afoul of Rahab, a fleshless leviathan that hunts the Sea of Secrets](book/RHW/140-13-005.sea-of-secrets.webp)



#### Lamordia Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Lamordia often make the characters subjects or accomplices to Viktra's schemes. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2** A dean of Ludendorf University hires the characters to escort the coach of students traveling to an assistantship at Schloss Mordenheim. Along the way, they are plagued by mismatched *Homunculi* that sabotage their travels. These are members of the Children, seeking to stymie folk they take for Mordenheim's allies.
- **Levels 3–6** At Schloss Mordenheim, Viktra Mordenheim hires the character to recover her invention, the Unbreakable Heart. She explains it was stolen by a monster that dwells on the Isles of Agony. Viktra wishes the characters to bring back the heart and the monster. The characters face dangers in the wilds, but the quest culminates in the "Isles of Agony" adventure (see below).

The conclusion of the campaign depends on whether the characters aid Viktra or Elise. When they return to Schloss Mordenheim, events might play out in the following ways:

- **Levels 7–9 (Aiding Viktra)** If the characters aid Dr. Mordenheim, the doctor seeks to remove the Unbreakable Heart from Elise or test it by reanimating a new being. This results in a dramatic operation where an enraged *Mordenheim's Monster* (see x) breaks free and rampages through the castle.
- **Levels 7–9 (Aiding Elise)** If the characters aid Elise, the characters must free innocent victims of the doctor from the castle and prevent Dr. Mordenheim from animating new terrors by destroying her laboratory. Ultimately the characters must face *Viktra Mordenheim* (detailed earlier in x) and two *Flesh Golems* made from the assistants the characters brought to the castle.

The campaign might continue with the characters continuing to aid or being targeted by the Children.



#### Isles of Agony

Adventure for Level 5 Characters

- **Situation** The characters must recover the Unbreakable Heart (detailed earlier in x). They don't know it's inside the outcast Elise.
- **Hook** Viktra hires the characters to recover the Unbreakable Heart, which was stolen by a monster. They are offered 2,500 GP, plus a 1,000 GP bonus if they capture the monster.



#### Encounters

The adventure begins when the characters reach the Isles of Agony and consists of these encounters.



#### Shipwreck

Soon after reaching the icy isles, the characters find six human survivors of a wrecked whaling ship. These sailors (*Pirates*) are led by Mate Herzogin, and their captain was carried off by a half-human, half-machine monster. The survivors seek help returning home but want to recover their captain's corpse (and their pay, which he carried).



#### The Monster

The monster the survivors fear is one of the Children, a *Flesh Golem* named Kartad. He's peaceful, but the survivors' captain, Hans Giesbrecht (Medium *Pirate Captain*), attacked him on sight. Kartad knocked out Hans, panicked, picked him up, and fled to Hope's Heart.



#### Track of the Monster

Characters who succeed on a 12 Wisdom (*Survival*) check find and can follow Kartad's tracks to Hope's Heart. If the characters fail, a survivor points out the path. Roll on or choose results from the following table for three encounters that happen on the way (rerolling duplicates).

| 1d4 | Encounter |
|---|---|
| 1 | Six *Dire Wolves* pursue a *Homunculus*. The homunculus flees as soon as possible. |
| 2 | 1d8 *Zombies* animated by mechanical apparatuses stare into the sky. They are Constructs and don't react, even if harmed. |
| 3 | A *Primeval Owlbear* made of mismatched parts forages for food; it is a Construct. It is *Indifferent* to the characters. |
| 4 | A *Troll* hunts alongside a *Winter Wolf*. |



#### Hope's Heart

Hope's Heart is a hidden canyon home to numerous harmless Constructs that is accessed via a passage in an abandoned cabin. When the characters approach, Elise appears on the cliffs 20 feet above and demands to know their business. Elise is a *Mordenheim's Monster* (see x). The Unbreakable Heart glows from her chest.



#### Fighting Elise

Elise attacks to prevent entry to the cabin and to defend herself. She avoids killing and won't pursue those who flee. If the characters attack, they'll likely have to make multiple attempts to wear down Elise or use trickery to defeat her.



#### Negotiating with Elise

Elise is *Indifferent* to the characters or *Hostile* if they harmed any Constructs on the isle. She's wary of those who working for Viktra and can share the details described in "x." If a character explains they're seeking the missing captain, she brings forth Hans and Kartad. Kartad has nursed Hans back to health; he apologizes and releases the bewildered captain.



#### The Crew

The six survivors arrive to see the characters speaking with Kartad. They overreact on seeing the "monster" and initiate combat. Kartad panics and defends himself. Hans has 10 Hit Points but is too weak to command his crew or fight.



#### Aftermath

If the characters fight alongside the crew, Kartad and Elise defend themselves but flee after 3 rounds or if anyone is killed. Elise leads her followers to hide elsewhere on the island. The sailors thank the characters and offer to help them rally aid in Ludendorf to return and hunt the monsters.

If the characters deescalate the conflict or defend Kartad, Elise's attitude toward them improves. She won't give them the Unbreakable Heart or return to Schloss Mordenheim. Rather, she tries to convince the characters to see Viktra for the villain she is. She entreats them to return to the castle, save captive members of the Children, and thwart the doctor, as detailed in "x." In return, Elise offers a trove of 4,000 GP and an *Immovable Rod*.

Characters who defeat or choose to aid Elise earn a bonus 1,100 XP.



## Mordent

Domain of the Haunted

- **Darklord:** x
- **Adventure Genre:** x
- **Hallmarks:** Ancestral curses, haunted mansions, mist-shrouded moors, vengeful spirits
- **Mist Talismans:** Broken jewelry, death mask, faded love letter, family portrait
- **Aligned Tarokka Card:** Miser
- **Opposed Tarokka Card:** Horseman

In Mordent, the dead don't rest. Here, farmers and fishers toil in scattered villages, cleaving to stoic, hardworking traditions. In the manors of landed, aristocratic families, the bearers of noble names view themselves as conservators of the land and of stifling reputations. Tradition, memory, and expectation haunt the lives of Mordent's people, and when they die, nothing changes.

Little known to the living, the dead in Mordent rise as spirits, and for most—knowing no other ways—their work continues. Abandoned estates hide spectral generations of frustrated nobles and their downtrodden servants. While some spirits drift idly or deteriorate to mere impressions of their past selves, others greedily cling to their former possessions and ambitions. Some pernicious spirits become infamous hauntings, while others—such as the domain's Darklord, the ghostly *Lord Wilfred Godefroy*—seek to dominate the living and dead.



### Domain Features

Mordent is known for the following features:

- **Lingering Spirits** All manner of spectral undead and other hauntings lurk in Mordent. Ghost stories and rumors of haunted sites are common.
- **Local Nobility** Mordent is governed by town mayors and local lords. Few nobles remain, and some have only decrepit manors left to their names.
- **Old Faiths** People casually worship vague deities in Mordent, but evidence of forgotten druidic traditions lies scattered around the wilds.
- **Spiritualism** Attempting to communicate with the dead is a popular pursuit for investigators, bored nobles, and charlatans.
- **Tradition and Shame** The people of Mordent follow traditions that prioritize hard work, self-sufficiency, and avoiding public embarrassment. Locals overlook blatant strangeness so not to shame their neighbors, and every family has secrets.



### Locations in Mordent

Mordent is a foggy land of forests, fields, and moors that endures frequent rainstorms. The land is dotted with tiny farming hamlets and the rotting homes of forgotten nobles.

The town of Mordentshire is detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the Mordent Locations.



#### Mordentshire

Mordentshire is the largest community in Mordent. Sturdy fisherfolk work the town docks and, after dusk, fill crowded tavern common rooms. Cold winds frequently blow in from Arden Bay. When they stop, they're replaced by a shroud of fog the locals call "the breath of the dead."

To the chagrin of the town's no-nonsense populace, Mordentshire is home to a small community of scholars and adventurers. Saulbridge Sanitarium provides a refuge for the ill while also welcoming researchers from other domains. Across town, an unassuming herbalist shop is run by *Rudolph van Richten* (see x), an investigator of all things monstrous and mysterious.

The lands around Mordentshire host two prominent estates. Heather House is the home of the Weathermay family, regional lords who count numerous heroes among their number. To the east stands Gryphon Manor, the notorious House on Gryphon Hill. The mansion has a history of violence, tragedy, and hauntings and is the home of the domain's Darklord, Lord Wilfred Godefroy.

**Mordent Locations**

| Location | Description |
|---|---|
| Abbey Point | A group of silent Ezra worshippers maintain a sanctuary at Abbey Point. Maps there claim that only the sea lies north of the abbey, making the nearby wooded coast a mystery. |
| Blairsbay | Little more than a dock, market, and tavern, Blairsbay serves a line of coastal noble estates. Many of these great homes are abandoned, including Lumley House and Preston Hill. |
| Candle Cross | The hamlet of Candle Cross spills from the remains of a ruined castle, the drawbridge of which extends over the Arden River. The bridge rises of its own accord to bar evil from entering. |
| Crawford | Near the village of Crawford, countless of ravens roost at Crawford Manor. A carving in the manor reads: "The Death of Ravens Shalt Thou Abhor, Lest the Crawford Line Be Nevermore." |
| Glaston | The residents of the village of Glaston cleave to druidic traditions. Rumors say ancient druids forged magical passages between the nearby Sigil Lakes and similar sites in realms beyond. |
| Glenwich | Years ago, the sand cliff that bore half the village of Glenwich—including its ancient church—collapsed into the bay. Locals avoid the tide pools mingling amid dilapidation and the dead. |
| Haworth Hall | Haworth Hall numbers among the domain's dozens of lonely, decaying manors. Something inhabits the estate, but whatever it is terrifies Mordent's ghost and they avoid it at all costs. |
| Idlethorp | Miniature constructs made of stitched-together body parts run amok in this abandoned hamlet's Punchinel Manor, once home to an eccentric inventor. |
| Locustbranch Hospital | Locustbranch was once a renowned hospital, but it was abandoned after a series of mysterious deaths. Now, ghostly patients pack its wards, crying out for cures to eternal ills. |
| Waterford | The hamlet of Waterford stands at a confluence of rivers and roads. Here, the Globe inn quietly keeps a back entrance and rooms to accommodate silent, ghostly travelers. |
| Whelk Spring House | The last of the noble Esker family recently died, bequeathing Whelk Spring House to distant relatives. At low tide, the waters of Bent Key Causeway reveal a muddy path to the estate. |



### Wilfred Godefroy

Darklord Tormented by Ghostly Undeath

![image](book/RHW/145-14-003.wilfred-godefory.webp)

> Speak your piece, then hold your tongue. No fools are more insufferable than the living.

Lord Wilfred Godefroy rules the afterlife of all who die in Mordent. Arrogant, impatient, and vengeful, the Darklord seeks any opportunity to exert his control and reinforce his undying noble standing.

Lord Godefroy haunts the House on Gryphon Hill, along with countless other spirits. Wilfred can send mobs of obedient spirits to do his will anywhere in the domain. He uses his control over the dead to influence the living, threatening to harm his victims' dead loved ones if they don't obey his fickle commands.

A generation ago, the creators of the mist-piercing device called the x vanished from Mordent. Lord Godefroy has discovered the hidden machine, but, to his frustration, lacks a way to use it.


##### Wilfred Godefroy

*M • undead • N E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 8 | 14 | 10 | 13 | 14 | 17 |

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** Common

**Challenge** {"cr":"6","xpLair":2900}

**Traits**

**Darklord Restoration.** If Wilfred dies, he revives with all his *Hit Points* in 1d10 weeks somewhere in Mordent.

**Incorporeal Movement.** Wilfred can move through other creatures and objects as if they were *Difficult Terrain*. He takes 5 (1d10) Force damage if he ends his turn inside an object.

**Legendary Resistance (3/Day, or 4/Day in Domain).** If Wilfred fails a saving throw, he can choose to succeed instead.

**Possessive Aura.** Grasping, ghostly servants surround Wilfred in a 5-foot *Emanation* originating from him. A creature that ends its turn in this area is subjected to the following effect. cha 14. {@actSaveFail} The target has the *Charmed* condition. While the creature is *Charmed* in this way, its *Speed* is reduced to 0. The target repeats the save at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success. After 1 minute, it succeeds automatically.

**Legendary Actions**

**Bone-Chilling Step.** Wilfred teleports up to 60 feet to an unoccupied space he can see, and each creature within 10 feet of the space he left takes 4 (1d8) Necrotic damage. Wilfred can't take this action again until the start of his next turn.

**Fated Bullet.** dex 14, one creature Wilfred can see within 120 feet. {@actSaveFail} 16 (2d12 + 3) Necrotic damage, and the target can't regain *Hit Points* until the start of its next turn. {@actSaveSuccessOrFail} Wilfred can't take this action again until the start of his next turn.

**Slam.** Wilfred makes one *Object* Slam attack.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** Wilfred makes two attacks, using *Object* Slam or Hunting Rifle in any combination.

**Object Slam.** m 6, reach 5 ft. {@h}10 (2d6 + 3) Force damage.

**Hunting Rifle.** r 6, range 40/120 ft. {@h}9 (1d12 + 3) Necrotic damage.

**Reactions**

**Redirect Attack.** {@actTrigger} A creature Wilfred can see makes an attack roll against him. {@actResponse} Wilfred chooses a Small or Medium creature within 5 feet of himself that has the *Charmed* condition. Wilfred and that creature swap places, and the creature becomes the target of the attack instead.



#### Wilfred's Tale

In life, Lord Wilfred Godefroy was an unremarkable minor aristocrat. He inherited the estate of Gryphon Hill near Mordentshire centuries ago by murdering his father and framing it as an accident. During a bloody night years later, the entire Godefroy family—Wilfred; his wife, Estelle; and their daughter, Penelope—died violently. But instead of passing on to the afterlife, the Godefroys' souls lingered at Gryphon Hill. In death, Wilfred is haunted by the ghosts of his family, recent and the past generations, who blame him for their deaths and the family's disgrace.

A generation ago, a mysterious alchemist created a device in Mordent called the x. This magical machine had many fantastic powers, including the ability to open passages between the planes and separate a creature's good and evil natures into separate beings. The Apparatus drew multiple powerful beings to Mordent and eventually attracted the Mists themselves when the device malfunctioned, causing a deadly disaster. The Mists collected Mordent into the Domains of Dread, and the mysterious alchemist vanished. With the departure of mightier beings, Lord Godefroy remained as the land's most fearful villain. He inherited the mantle of Darklord of the new domain of Mordent.

Since then, Wilfred has claimed lordship of all who die in Mordent. He knows the location of the Apparatus and seeks to master its powers, but how to do so and the location of a vital piece of the machine—the Rod of Rastinon—both elude him. He seeks to blackmail anyone who might be able to reveal the device's secrets or find the missing rod. Wilfred forces Alice Weathermay, mayor of Mordentshire, to keep him appraised of useful visitors to the domain, by holding her dead husband, Daniel Foxgrove, hostage.



#### Wilfred's Domain

Mordent is altered by Lord Godefroy's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders** While in his domain, Lord Godefroy can close or open the borders to Mordent. While the borders are closed, the groans and whispers of the dead fill the Mists surrounding Mordent. Creatures in the Mists have the *Deafened* condition.
- **Ears Everywhere** While in his domain, Lord Godefroy can cast *Sending*, requiring no Material components and using Charisma as the spellcasting ability. When casting the spell in this way, Lord Godefroy can target any Undead creature in Mordent, in addition to the usual targets.
- **Spectral Serfs** A Humanoid that dies in Mordent rises 7 days later as a *Specter* under Lord Godefroy's control, unless the Humanoid is restored to life.

If Wilfred dies, these effects end immediately.



#### Wilfred's Lair

The House on Gryphon Hill lies just outside Mordentshire and is home to Lord Wilfred Godefroy. Hundreds of spirits remain bound to the house and the surrounding grounds, and all serve the lord of the house and struggle to stay in his good graces. Spirits that rebel are punished—either forced to face Wilfred's kennel of spectral hounds or dragged into the deepest recesses of the house, which even the eldest spirits fear.



#### House on Gryphon Hill

Cobwebs and dust coat the House on Gryphon Hill. Lurking spirits remain out of sight until trespassers pose a threat or Lord Godefroy orders them to attack. The house has the following features:

- **Basement** Lord Godefroy orders ghostly teams to endlessly dig deeper and wider basements beneath the house. As if creating his own underworld, Wilfred imprisons spirits who displease him in the expanding haunted dungeons beneath the house. Somewhere amid these dungeons, a passage connects to the site where the x is hidden.
- **Haunted Rooms** Estelle and Penelope Godefroy haunt the house's attic, avoiding Wilfred and doing all they can to frustrate the Darklord and stymie his ambitions. The house's other spirits obey Estelle and Penelope unless their commands contradict an order from Wilfred.
- **Withered Estate** Wilfred's ghostly hounds patrol the house's grounds, while spectral groundskeepers tend to dead topiaries and hedges as if they still thrived.



### Adventures in Mordent

Mordent is a realm of ghost stories (see x). Moldering manors, lonely moors, neglected graveyards, and similar gothic sites provide natural settings for encounters with spirits and the tragic dead. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Fog locally known as the breath of the dead obscures mysterious shapes on the streets of Mordentshire](book/RHW/146-14-004.breath-of-death.webp)



#### Horror in Mordent

Adventures in Mordent often include the following elements.



#### The Apparatus

Wilfred is obsessed with control over the dead and the living. He knows where the magical device known as the Apparatus is hidden but has limited understanding of how to use it. Nevertheless, he knows it is powerful and can produce devastating effects. He cares nothing for the machine's remarkable abilities and seeks to use it as a weapon to force all in Mordent to obey him.

To fulfill his goals, Wilfred seeks individuals with magical and alchemical insights, as well as rumors of the Apparatus's missing piece, the Rod of Rastinon. He might threaten or blackmail the living into aiding him. Should he suspect the Rod of Rastinon or other vital information lies beyond Mordent, he might send his agents to other domains.

The Apparatus can exchange souls, open passages through the Mists, and create more dangerous effects, but the magical device might have any properties an adventure demands.



#### Bastion of Heroes

Despite the horrors lurking in Mordent, the domain hosts several quiet, relatively peaceful communities. Characters from Mordent might have had relatively peaceful, mundane lives before mysteries or tragedies led them to adventure. The abandoned estates of Mordent also make fine places to use the rules for Haunted Bastions, detailed in x.



#### Ghosts of Mordent

Ghost stories often involve spirits that linger as the result of some tragedy or unfinished work. In Mordent, spirits linger and might request help from the living. Roll on or choose a result from the Mordent Hauntings table to inspire adventures featuring the lingering dead.

**Mordent Hauntings**

| 1d8 | The Spirit Seeks Aid In... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Freeing a living loved one from possession by another ghost. |
| 2 | Hiding a secret that could embarrass or undermine a living loved one. |
| 3 | Liberating another spirit from the dungeons beneath the House on Gryphon Hill. |
| 4 | Locating a spirit that wanders a broad region or who appears only during the new moon. |
| 5 | Restoring the memory of an ancient spirit that has almost lost its sense of self. |
| 6 | Searching a distant haunted site for a spirit it has been separated from. |
| 7 | Sealing the site of an ancient evil or the lair of a creature that torments spirits. |
| 8 | Smuggling a living relative out of Mordent, away from Wilfred's clutches. |

Even though spirits are trapped in Mordent, many find secluded places where they reflect on nature, their lives, and eternity. Over generations, such spirits often become little more than vague shapes or disembodied voices or emotions before fading away entirely.



#### Van Richten's Herbalist Shop

*Rudolph van Richten* (see x) is the foremost scholar of monsters and strange occurrences in the Domains of Dread. He lives and works from the Mordentshire herbalist shop (see Map 2.27: Van Richten's Herbalist Shop). Beyond the storefront, Rudolph's studies and prepares methods of combating evils plaguing the Land of the Mists. Adventurers might find lore and tools to combat all manner of monsters here.

When absent from his shop, Rudolph leaves it in the care of his protégés, *Gennifer* and *Laurie Weathermay-Foxgrove* (detailed in x) and Beatrice Polk, an elderly local gardener and accomplished detective.



#### Mordent Campaign Arc

Mordent campaigns often involve ghostly mysteries. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2** Caarey Gelthik, a local ne'er-do-well in Mordent, has become a *Ghast* and lurks beneath the town docks. By night, he robs graves to consume the bodies within. The characters take note when silent spirits—perhaps of allies—begin wandering town, each missing limbs, tongues, and other soft features. Only finding and defeating Gelthik causes the dismember spirits to depart.
- **Levels 3–4** Beatrice Polk, caretaker at the Mordentshire herbalist shop, hires the characters to end a haunting afflicting the shop. See the adventure "x."
- **Levels 5–10** Alice Weathermay, mayor of Mordentshire, hires the characters to find a lost piece of local history: the Rod of Rastinon. She shares leads involving various strange sites, but the rod doesn't appear. Eventually, *Lord Godefroy*—who has been working through Alice Weathermay—grows impatient. He threatens the party's dead loved ones, insisting the characters find the rod swiftly and help him use the Apparatus (see 3).



#### The Ghost Hunter's Haunting

Adventure for Level 3 Characters

- **Situation** An accident at x herbalist shop broke a strange relic and unleashed a deadly feline spirit from another domain.
- **Hook** Beatrice Polk, the shop's caretaker, offers the characters 400 GP if they end the haunting.



#### Encounters

This adventure uses map 2.27 and consists of these encounters.



#### Beatrice Polk's Aid

Beyond her folksy politeness and dislike of curse words, Beatrice Polk takes her stewardship of the herbalist shop seriously but doesn't enter the shop during the haunting. She can provide the characters with a number of *Potions of Healing* equal to the party's members. She scuttles plans that involve harming or stealing Rudolph's possessions.



#### Ghost Cat

A *Wraith* that appears as a black cat the size of a panther haunts the shop. Whenever the characters enter a room without monsters present, roll a die. If the number is odd, the cat is in the room. If the cat has more than half its Hit Points, it fights for a round, then flees to another room or floor; otherwise, it flees without attacking. If destroyed, the wraith reappears 24 hours later with full Hit Points. Its threat ends only if the ritual in the cellar is completed.



#### Laboratory

Two *Poltergeists* haunt this room.



#### Stairs

An unnatural wind blows against anyone who tries to ascend either stairway to the second floor. A character must succeed on a 16 Strength (*Athletics*) check to climb the stairs.



#### Dumbwaiter

A dumbwaiter connects the kitchen and the upstairs hall. It can hold one Medium or smaller creature. A creature outside the dumbwaiter can use an action to raise or lower the dumbwaiter and its contents.



#### Upstairs Hall

Broken on the floor is a strange relic: a mummied cat. Shelves nearby hold accounts of Rudolph's travels in a land called 2.



#### Library

Rudolph's library is filled with occult texts. Any character who spends a minute investigating the library finds a copy of Van Richten's Guide to Ghosts. Those who spend at least 10 minutes reading this book and have seen both the relic in the upstairs hall and the ritual room in the cellar understand how to use the cellar room to exorcise the ghostly cat. Additionally, a character who succeeds on a 12 Intelligence (*Investigation*) check finds a *Spell Scroll* of *Protection from Evil and Good*.



#### Guest Room

Standing facing a corner of this room is *Gennifer Weathermay-Foxgrove*. She is possessed by a *Ghost*, which holds her in a catatonic state. Gennifer is freed of her possession if she's affected by a spell like Protection from Evil and Good or if she's removed from the shop. The feline-featured wraith attacks the party if its possession ends or if Gennifer is moved from the room. If freed from the ghost's control, Gennifer is aware of the ghostly cat, as she accidentally broke the relic in the hall. She knows how to exorcise the spirit using the wards in the cellar.



#### Cellar

A room in the cellar is prepared for magic rituals. A character who succeeds on a 12 Intelligence (*Arcana*) check realizes this space is warded to contain or dispel spirits. If the characters place the relic from the upstairs hall within the space, the ghostly cat appears 1 minute later and fights until destroyed. If the cat is defeated here, the relic repairs itself and the haunting ends. Each character gains a bonus 400 XP for ending the haunting.



## Shadowlands

Domain of Faded Glory and False Virtue

- **Darklord:** x
- **Genre:** x
- **Hallmarks:** Cursed magic items, doomed quests, falls from grace, knightly lineages, obsessive zeal
- **Mist Talismans:** Broken holy symbol, religious relic, symbol of the Circle
- **Aligned Tarokka Card:** Torturer
- **Opposed Tarokka Card:** Broken One

For the knights of the Shadowlands, the struggle with evil isn't a philosophical trial—it is an active war. East of the rugged Theospine Mountains spreads the peaceful realm of Nidala, where the virtuous knights of the Circle guard their lands against wickedness beyond and within. To the mountains' west lies the ruined land of Avonleigh, the birthplace of the knightly Circle; this realm fell to evil long ago and has become overgrown by the spirit-stalked Phantasmal Forest. Many knights of the Circle view themselves as inheritors of a legacy of shame. They aspire to the heroism of their storied ancestors and battle to absolve themselves of imagined failures. They throw themselves into crusades against foes, real and imagined, sacrificing their lives—and those of their people—for redemption and glory.

For all the Circle's good intentions, these knights are cursed. Monsters and villains they've defeated reappear in the Shadowlands seeking vengeance. Most infamously, deep in the Phantasmal Forest lingers the evil that caused Avonleigh's downfall: *Ebonbane*, Darklord of the Shadowlands and the sapient sword of the Circle's founder, Kateri Shadowborn.



### Domain Features

The Shadowlands is known for the following features:

- **Bastions on the Borderlands** The Circle seeks to reclaim a foothold in Avonleigh in a region called the Borderlands. They often reward allies with Bastions here (see x and the Dungeon Master's Guide for details on 10).
- **The Circle** The knights of the Circle (described in x) make their home in this domain.
- **Nidala's Ruler** Elena Faith-hold rules Nidala. But this knight is rarely present in the land, as she leads deadly quests beyond the domain's borders (see "x").



### Locations in the Shadowlands

The Shadowlands is a dualistic domain: Avonleigh remains an overtly haunted wilderness home to lurking evils, while Nidala touts itself as the virtuous opposite. But the land's harmony is artificial, its people forced to smile while trapped in the service of Elena Faith-hold and her sycophants. Accordingly, the domain's conflict isn't one of good versus evil, but rather of overt and covert evils.

The Phantasmal Forest is detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the Shadowlands Locations.



#### Phantasmal Forest

The Phantasmal Forest dominates the haunted land of Avonleigh, a shifting, surreal woodland cloaked by perpetual night. A dreamlike place controlled by Ebonbane, the forest changes constantly, and locations within drift like flotsam on a dark sea. The River Avalon and the King's Highway—an overgrown route of misaligned stones—enter the forest, but within the woods they circle endlessly and never leave. Only those descended from the Circle's founding members can navigate the Phantasmal Forest without becoming lost. All others wander at Ebonbane's whim, becoming prey for the wolves, corrupted fey, cursed knights, or wicked souls that haunt the forest.

**Shadowlands Locations**

| Location | Description |
|---|---|
| Banemaw's Lair | After being slain by Elena Faith-hold, the dragon Banemaw returned as a *dracolich*. Elena keeps this a secret and sacrifices a dozen villagers to the creature every three years. |
| Borderlands | Several abandoned keeps stand within sight of the Phantasmal Forest. The Circle grants these holdings to members and allies who swear to restore them as bastions of light. |
| Faith Hold | From her castle, Elena readies knights for bold quests, makes her "Decrees of Faith," and employs harsh inquisitors in hidden torture chambers and reeducation cells. |
| Lake Amenta | Icy Lake Amenta is said to hide a golden realm beneath its waters. Only Elena remembers the city of "heretical" dwarf artisans she drowned in a flood here long ago. |
| Proll | Levity is forbidden in the lumbering community of Proll. People are wary of smiling and report those suspected of secretly being bards. Those who transgress are sent to the Faith Hold. |
| Ruins of Eckham | The peasants of Eckham rebelled against their harsh treatment. Elena claimed the people succumbed to demon worship and had her followers slay the locals and burn the town. |
| Ruins of Ludyard | Ludyard met a fate similar to Eckham. Freedom fighters hide out here and plan Elena's undoing, but they endlessly squabble over how best to rule after her downfall. |
| x | Ebonbane tempts virtuous souls to Shadowborn Manor, crushes their faith, and takes control of their bodies. The manor is still haunted by the spirit of Kateri Shadowborn. |
| Stone Circle | The Circle was founded here long ago. Amid rune-carved dolmens is a circular slab marked with the impression of thirteen distinct swords. Ebonbane sees nothing that happens here. |
| Tergeron Manor | Long ago, the wizard Morgoroth betrayed the Circle but was trapped in a mirror in Tergeron Manor. Within the manor lies a crystal coffin that holds the hero Aurora Shadowborn in stasis. |
| Touraine | The gleaming, white-walled city of Touraine is peaceful and safe. The people are wary of strangers and the evils they bring. A grand temple of Ezra serves as a meeting place for the Circle. |
| Wynderton | Wynderton is a farming community protected by a family of knights of the same name. To prove their piety, the family insists the villagers attend religious services three times a day. |



### Ebonbane

Darklord of Endless Vengeance

![image](book/RHW/155-15-003.ebonbane.webp)

> Questing knights? Champions of the realm? Look upon thy sterling souls. Tell me, heroes, by what fair deeds art thou known in this rotted world?

*Ebonbane* is an evil, sapient blade that seeks to annihilate the legacy of the Shadowlands' greatest hero and her allies. This includes all with the Shadowborn name and every member of the Circle.

Ebonbane is a magic weapon (see "x" later in this section), but within Shadowborn Manor, it becomes a creature that can move on its own (see the Ebonbane stat block). Beyond the manor, it doesn't use its stat block—it requires a wielder to work its evil in the world.

Many who attempt to attune to the weapon are slain outright by its evil. Those who do manage to wield Ebonbane must endure the Darklord's constant demands and risk becoming its pawn (see "Sentient Magic Items" in the Dungeon Master's Guide). If unattended outside Shadowborn Manor, Ebonbane eventually finds its way back there. No one can carry Ebonbane out of the Shadowlands. If someone tries, the sword vanishes and reappears in Shadowborn Manor.

Ebonbane has a flamboyant personality and a penchant for the dramatic and sadistic. It has no regard for life and delights in animating the corpses of foes, then destroying them in front of their allies. When it speaks, it uses language that mocks the elevated speech of knights.


##### Ebonbane

*S • construct • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 18 | 18 | 13 | 17 | 14 | 19 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Skills** 

**Senses** Truesight 120 ft.

**Languages** Common; telepathy 10 ft.

**Challenge** {"cr":"13","xpLair":11500}

**Traits**

**Darklord Restoration.** If Ebonbane dies, it revives with all its *Hit Points* in 1d10 weeks, teleporting somewhere in Shadowborn Manor. Until it revives, Ebonbane acts as a +3 Longsword when wielded by a creature.

**Legendary Resistance (3/Day, or 4/Day in Domain).** If Ebonbane fails a saving throw, it can choose to succeed instead.

**Magic Resistance.** Ebonbane has *Advantage* on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.

**Legendary Actions**

**Retaliate.** Ebonbane moves up to half its *Speed* and makes one Darkflame Slash attack.

**Runic Flare.** con 17, each creature of Ebonbane's choice in a 30-foot *Emanation* originating from Ebonbane. {@actSaveFail} The target has the *Blinded* condition and repeats the save at the end of each of its turns. The target succeeds automatically after 1 minute. {@actSaveSuccessOrFail} Ebonbane can't take this action again until the start of its next turn.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** Ebonbane makes three Darkflame Slash attacks. It can replace one of these attacks with a use of Possess *Dead* if available.

**Darkflame Slash.** m,r 9, reach 5 ft. or range 90 ft. {@h}9 (1d10 + 4) Slashing damage plus 10 (3d6) Necrotic damage.

**Possess Dead 5.** Ebonbane raises a Medium or Small Humanoid corpse within 5 feet of itself and possesses it. The corpse wields Ebonbane and is under its control. Ebonbane gains 50 *Temporary Hit Points*, and its statistics are the same, except its *Speed* increases to 30 feet, and it can speak through the corpse using any language the corpse knew in life. The possession lasts until Ebonbane drops to 0 *Hit Points* or Ebonbane ends the possession as a *Bonus Action*. Once the possession ends, Ebonbane can't possess the corpse again. The corpse crumbles to dust 24 hours after the possession ends.

**Worthy Wielder.** cha 17, one willing Humanoid within 5 feet. {@actSaveFail} 36 (8d8) Force damage. If this damage reduces the target to 0 *Hit Points*, Ebonbane devourers its soul. A creature whose soul has been devoured by Ebonbane can be restored to life only by a *Wish* spell. {@actSaveSuccess} The target attunes to Ebonbane and can wield the sword.

**Reactions**

**Parry.** {@actTrigger} Ebonbane is hit by a melee attack roll. {@actResponse} Ebonbane adds 5 to its AC against that attack, possibly causing it to miss.



#### Ebonbane's Tale

Kateri Shadowborn was a great hero who, alongside her order of valorous knights called the Circle, spent her life in service of good. Among her greatest deeds was leading an army against a nation whose king had been possessed by a fiend. She defeated the fiend, though doing so caused her magic sword to shatter.

After a life of great deeds, Kateri Shadowborn retired to live in peace with her family at Shadowborn Manor. But the hero had made many enemies. Thinking her vulnerable, wicked cultists recovered the pieces of Kateri's broken sword and conjured the lingering malice of the evils she had thwarted. These the cultists forged into a terrible weapon, Ebonbane—and they became its first victims.

Animated by hatred for Kateri and her allies, Ebonbane took control of its creators and became a curse on the world. For years it worked to destroy what Kateri had created, ruin what she loved, and slaughter those who aided her. Many times the evil sword's wielder was captured, but none ever suspected that the weapon itself was behind the grisly crimes.

Finally, in the hands of an unassuming monk, Ebonbane found its way to Shadowborn Manor, where grim news had isolated Kateri and worn her down. Aged but still a mighty knight, Kateri recognized Ebonbane's threat, and a great battle ensued. During the clash, Kateri kept Ebonbane's attention and ensured her family and friends escaped the manor. When only the hero and the wicked sword remained, Kateri summoned her remaining might into a blow to destroy Ebonbane. But the wicked sword proved too powerful. Kateri's blade shattered, and Ebonbane struck down the legendary knight. Exalting in its victory, the evil weapon possessed Kateri's body and pursued her fleeing family. But as it did so, it witnessed its quarry fading into the rising Mists.

When the Mists receded, Ebonbane found itself in a realm where the residents regarded the ancestors of Kateri Shadowborn and her fellow knights as heroes. Thrilled to continue its spree, Ebonbane sought to leave Shadowborn Manor, but it had no one to carry it beyond the grounds. Now, the evil blade seethes in frustration, waiting for a worthy bearer to carry it into the world so it might destroy all the good that came from Kateri's work.



#### Ebonbane as a Magic Item

Ebonbane's magic weapon form is described below.



#### Ebonbane

Weapon (Longsword), Artifact (Requires Attunement)

The Darklord of the Domain of Dread known as the Shadowlands is Ebonbane, a sapient sword. *Ebonbane* uses its monster stat block while in Shadowborn Manor.



#### Bound to the Shadowlands

When you enter a space outside of the Shadowlands, your Attunement immediately ends and Ebonbane teleports to somewhere in Shadowborn Manor.



#### Insatiable Rage

The sword demands destruction. If the sword hasn't slain a Celestial or a Humanoid for 3 days, you make a 17 Charisma saving throw at the next dawn. On a successful save, you take 8d8 Force damage. On a failed save, you are dominated by the sword, as if by the *Dominate Monster* spell, and the sword demands the blood of a Celestial or a Humanoid. The spell effect ends when the sword's demand is met.



#### Magic Weapon

You gain a +3 bonus to attack rolls and damage rolls made with this magic weapon. When you hit a Celestial or a Humanoid with it, that attack also deals 3d6 Necrotic damage.

While you hold this weapon, you have *Advantage* on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.



#### Sentience

Ebonbane is a sentient Chaotic Evil weapon with an Intelligence of 17, a Wisdom of 14, and a Charisma of 19. It has hearing and *Truesight* out to 120 feet. The weapon speaks Common and can communicate with its wielder telepathically. While you are attuned to it, Ebonbane also understands every language you know.



#### Personality

Ebonbane was created to kill the paladin Kateri Shadowborn, and it still possesses a burning hatred for goodly knights. Ebonbane revels in seeing good defeated and hope vanquished. The sword bonds with any wielder that assists in its goals but always views it wielder as a lackey.



#### Destroying Ebonbane

The only way to destroy Ebonbane is to forge a weapon from the x and reduce Ebonbane to 0 Hit Points with it (see the Ebonbane stat block).



#### Ebonbane's Domain

The Shadowlands is altered by Ebonbane's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders** While in its domain, Ebonbane can close or open the borders of the Shadowlands at will. While the borders are closed, whirling blades of magic fly through the Mists surrounding the Shadowlands. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must succeed on a 15 Dexterity saving throw or take 3d10 Force damage. A creature makes this save only once per turn.
- **Haunted Woods** The forest within 1 mile of Ebonbane's lair is wreathed in a powerful illusion. Whenever a creature other than Ebonbane or the sword's allies finishes a Short or Long Rest in that area, it must succeed on a 15 Intelligence saving throw, or it is lost in the forest, always finding itself at the location it started in until it finishes a Short or Long Rest.
- **Turning Weapons** While in its lair, Ebonbane can transform nonmagical *Greatswords* and *Longswords* within 1 mile of the lair into *Animated Flying Swords* by completing a 24-hour ritual.

If Ebonbane is destroyed, these effects end immediately.



#### Ebonbane's Lair

Ebonbane remains imprisoned in Shadowborn Manor, a fortified estate hidden in the Phantasmal Forest. The grounds are strewn with the bodies of those who sought the legendary blade and failed.



#### Shadowborn Manor

Though abandoned, Shadowborn Manor remains in decent repair. The estate is depicted on Map 2.29: Shadowborn Manor and has the following features:

- **Dungeon** The Circle understood that some evils needed to be contained. A secret stairway in the east wing leads to a dungeon that has remained hidden from Ebonbane.
- **Great Hall** This hall hosts the round table where members of the Circle once met. Ebonbane poses the bodies of knights here to possess as it pleases.
- **Lady's Chambers** Kateri Shadowborn's armored corpse lies in the largest bedroom on the second floor. It is Ebonbane's favorite body to reanimate, and if destroyed, it reappears in this chamber.



### Adventures in the Shadowlands

Adventures set in the Shadowlands feature individuals striving to prove their worth or superiority. Characters might be welcome to join the knights of the Circle, or perhaps they belong to families with heroic histories. Such ties could connect characters to the domain's history and future quests. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![The remains of failed quests and fallen knights lie near Shadowborn Manor in the Phantasmal Forest](book/RHW/156-15-004.phantasmal-forest.webp)



#### Horror in the Shadowlands

Adventures in the Shadowlands often include the following elements.



#### Faith-hold's Crusades

Elena Faith-hold rules Nidala, crushing its people under the weight of her intolerance and need to maintain her virtuous reputation. While she doesn't lead the Circle, she is its most respected member.

Elena leads forays of knights into the Mists on lengthy quests to defeat wicked foes in mysterious lands. An invitation to join one of Elena's crusades is a great honor and a death sentence. Whenever Elena returns from the Mists, she always does so alone, claiming to be the sole survivor of a great victory.

Elena Faith-hold isn't a Darklord, but should someone ever destroy Ebonbane, she might ascend to that position.



#### Quest of the Four Keys

One can destroy Ebonbane permanently using the sword of Kateri Shadowborn. However, the Dark Powers shattered her sword and scattered its pieces. These fragments are known as the Four Keys—emblems of Kateri's valor and faith. Each embodies a different virtue and one of the four elements.



#### The Keys' Locations

The Four Keys might appear anywhere in the Shadowlands or other domains. The ghost of Kateri Shadowborn or lore hidden amid tragic sites might point toward the keys.



#### Using the Keys

Should the characters collect the Four Keys, they can reforge them into a weapon that—if used to reduce *Ebonbane* to 0 Hit Points—negates its Darklord Restoration trait. It's up to you whether this ends the Darklord's threat or unleashes a greater evil bound within.



#### Shadowlands Campaign Arc

Campaigns in the Shadowlands often involve quests that reveal evils steeped in tragedies and abuses of power. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–4** The characters aid members of the Circle in defeating a dangerous *Basilisk* in Nidala. Impressed, the knights charge the characters with reclaiming a fort in the Borderlands from a wicked knight. The knight—a Circle member who died trying to recover Kateri Shadowborn's sword—is now a *Revenant*. Once the knight is defeated, the Circle gives the characters its fort as a Bastion (10 in the Dungeon Master's Guide).
- **Level 5–8** In their Bastion, the characters find a piece of a broken sword. The spirit of Kateri Shadowborn appears to the most virtuous character and asks for their help freeing her spirit and defeating Ebonbane. She shares the details in the "x" section. The characters begin a journey across the Shadowlands and beyond to recover the other three sword fragments.
- **Levels 9–11** Once the characters have the Four Keys, Kateri's spirit instructs them to travel to the Stone Circle in the Phantasmal Forest, where the sword can be magically reforged as a *Holy Avenger*. With this weapon, the characters journey to Shadowborn Manor and face *Ebonbane*.



#### The Shadowborn Sword

Adventure for Level 10 Characters

- **Situation** A knight seeks to prove herself by finding a hero's lost sword.
- **Hook** The human knight Lucia Lambert (Medium, Lawful Good *Questing Knight*) invites the characters to join her mission to recover the lost sword of the hero Kateri Shadowborn. In return, she'll reward them with 4,000 GP—or double that amount in additions to the characters' Bastions.



#### Encounters

The adventure starts at the edge of the Phantasmal Forest and consists of these encounters.



#### Phantasmal Forest

The journey to Shadowborn Manor is 18 miles, with the forest's density and perpetual *Darkness* limiting characters to a TravelPace. As Lucia's family members have belonged to the Circle since its founding, she can navigate the forest at a Normal pace, so the journey takes only 8 hours.



#### Fallen Knight

Outside the manor, a *Death Knight Aspirant* wearing the armor of a Circle knight bars the path and warns characters not to enter. A Good character who succeeds on a 16 Charisma (*Persuasion*) check can convince the corpse to let them pass; otherwise, it attacks those who try to enter.



#### Shadowborn Manor

Armored corpses lie about Shadowborn Manor (use map 2.29). If the characters disturb them or enter the great hall, five rise as *Strahd Skeletons* (see x).



#### Shadowborn's Ghost

The Lawful Good *Ghost* of Kateri Shadowborn haunts the manor. If the characters seem near defeat, she appears and can distract Ebonbane or lead them to the hidden dungeon.



#### Ebonbane

*Ebonbane* (see earlier in x) lies in the great hall. If with the characters, Lucia claims the sword and is stricken dead by Ebonbane, who animates her body. Otherwise, Ebonbane animates another corpse. The Darklord tries to convince the characters to take it from the manor so it can slay their foes. If they reject it, Ebonbane fights.



#### Conclusion

Should the characters escape Shadowborn Manor, each of them earns a bonus 3,100 XP. If they don't take Ebonbane, Kateri's ghost appears to them the following night and explains that Ebonbane's evil isn't ended. She goes explains the Darklord's history and how to destroy it (see "x"). The Circle rewards the characters in Lucia's stead if she is slain.



## Sithicus

Domain of the Soul's Shadow

- **Darklord:** x
- **Genre:** x
- **Hallmarks:** Cataclysmic fire, malicious shadows, tormented memories, twisted fantasy
- **Mist Talismans:** Black rose, burnt armor, scrap of black fabric, three thorns
- **Aligned Tarokka Card:** Paladin
- **Opposed Tarokka Card:** Innocent

Whatever Sithicus was or could have been, it will never be. The dramatic ruins of a fabulous elven realm cover a land realm forested by gigantic trees and burning with the flames of a forgotten magical disaster. Scattered communities appear among the dilapidation, the domain's predominantly elf population living like strangers amid structures to which they have no connection. At dusk, people withdraw, hiding from the domain's true residents: the shadows.

By night, the shadows of Sithicus reenact forgotten lives or mimic the deeds of questing knights, devoted lovers, and lurking monsters. Most of these shadows are harmless, if unnerving, and seem not to notice other beings. Some, however, resent the domain's other residents and torment the living.

Though few in the domain realize it, Sithicus has ties to the world of Krynn on the Material Plane. Ruins suggest the work of elves from that world, while the night sky blazes with the five-headed dragon constellation of the deity Takhisis. As on Krynn, the black moon Nuitari is visible only to evil beings. But the domain's clearest tie to Krynn is its Darklord, the accursed knight *Lord Soth*.



### Domain Features

Sithicus is known for the following features:

- **Bound to Krynn** Sithicus is a warped reflection of the lands of Krynn. This world and its people, such as *kender*, are described in Dragonlance: Shadow of the Dragon Queen.
- **Cataclysmic Fire** Accursed flames blaze amid prominent ruins and turn shadows into monsters drawn from Lord Soth's past.
- **Living Shadows** Shadows in Sithicus move on their own. Most are harmless, but some are deadly creatures such a *Shadows* or *Shadow Demons*.
- **Soth's Traitor** Lord Soth's undead soldiers hunt for the ghostly knight Caradoc, whom Soth blames for his imprisonment in Sithicus.



### Locations in Sithicus

Two significant features of Sithicus are detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the Sithicus Locations.



#### Endless Ruins

Sithicus lies blanketed in endless ruins. Ancient forests rise from them, rivers flow in their broken avenues, and whole mountain ranges are sculpted with crumbled towers. These structures suggest the work of a vast, magical elven nation, but all evidence of these people has been reduced to enigmatic scraps of art and lore. At the heights of crumbling towers or in empty crypts blaze violet, cataclysmic fire (see "x"). In rare cases, these phantasmal flames reveal glimpses of Lord Soth's past and details that the clever might use to win the Darklord's favor.



#### Great Chasm

The Great Chasm gapes in Sithicus like a wound. None can say how deep it goes, as light fails to pierce more than a few dozen feet into the ravine. Those who descend deeper vanish into the shadows and rarely return. Those who do tell of a malicious darkness beneath the domain, a cacophony of hateful voices, and shadows that hunger.

Hidden amid ruins spilling into the chasm is the home of Inza Kulchevich, a hateful witch who can speak to shadows and believes all virtue is a lie. Despite her cynicism, she might perform prophetic fortune-telling or share strange lore in return for her visitors' shadows.

**Sithicus Locations**

| Location | Description |
|---|---|
| Giant's Cloak | Throughout the Giant's Cloak forest are petrified trees carved with strange runes and weeping tar-like sap. Stone giant hermits tend these groves and set deadly traps against trespassers. |
| Har-Thelen | Har-Thelen is largely abandoned. Its gates stand open, and only a few hundred people reside at its center. By night, stray shadows work and live among the abandoned structures. |
| Hroth | The decrepit town of Hroth is built amid giant swamp trees, many of which lean at precarious angles. The bogs nearby are said to be magic and can return to life those buried within. |
| Iron Warden Inn | The Iron Warden Inn is closed by day, but at night, those with enough wealth to buy entry gamble at games of cards and death's-head dice. Sometimes the dead come to play. |
| Kendralind | A hidden village of faded tree houses, huts, and burrows, Kendralind is home to a few dozen kender vampires. The residents are equally delighted by games, whimsical tales, and bloodshed. |
| Lake of Glass | The Lake of Glass moves like water but is as solid as glass. At night, the lake reflects the hidden moon, Nuitari, and magic cast within its reflected light is empowered but cursed. |
| Mal-Erek | Forgotten scholars built Mal-Erek amid giant trees. Now only squatters and obsessed scholars reside here, with few noticing the decay of the vaults and archives around them. |
| Merchant's Slash | The Merchant's Slash trail is littered with the wreckage of merchant and traveler caravans. Some are still occupied by eccentric traders selling eerie wares from strange lands. |
| x | The towering fortress of Lord Soth is strangled by black thorns and blazes with cataclysmic flame. Within, undead knights and spectral elves reenact and recite Soth's great failures. |
| Sorrow | A hidden prison for the living guarded by the dead, Sorrow accepts mysterious transfers from beyond the Mists. Many thought dead in other domains are imprisoned here. |
| Veldrava | A dismal work camp stands at the entrance to a maze of unfathomably deep salt mines. Caustic minerals burn explorers who seek the source of whispers from the depths. |



### Lord Soth

Darklord Cursed by Memories

![image](book/RHW/163-16-003.lord-soth-of-sithicus.webp)

> Explain why you have interrupted my reverie, or I will turn your waking hours into nightmares.

Lord Loren Soth seethes within a realm that mocks and frustrates him. Having known the rigid standards of knighthood and warfare, Soth finds Sithicus empty and chaotic, his people apathetic and undisciplined. The elven beauty that once captivated him lies ruined, the land burns with the flames of Krynn's Cataclysm, and the realm's shadows remind Soth of his past failures. Worse, no worthy foes exist to challenge him. So Soth broods on his throne in Nedragaard Keep, haunted by banshees that sing the tale of his disgrace and by rotted, undead copies of the knights who once served him.

Lord Soth cares nothing for his domain. But should noteworthy threats or remarkable individuals appear, he seeks to crush or enlist them. The only exception is the spirit of his treacherous former ally, Caradoc. Soth's undead servants and his werebadger seneschal, Azrael Dax, scour the land for the elusive ghost.

Soth shares his imprisonment in Sithicus with all in the domain by keeping its borders perpetually closed. Only those who rouse him to activity or invade Nedragaard Keep might convince him to let them escape. This risks provoking the mighty death knight's wrath, but Soth still thinks of himself as a true knight—he might assist those who present themselves as honorable warriors or show knowledge of his home (see "x").


##### Lord Soth of Sithicus

*M • undead • L E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 22 | 11 | 20 | 12 | 16 | 20 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** Common Infernal

**Challenge** {"cr":"19","xpLair":25000}

**Traits**

**Darklord Restoration.** If Lord Soth dies, he revives with all his *Hit Points* in 1d10 weeks somewhere in Sithicus.

**Legendary Resistance (3/Day, or 4/Day in Domain).** If Lord Soth fails a saving throw, he can choose to succeed instead.

**Magic Resistance.** Lord Soth has *Advantage* on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.

**Marshal Undead.** Undead creatures of Lord Soth's choice (excluding himself) in a 60-foot *Emanation* originating from him have *Advantage* on attack rolls and saving throws. Lord Soth can't use this trait if he has the *Incapacitated* condition.

**Legendary Actions**

**Punish.** Lord Soth moves up to half his *Speed*, and he makes one Forsaken Brand attack.

**Soth's Command.** Lord Soth casts *Command* (level 3 version), using the same spellcasting ability as Commanding Magic. Lord Soth can't take this action again until the start of his next turn.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** Lord Soth makes three Forsaken Brand attacks.

**Forsaken Brand.** m 12, reach 5 ft. {@h}10 (1d8 + 6) Slashing damage plus 13 (3d8) Necrotic damage.

**Cataclysmic Fire 5.** dex 19, each creature in a 20-foot-radius *Sphere* centered on a point Lord Soth can see within 120 feet. {@actSaveFail} 24 (7d6) Fire damage plus 24 (7d6) Necrotic damage. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage.

**Face of Death (1/Day).** cha 19, each creature in a 60-foot *Emanation* originating from Lord Soth. {@actSaveFail} 22 (4d10) Psychic damage, and the creature has the *Frightened* condition. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage only. {@actSaveSuccessOrFail} If this damage reduces the target to 0 *Hit Points*, the target dies.

**Villain of Two Worlds**

Lord Soth features in adventures in both the Dragonlance and Ravenloft campaign settings. If you want to give Soth a unique relationship to the Domains of Dread, consider these possibilities:

- The nature of Soth's curse creates aspects of the death knight in both Krynn and Sithicus. When Soth broods in his fortress in Krynn, he remains active in Sithicus. When the evil god, Takhisis, calls for his service on Krynn, Soth enters a magical torpor in his fortress in Sithicus.
- Soth traveled from Krynn to Sithicus and is destined to return. If he leaves Sithicus, the domain might be destroyed, or a villain like Inza Kulchevich might take over.
- Soth was trapped in Sithicus, escaped, and was trapped again, perpetuating a cycle of despair.

Soth's story and where characters encounter him are for you to detail in your adventures.



#### Lord Soth's Tale

Lord Soth was given a quest to save the people of his world, Krynn, from the wrath of the gods. Possessed by baseless paranoia and possessiveness of his elf wife, Soth forsook that quest, and the world was devastated in a great Cataclysm. In punishment, Soth was resurrected as a death knight and, for centuries, brooded on his disgrace in the charred ruins of his fortress, Dargaard Keep.

When the evil god Takhisis whispered to Soth, promising to restore his glory and avenge him against the heroic knights who banished him long ago, Soth answered and served Takhisis. During this time, he called on his undead servants, including the ghost of the knight Caradoc. Seeking to forge a new knighthood of loyal dead, Soth became obsessed with Dragon Highlord Kitiara Uth Matar and charged Caradoc with claiming her soul. When Kitiara died in battle, Caradoc refused to capture her spirit unless Soth bargained with Takhisis to restore Caradoc to life. Enraged, Soth tried to destroy Caradoc as the Mists rose around them.

When the Mists faded, Soth found himself in the domain of 2. For a time, he found an ally in *Count Strahd von Zarovich*, but the two villains couldn't abide one another for long. Soth eventually pursued rumors of his treacherous servant, Caradoc, into the Mists. When the Mists parted again, the domain of Sithicus spread before him.



#### Lord Soth's Domain

Sithicus is altered by Lord Soth's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders** While in his domain, Lord Soth can close or open the borders to Sithicus. While the borders are closed, purple flames fill the Mists surrounding Sithicus. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there takes 5 (1d10) Fire damage plus 5 (1d10) Necrotic damage.
- **Fearless Soldiers** Undead allies of Lord Soth have Immunity to the *Frightened* condition.
- **Guilt of Sithicus** Few sleep soundly in Sithicus. Whenever a creature other than Lord Soth and his allies finishes a Long Rest in the domain, the creature must succeed on a 10 Constitution saving throw or gain 1 *Exhaustion* level.

If Lord Soth dies, these effects end immediately.



#### Lord Soth's Lair

![Nedragaard Keep](book/RHW/164-16-004.nedagaard-keep.webp)

Lord Soth rules from Nedragaard Keep, a twisted, copy of his accursed fortress on Krynn, Dargaard Keep. Nedragaard Keep grows and withers over time like a living thing. Undead soldiers patrolling the keep regularly forget their duties or collapse into lifelessness. The disorder within the rigid death knight's fortress endlessly frustrates Lord Soth.



#### Nedragaard Keep

Nedragaard Keep is a towerlike fortress of crumbling, flame-scarred stone. Prominent locations in the keep are depicted on Map 2.31: Nedragaard Keep and have the following features:

- **Gatehouse** Undead soldiers guard the gates to Nedragaard Keep, demanding to know trespassers' identities. Those who identify themselves with the proper passphrase, such as "a seeker of the rose" or "a servant of Nightlund's lord," are admitted. Stairs beyond the gate climb several floors to the top of the keep's walls.
- **Garden** Gardens on the keep's second floor are overgrown with thorny plants—use the rules for razorvine from the Dungeon Master's Guide. From here spread massive vines that bloom with black roses and strangle the entire castle.
- **Throne Room** High in the keep is Soth's throne room. Here Lord Soth spends much of his time dwelling on failures and twisted fantasies. Thirteen *Banshees* haunt the keep, and at any time, at least three linger here, singing of Soth's disgrace.



### Adventures in Sithicus

Adventures set in Sithicus feature mysterious shadows, grim ruins, and strange foes from the warped memories of Lord Soth. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.



#### Horror in Sithicus

Adventures in Sithicus often include the following elements.



#### Cataclysmic Flames

Illusory violet flames burn across Sithicus—fires from the Cataclysm that devastated Krynn. Powerful shadows guard prominent, bonfire-like pillars of these flames. These shadows might use the stat blocks of any monster, but they resemble dragons, knights, and figures from Soth's past.

Whenever someone defeats one of these guardians, the flame it protected reveals an illusory scene from the Darklord's past before vanishing. Any character who witnesses such a scene learns something of Soth's history, the world he comes from, or the knighthood he once belonged to. One of the viewers then gains the Charm of the Black Rose (see "Supernatural Gifts" in the Dungeon Master's Guide for additional details).



#### Influencing Lord Soth

Lord Soth is typically *Hostile* to strangers, but characters can adjust his attitude to *Indifferent* by succeeding on a 20 Charisma (*Deception* or *Persuasion*) check. Soth might employ characters he deems worthy on quests, such as the hunt for the ghost Caradoc. Making a second successful 20 Charisma (*Deception* or *Persuasion*) check while offering Soth something he covets can improve Soth's attitude to *Friendly* for a short time, during which he might let others leave his domain.



#### Living Shadows

Shadows in Sithicus often act with a life of their own. Roll on or choose a result from the Shadows of Sithicus table to inspire these shapes' behavior.

**Shadows of Sithicus**

| 1d6 | The Shadows Behave As... |
|---|---|
| 1 | An elf desperately offering a swaddled bundle. |
| 2 | Glimpses of skeletal warriors or horses. |
| 3 | Knights in battle or in the midst of a siege. |
| 4 | Peasants being consumed by shadowy flames. |
| 5 | Marching soldiers with dragon-like features. |
| 6 | Solemn elf priests being ambushed by ogres. |



#### Sithicus Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Sithicus often involve trying to gain Lord Soth's favor and win escape from the domain. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–4** Azrael Dax, Lord Soth's werebadger seneschal, brusquely recruits the characters to hunt down deadly shadows. These shadows take the form of and behave as noble knights.
- **Level 5–9** Impressed by the characters, Azrael sends them to Inza Kulchevich to ask the witch to use her powers to find Lord Soth's elusive former servant, Caradoc. Inza can do this, but first she requires the characters to collect the cataclysmic flame from three ruins across the domain in a magical iron pendant. Each flame is guarded by a shadow creature that resembles some foe from Soth's twisted memories—like a lance-wielding *Warrior Commander* or a pompous *Archpriest*.
- **Levels 10–14** Inza uses the pendant to reveal that Caradoc's soul is trapped in a black sapphire that Azrael already possesses. The characters must recover the gem. They might then infiltrate Nedragaard Keep to offer it to *Lord Soth*. Soth is fickle though, and this approach might end in a confrontation with the death knight.



#### Shadow of the Black Rose

Adventure for Level 14 Characters

- **Situation** The characters seek to escape Sithicus or the Domains of Dread.
- **Hook** Inza Kulchevich (Medium, Neutral Evil *Death Cultist*) offers to tell the characters how to escape Sithicus if they recover a magical gem from Lord Soth's seneschal, Azrael Dax.



#### Encounters

The adventure consists of these encounters.



#### Inza's Quest

The witch Inza loathes Lord Soth. She knows he has tasked Azrael with recovering a magical gem that holds the spirit of the Darklord's treacherous former ally, the knight Caradoc. Inza gives the characters an iron pendant bearing an image of a rose that's missing its central gem. She asks them to follow Azrael to a ruin in the Misttop Mountains, where he hunts the missing gem, and recover it before him.



#### Inza's Secret

Inza doesn't share that she seeks to release Caradoc to provoke Soth into a conflict with the characters.



#### Searching the Ruins

The ruins where Azrael hunts for the gem appear on map 2.31. For every 10 minutes the characters are exploring, roll 1d6 on the table below for an encounter. For each previous encounter rolled on this table, add 1 to the result.

**Encounters in the Ruins**

| 1d6 + #$prompt_number:title=Enter a Modifier$# | Encounter |
|---|---|
| 1–2 | *Death Knight Aspirant* and two *Banshees* |
| 3–4 | Two *Relentless Nightmares* |
| 5 | A *Gulthias Blight* covered in black roses |
| 6 | Kender Nosferatu (see below) |
| 7 | Shadow Highlord (see below) |
| 8+ | Azrael Dax (see below) |



#### Kender Nosferatu

A morbidly whimsical pair of *Vampire Nosferatu* pesters the characters, hoping to be entertained. If the characters don't keep them amused, the nosferatu attack. Because these monsters were kender in life—mischievous folk from the world of Krynn—they are Small.



#### Shadow Highlord

A dragon rider made of shadows guards a pillar of illusory violet flame. It reflects one of Lord Soth's warped memories and uses the stat blocks of a *Dullahan* (see x) riding a *Young Blue Dragon*, followed by a withered *Death's Head*. The monsters are *Hostile*. If they're defeated, the nearby pillar of flames shows a scene of Lord Soth being knighted and grants a character the benefits noted in "x." If you roll this encounter a second time, treat it as a meeting with Azrael Dax.



#### Azrael Dax

Azrael Dax is Lord Soth's dwarf seneschal and a murderous werebadger (use the *Werebear* stat block). Azrael and the six *Strahd Skeletons* (see x) attending him are Hostile. If reduced to 50 Hit Points or fewer, Azrael bargains for his life and offers the characters the black sapphire they're looking for, which he's been hiding from Soth for moons. After this, don't roll for more encounters in the ruins.



#### Repairing the Pendant

Place the black gem in Inza's iron amulet releases Caradoc (Neutral Evil *Ghost*). The arrogant creature is *Indifferent* to the characters. If they don't free Caradoc, Inza does when the group returns the gem and pendant to her.



#### Soth Appears

Three rounds after Caradoc is freed, *Lord Soth of Sithicus* (see earlier in x) appears from the shadows. Soth fights Caradoc and mistakes the characters for the ghost's allies. A character might convince him otherwise—see "x."



#### Escape

Characters who flee or defeat Lord Soth gain an additional 6,200 XP. Those who change the Darklord's attitude to *Friendly* or help him defeat Caradoc can convince him to let them leave Sithicus. Defeating Soth also causes the domain's borders to open. If the characters confront Inza about her method for leaving Sithicus, she cryptically explains that the only route to do so leads through Soth, encouraging them to seek the Darklord's aid or confront the death knight again.



## Tepest

Domain of Nature's Cruel Secrets

- **Darklord:** x
- **Adventure Genre:** x
- **Hallmarks:** Fey bargains, rural cults, secret sacrifices, sinister festivals
- **Mist Talismans:** Bloodstained farm implement, dried crown of white camellias, straw doll
- **Aligned Tarokka Card:** Druid
- **Opposed Tarokka Card:** Executioner

All is well in Tepest. Fields shimmer with bountiful harvests, and horned village children recite sing-song rhymes. But those who linger among this land's pastures and colorful cottages can't escape the feeling of being watched or the impression that strange forms move amid the fields. Locals dismiss such worries as the work of fey tricksters, but their smiles fail to mask the desperation in their eyes.

Brutality wears a welcoming face in Tepest, a truth embodied by the ancient hag Lorinda, who betrayed her coven in pursuit of adoration. Taking the guise of a deity called Mother, *Lorinda* adopted the village of Viktal, protecting its people from nature's whims so they can worship her even as they sacrifice themselves to feed her monstrous offspring. In the wilderness beyond, resentful fey watch and plot, offering cruel bargains to those who stray beyond Mother's sight. The people of Viktal do what they must to survive, using tradition to cloak their fear and complicity in a cycle of murder. Strangers become symbols of hope for Viktal's citizens—welcome alternatives to slaughtering their families in Mother's name.



### Domain Features

Tepest is known for the following features:

- **Children of the Fey** Few children are born in Viktal. Would-be parents must bargain with Mother or the fey to bring them a child.
- **Fey Threats** Caves dot the land, connecting to depths where dangerous fey dwell. The people of Viktal fear them and blame them for every ill.
- **The Last Village** Viktal is the only community in Tepest. The others displeased Mother and suffered terrible fates.
- **Mother** Viktal's residents devoutly follow the optimistic faith of the nature deity called Mother.
- **Mother's Minders** Mother's most zealous faithful are called Mother's Minders. These devotees sacrifice their left eyes to Mother to show their faith.
- **The Tithe** Viktal's festivals include a fertility celebration called the Tithe that occurs once a season.



### Locations in Tepest

The valley of Tepest is rocky, ill-suited to farming, and plagued by dangerous fey. Nevertheless, those who worship Mother are protected from the worst of the land's dangers. Mother's Sight and Viktal are detailed below, and other notable locations are summarized on the Tepest Locations.



#### Mother's Sight

A mile outside Viktal, in a field apart from the surrounding farms, stands Mother's Sight: an array of rune-etched standing stones. These stones rise as tall as thirty feet, and several have pieces that defy gravity. Within the central and largest stone floats a disk reminiscent of a great eye.

Here the people come to worship, celebrate, and sacrifice. Colorful crafts adorn long tables, where the villagers play games and feast in celebration of Mother's bounty. Meals here are tasty, and guests are encouraged to eat and drink beyond their fill.

During rituals here, Viktal's community leaders give thanks to Mother before a dramatic fire surrounded by an eight-foot scaffold. (See "x" adventure for additional details.)



#### Viktal

Mother ensures peace in Viktal. The village consists of a few dozen cottages, a market square, and an inn on the banks of Lake Kronov. Wicker scarecrows guard the rich fields blessed by Mother, and friendly people go about their daily lives. Cheery villagers welcome visitors, show them hospitality, and demonstrate interest in their stories.

**Tepest Locations**

| Location | Description |
|---|---|
| Arkenheights | Mysterious valleys hide amid the forested Arkenheights mountains. Each is home to territorial fey who know the strange histories and mystical properties that linger in each. |
| Blackroot | A gigantic evil *Treant* called Blackroot roots amid the stone circles of an ancient order of druids. Blackroot hoards the druids' magic and protects its glade with its deadly saplings. |
| Briggdarrow | This ruined village of Briggdarrow is overgrown by a toxic, vision-inducing fungus. Eerie fungal beings emerge from the ruins by night to spread the infestation beyond the village. |
| Cas Island | A ruined fortress covers most of Cas Island. Within it lies a mysterious magical relic, but the waters around the island are guarded by a notorious, crocodilian lake monster, the Avanc. |
| The Cauldron | A fey witch drowned in this pool long ago. Now, any corpse bathed in its magical waters returns to life—but the spirit inhabiting the body never matches the original owner's. |
| Goblinwood | People-eating goblins lurk in the Goblinwood. They attack trespassers, but a curse affecting the goblins prevents them from seeing anyone wearing a cap of a certain color. |
| Kellee | The walled village of Kellee once worshipped Mother, but something went wrong. Now, Lorinda's forsaken followers haunt the place, and neither she nor her current worshippers dare approach. |
| The Lost Court | By day, this idyllic valley is serene and filled with friendly animals. At night, the ground turns to mud and brambles, from which rise the transformed victims of fey curses. |
| Mount Arak | Beneath Mount Arak lies a hidden realm of the fey. The goodly Queen Maeve and wicked Prince Loht jointly rule their people. The fey resent the surface folk for ancient slights. |
| Nobody's Inn | Fey creatures avoid this sturdy, welcoming Nobody's Inn. Few travel so far from Viktal, but those who do are welcomed by Bryonna, the inn's gregarious but unnerving skeleton proprietor. |
| Seer's Glass | The mountain lake called Seer's Glass has prophetic powers. Those who gaze on their reflection in it see their past by day and their future by night. |



### Mother Lorinda

Darklord Who Demands Adoration

![image](book/RHW/173-17-003.mother-lorinda.webp)

> What precocious moppets you are! Little ones who show Mother love get rewarded, but bad children get punished. Which sorts of tots are you?

Mother Lorinda desires a family over all else, not realizing she's destroyed every family she's ever had. A creator of monstrosities, this ancient green hag obsesses over unnatural maternalistic pursuits.

Over generations, Tepest's villagers have come to view Lorinda not as a powerful witch, but as a god of the land and fertility called Mother. Lorinda doesn't dissuade her fragile mortal followers from their baseless cult practices. The villagers provide willing sacrifices for the hag's flawed magical attempts to create life, and their adoration gradually soothes the violent, magical outbursts that follow her failures.

Lorinda's walking tower of bones, the Gurgyl, ranges across Tepest. Those who seek her here find a distracted but deceptively cunning hag clinging to grotesque dolls of her family. She laments the loss of her sisters, Laveeda and Leticia, never acknowledging that they remain alive as her prisoners. She often speaks of her daughter, Laoirse (pronounced "LUR-shuh")—the name she uses over and over again for each of her monstrous creations.

When Lorinda visits Viktal, she appears in her illusory guise as Mother, an ancient, powerful woman wearing a mothlike cloak and bearing a branch with burning limbs. She calls on the people to prove their love for her through sacrifice, whether of food and crafts, their left eyes, or their lives. Sometimes her arrival is sudden and terrifying, such as when she magically appears to crawl from one of her followers' empty eye sockets.

Lorinda seeks new ways to create a permanent family. This might involve great sacrifices, stolen fey magic, strange adoptions, or all manner of supernatural bargains.


##### Mother Lorinda

*M • fey • N E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 18 | 13 | 16 | 13 | 17 | 15 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 60 ft.
