**Languages** Common Elvish Sylvan

**Challenge** {"cr":"8","xpLair":5000}

**Traits**

**Amphibious.** Lorinda can breathe air and water.

**Darklord Restoration.** If Lorinda dies, she revives with all her *Hit Points* in 1d10 weeks somewhere in Tepest.

**Legendary Resistance (3/Day, or 4/Day in Domain).** If Lorinda fails a saving throw, she can choose to succeed instead.

**Mimicry.** Lorinda can mimic noises and animal sounds. A creature that hears the mimicry can tell it is an imitation only with a successful 15 Wisdom (*Insight*) check.

**Legendary Actions**

**Brand.** Lorinda teleports to an unoccupied space she can see within 30 feet and can make one Mother's Brand attack.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** Lorinda makes two Mother's Brand attacks.

**Mother's Brand.** m 7, reach 5 ft. {@h}8 (1d8 + 4) Bludgeoning damage plus 5 (1d10) Fire damage.

**Bonus Actions**

**Mother's Visage (1/Day).** Lorinda shape-shifts into Mother, a deity revered by the people of Tepest, for 8 hours. Her game statistics are the same in each form. Any equipment she is wearing or carrying isn't transformed. While in the form of Mother, Lorinda can use Spellcasting to cast *Charm Person* as a *Bonus Action*. Lorinda reverts to her true form if she drops to 50 *Hit Points* or fewer. When Lorinda reverts to her true form, each creature in a 30-foot *Emanation* originating from Lorinda is subjected to the following effect. wis 14 (the target succeeds automatically if it is a Construct or an Undead). {@actSaveFail} The target has the *Frightened* condition for 1 minute. While *Frightened*, the target has *Disadvantage* on saving throws.



#### Mother Lorinda's Tale

The sisters Lorinda, Laveeda, and Leticia Mindefisk lived desperate lives at the wooded edge of a terrible land. Their brutish family claimed the girls were unnatural fey in disguise and forced them to toil constantly. After years of harsh treatment from their cruel father and brothers, the hopeless sisters snapped and killed an abusive traveler during a chance encounter. They butchered the body and served the remains to their unwitting family. Thus began a cycle of murder and cannibalism that persisted for years.

The Mindefisk sisters' crimes were finally revealed when they all fell in love with a charming stranger. They squabbled, and unwilling to relent or share, they murdered the stranger in full view of their horrified family. With nothing left to lose, the sisters killed the rest of their family as the Mists rose around them.

The horror of the Mindefisk sisters only grew in the Domains of Dread. Finding themselves in Tepest, the sisters discovered their new nature as hags. Over generations, mortals and fey alike came to know them as fickle miracle workers. Despairing families came to them often, willing to trade much for *hexblood* children born from the hags' magic.

Eventually, Lorinda grew fascinated by others' pursuit of family. She entreated her sisters to help her create a child, but Laveeda and Leticia refused, loathing the idea of any one of them having greater happiness than the others.

Defying her sisters, Lorinda assembled a monstrosity of animal parts and foul magic in secret. With her new daughter's help, the hag trapped her sisters inside their magic cauldron and stole their powers. Yet Lorinda's joy with her creation was short—the monster's magic quickly waned, and it rotted away. Ever since, Lorinda has sought to create a family of her own, producing countless monstrosities in experiments and approaching the villagers of Viktal in her guise as Mother. Over generations, this has given rise to the cult of the Mother in Viktal, but it has brought Lorinda no closer to attaining the lasting family connection she covets.



#### Mother Lorinda's Domain

Tepest is altered by Lorinda's presence, creating the following effects:

- **Closing the Borders** While in her domain, Mother Lorinda can close or open the borders to Tepest at will. While the borders are closed, a violent storm fills the Mists surrounding Tepest. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there must succeed on a 15 Strength saving throw or take 2d8 Lightning damage and be pushed up to 30 feet straight toward Tepest. A creature makes this save only once per turn.
- **Mother's Watchers** Creatures that have sacrificed an eye to Mother can take a *Magic* action and pray to her. When they do so, Lorinda can perceive through the creature's senses as well as her own until the end of the creature's next turn. When perceiving through a creature's senses, Lorinda benefits from any special senses it has.
- **Sun and Storms** While in Tepest, Lorinda can cast *Control Weather*, requiring no Material components and using the same spellcasting ability as Spellcasting. When casting the spell this way, Lorinda can control the weather within 5 miles of herself, regardless of whether she is inside or outside.

If Lorinda dies, these effects end immediately.



#### Mother Lorinda's Lair

Ranging across the domain is Mother Lorinda's home, the Gurgyl. This towerlike structure of thorns, wicker, and giants' bones walks on three skeletal dragon legs.



#### The Gurgyl

The villagers of Viktal know the Gurgyl serves their god in some way, but sighting it portends bad luck. The site has the following features:

- **Kitchen-Laboratory** The Darklord concocts foul creation magic in this central chamber.
- **Nursery-Oubliette** This room is home to whichever monster Lorinda calls her daughter, Laoirse.
- **Old Cauldron** Lorinda's hag sisters languish in this plugged, oversize pot.



### Adventures in Tepest

Adventures set in Tepest feature rural cults, deceptive fey, and dread of nature's mysteries. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Celebrants parade from Viktal to Mother's Sight to honor their god on the day of the Tithe](book/RHW/174-17-004.parade-to-mothers-sight.webp)



#### Horror in Tepest

Adventures in Tepest often include the following elements.



#### Strangeness in Viktal

The locals seem welcoming and vigorous in their worship of the nature deity, Mother. The village leader, Wyan, guides them in their faith, assisted by elders called Mother's Minders—all of whom are missing their left eye.

Residents invite visitors to stay at the village's only inn, the Fisher's Rest, free of charge for as long as they please. They encourage new arrivals to linger and participate in their upcoming festival, called the Tithe (detailed later in x).



#### Mother's Children

Multiple times a year, Lorinda goes through a cycle of trying to magically create a new child. She calls this monstrous being Laoirse and dotes on it for a time. She believes that sacrifices to Laoirse during the Tithe can extend her child's life, but inevitably, the monster's magic fades, and it becomes mud and bones once more. For weeks afterward, Lorinda remains inconsolable, and violent storms and strange disasters plague Tepest.

Lorinda's children take varied forms. To create such a monster, choose a stat block appropriate to challenge your characters, then consider how that creature might appear if it were made from different parts. For example, a *Minotaur of Baphomet* or *Werewolf* might be a bipedal mixture of ram, stag, and wolf parts, while a *Shambling Mound* might be a person made of wicker. These descriptions should seem outlandish but reflective of the creature's traits and actions. And no matter how bizarre her children are, Lorinda loves them all the same.



#### Tepest Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Tepest often involve Viktal's cult and the dangerous spirits of the wilds. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–2** Characters find themselves welcomed in Viktal and encouraged to take part in the Tithe (see the adventure below). At the rite's conclusion, the villagers try to sacrifice one or more characters to one of Mother's children. The characters defeat the monster, earning the enmity of both the villagers and Mother Lorinda.
- **Level 3–5** Fey creatures or druids who have been victims of Lorinda aid the characters; they reveal that she is no god, but a powerful hag who wanders the land in a walking tower called the Gurgyl. They send the group on a quest to learn from a mystical site or elder forest spirit how to infiltrate the hag's lair.
- **Levels 6–8** After learning how to infiltrate the Gurgyl, the characters locate and break into Lorinda's lair, finding some of the hag's bizarre creations and her diminished, imprisoned sisters. When they emerge from the mobile fortress, they find themselves near Viktal, where *Lorinda* confronts them, backed by her fanatical followers.
- **Levels 9+** If the group defeats Lorinda, the land spirals into chaos as fey from Mount Arak run wild. The characters might become involved in a power struggle between the good and evil fey of Arak. Lorinda's return might drive the fey back—but the Darklord will help only if someone becomes her new child.



#### The Tithe

Adventure for Level 2 Characters

- **Situation** The characters participate in a religious celebration, at the end of which they are poised to become sacrifices.
- **Hook** The human leader of Viktal, Wyan (Medium, Neutral Evil *Priest*) invites the characters to participate in the Tithe, a rite honoring their god, Mother.



#### Encounters

This adventure begins the day of the Tithe, after *Friendly* villagers from Viktal (*Commoners*) lead the characters to Mother's Sight. It uses map 2.33 and consists of these encounters.



#### Tithe Competitions

Wyan directs the assemblage in a prayer to Mother, and the day of games begins. Characters each can play three games, participating in each selected game once. During each game, a character makes the ability check listed on the table below three times. Those who succeed on the check two or more times win the game; if they fail, a villager wins.

| Tithe Game | Check |
|---|---|
| Crooked Joust. Participants use stilts strapped to their arms and legs to topple one another. | Strength (*Athletics*) |
| Powrie Chase. Pursuers play tag in while wearing tattered red cloaks. | Dexterity (*Stealth*) |
| Lost Siblings. Blindfolded participants identify other players by touching their hair. | Intelligence (*Investigation*) |
| Gossamer Glutton. Whoever eats the most live moths wins. | Constitution |
| Never Naughty. Participants flatter elderly villagers, who decide who wins and who gets paddled. | Charisma (*Persuasion*) |

Characters who don't play a game might socialize and see some benign oddity extrapolated from the details presented earlier in this section.



#### Competition Winners

The day's games draw to a close at dusk. Wyan names a character who won two or more games as Mother's Favorite and crowns them with a garland of white camellias. If no character won this many games, a human villager named Lorelei (Medium *Commoner*) wins the crown and invites them to sit with her at the head table during the feast.



#### Feast

Wyan begins the feast with another prayer as the Mother's Minders light a grand bonfire within a tall scaffold. During the feast, villagers encourage the characters eat and drink to excess. A character who does so must succeed on a 10 Constitution saving throw or gain the *Poisoned* condition for the next 6 hours.



#### The Sacrifice

At midnight, standing before the scaffold (see Map 2.33: Mother's Sight), Wyan announces, "Now we prove our undying love for Mother and beg her for another season of bounty. Bring forth our sacrifice!" Mother's Favorite receives a bowl of food and tiny crafts and is instructed to take it to the bonfire.

If Lorelei is Mother's Favorite, she obeys and approaches the bonfire. If a character is Mother's Favorite, they choose whether to approach. Regardless, 2 rounds later, a biped with wolflike features and stag's horns (use the *Minotaur of Baphomet* stat block) emerges from the field nearest Mother's Favorite. This is one of Lorinda's monstrous children. It fights Mother's Favorite (and anyone else who damages it) to the death. During combat, the villagers raise their voices in a hymn but stay out of the conflict. Lorelei smiles and doesn't defend herself if attacked.



#### Conclusion

If the monster dies, Wyan and the villagers are horrified that the Tithe went wrong. They turn *Hostile*, blaming the characters and demanding they leave. Mother Lorinda learns of this and seeks revenge.

If the monster wasn't killed, the villagers remain *Friendly*, but their true nature becomes clear. Mother Lorinda also takes an interest in the characters, potentially seeking to adopt them as her new children.

Regardless of how the Tithe concludes, the characters gain 200 XP.



## Valachan

Domain of the Hunter

- **Darklord:** x
- **Genres:** x and x
- **Hallmarks:** Deadly predators, death traps, hostile wilderness, survival games
- **Mist Talismans:** Displacer beast skin, poisonous flower blossom, rusty foot trap
- **Aligned Tarokka Card:** Shepherd
- **Opposed Tarokka Card:** Darklord

In the wild domain of Valachan, only the deadliest predators survive. Bestial hunters, carnivorous plants, and ravenous monsters stalk the dense rainforests, but the land's greatest threat is its Darklord: the devious, undying hunter *Chakuna*.

Chakuna stalks the jungle, testing herself against the domain's deadliest beasts. Yet little delights her more than discovering strangers to her realm—visitors who soon realize they've become the Darklord's newest quarry. Chakuna forces her victims to participate in the Trial of Hearts, a race through the wilderness to remote sanctuaries. Participants face deadly traps and all the dangers of the wilds, including Chakuna herself. Those who reach the goal at the end of the trial are permitted to leave Valachan. Those who don't reach it die, either due to the deadly wilderness or at the hands of Chakuna herself.



### Domain Features

Valachan is known for the following features:

- **Displacer Beast Packs** Packs of *Displacer Beasts* roam the jungle, led by Yana, a preternaturally large and cunning displacer beast that serves Chakuna.
- **Natural Hunters** Wild plants and creatures in Valachan usually seem hostile toward strangers. Most creatures here are carnivorous even if elsewhere they aren't.
- **Trial of Hearts** The deadly x is a battle royale that starts on the night of the full moon. Chakuna chooses participants.
- **Wilderness Domain** Valachan is covered by a fantastically dangerous rainforest. Visitors face constant perils, but the domain's residents flourish.



### Locations in Valachan

Valachan is lush and wild. Rare creatures and plants reign here, as do villages of people who understand and thrive in the rainforest. No roads pass through the land, but ships from other domains sometimes wreck on these shores. The settlement of Oselo and the Pantara Lodge are described below, and other notable locations are summarized on the Valachan Locations.



#### Oselo

The former home of Darklord Chakuna, Oselo is a prosperous village that welcomes visitors. When night falls, the residents change, shifting from people into panthers, ocelots, tigers, and other hunting cats. These shape-shifters hunt animals for food and do battle with other peoples only to defend their home. Most fear Chakuna and want no involvement with the Trial of Hearts, fearing the Darklord's wrath. However, in rare instances, Oselo's shape-shifters might be convinced to guide, hide, or otherwise aid participants in the Trial. This displeases Chakuna, but she respects the decisions of her people's elders. The villagers might adopt strangers deemed worthy, but outsiders first must prove themselves in an initiation ceremony focused on surviving unarmed in the forest for a week.



#### Pantara Lodge

The Pantara Lodge is a series of thatched structures strung together high in the forest canopy, suspended above the overgrown ruins of a burned castle. This is Chakuna's home. Its interconnected treehouses include a great hall, the Darklord's personal quarters, an armory, an infirmary, and several guest lodges. The Darklord's *Displacer Beast* and *Panther* allies prowl the trees amid the lodge's structures and can enter them freely.

**Valachan Locations**

| Location | Description |
|---|---|
| Council of the Whip Spider | Within this cavern, a sapient *Giant Spider* presides over representatives of countless insect species. Those seeking insect allies might entreat these councilors for aid. |
| Forest of Fossils | Dinosaurs and megafauna seem common in the Forest of Fossils. The region's most notorious predator is Mother Heartless, a heavily scarred *Tyrannosaurus Rex*. |
| Gasping Way | The steep walls of the forested ravine called the Gasping Way keep the forest below in near-constant shadow. *Quicksand*, common along this route, acts with deadly swiftness. |
| Poison's Taste | People say the lake called Poison's Taste is filled with the venom of a giant, sleeping snake. Most who drink from the lake die—but those who survive become immune to nearly all poisons. |
| Sangui Cove | Sharks, *Plesiosaurs*, giant aquatic snakes, and other waterborne menaces battle each other constantly in Sangui Cove. Deep below lie the wrecks of ships, some laden with fantastic wealth. |
| Shuaran | The human warriors of the village of Shuaran value honor above all. They avoid Chakuna and might help her foes or those who offer aid against the deadly howling *Apes* that dwell nearby. |
| Sleepless Forest | Noisy animals and pests are common in the Sleepless Forest. Anything that dies here reanimates as a *Zombie* the following night, shambles away, and collapses in a quieter resting place. |
| Starving Water | Skeleton-covered ruins jut from the center of the Starving Water. The deadly waters frequently release gases in limnic eruptions capable of suffocating nearby creatures. |
| Throne of Eels | An *Aboleth* named Apez-Zos lurks within bizarre ruins beneath the lake called the Throne of Eels. It has enthralled nearby lizardfolk communities into serving it and seeks to supplant Chakuna. |
| Weeping Rainforest | The predators in the Weeping Rainforest have a sadistic streak, grievously wounding their prey, then leaving it to struggle in high trees. The cries of the wounded ring through the canopy. |
| Yaguara's Heart | Within the canyon of Yaguara's Heart lies a temple, beneath which sprawl blood-painted caverns. Hidden inside is Chakuna's beating heart, which binds her to the land. |



### Chakuna

Darklord Who Hunts to Survive

![image](book/RHW/183-18-003.chakuna.webp)

> You seem capable, but do you have the heart of a hunter?

Chakuna is Valachan's deadliest hunter, a youthful werepanther with the intensity and calm of a veteran executioner. Few can elude her cold cunning, deadly traps, and packs of feline allies.

Chakuna is no mere murderer. She hunts because she must to protect the people of Oselo from a more terrible fate. To that end, she prefers to target strangers in her land, forcing them to participate in the Trial of Hearts. She relishes the chance to hunt the proud and disrespectful, as well as the skilled and unpredictable. Chakuna knows no mercy, though, and even those she comes to respect eventually face her blade. She spares the people of Oselo alone, even as her peoples' fear of her grows.


##### Chakuna

*M • monstrosity • N • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 17 | 18 | 16 | 10 | 15 | 11 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 150 ft.

**Languages** Common (can't speak in panther form)

**Challenge** {"cr":"11","xpLair":8400}

**Traits**

**Darklord Restoration.** If Chakuna dies and her heart remains intact, she revives with all her *Hit Points* in 1d10 weeks somewhere in Valachan. Chakuna's heart is a Tiny object that has AC 17, HP 10, and *Immunity* to all damage except Fire.

**Experienced Hunter.** *Difficult Terrain* composed of undergrowth doesn't cost Chakuna extra movement.

**Legendary Resistance (3/Day, or 4/Day in Domain).** If Chakuna fails a saving throw, she can choose to succeed instead.

**Legendary Actions**

**Pounce.** Chakuna moves up to half her *Speed* and makes one Scratch attack.

**Strike from Shadows.** Chakuna makes one Barbed Spear attack. If Chakuna has the *Hide* action's *Invisible* condition, this attack doesn't end that condition. Chakuna can't take this action again until the start of her next turn.

**Sudden Bite.** Chakuna uses Shape-Shift to turn into her hybrid form or panther form and then makes one Bite attack. Chakuna can't take this action again until the start of her next turn.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** Chakuna makes three attacks, using Scratch or Barbed Spear in any combination. She can replace one attack with a Bite attack.

**Bite (Panther or Hybrid Form Only).** m 8, reach 5 ft. {@h}20 (3d10 + 4) Piercing damage. If the target is a Humanoid, it is subjected to the following effect. con 15. {@actSaveFail} The target is cursed. If the cursed target drops to 0 *Hit Points*, it instead becomes a werepanther under the DM's control and has 10 *Hit Points* (use the Weretiger stat block). {@actSaveSuccess} The target is immune to Chakuna's curse for 24 hours.

**Scratch.** m 8, reach 5 ft. {@h}13 (2d8 + 4) Slashing damage.

**Barbed Spear (Humanoid or Hybrid Form Only).** m,r 8, reach 5 ft. or range 30/120 ft. {@h}8 (1d8 + 4) Piercing damage and the target receives a dire wound if it doesn't have one. While the target is wounded, its speed is reduced by 10 feet, and it loses 5 (1d10) *Hit Points* at the start of each of its turns. The wound closes after 1 minute, after a spell restores *Hit Points* to the target, or after the target or a creature within 5 feet of it takes an action to staunch the wound, doing so by succeeding on a 15 Wisdom (*Medicine*) check. {@hom}The spear magically returns to Chakuna's hand immediately after a ranged attack.

**Bonus Actions**

**Prowl (Panther or Hybrid Form Only).** Chakuna moves up to her *Speed* without provoking *Opportunity Attacks*. At the end of this movement, she can take the *Hide* action.

**Shape-Shift.** Chakuna shape-shifts into a Large panther-humanoid hybrid or a Large panther, or she returns to her true humanoid form. Her game statistics, other than her size, are the same in each form. Any equipment she is wearing or carrying isn't transformed.



#### Chakuna's Tale

For untold generations, Darklord Urik von Kharkov ruled Valachan from Castle Pantara and hunted the people of Valachan for sport. Yearly, the Darklord's hunts grew in carnage, with his favorite prey being the shape-shifters of Oselo. Von Kharkov viewed himself as the domain's greatest hunter, a title he confirmed every time he slaughtered one of Oselo's supernatural warriors.

Chakuna was a werepanther warrior of Oselo and, like most of her people, was a skillful hunter. Seeing that von Kharkov eventually would slay her entire village, she swore to save Oselo. Realizing it would take a monster to slay a monster, she left her people and sought the deepest secrets of her deadly homeland. When she returned, she volunteered to let von Kharkov hunt her. During the murderous game that followed, Chakuna burned Castle Pantara and took the former Darklord's head.

Valachan is no mundane land, though. A Domain of Dread demands a Darklord, and Valachan will be ruled only by its greatest hunter. Refusing to let von Kharkov return, Chakuna made a pact with the domain itself. Within the depths of the mazelike Yaguara Mountains, Chakuna ripped her own heart from her chest and consumed the heart of Urik von Kharkov. Doing so, she stole von Kharkov's powers. Yet to retain them, she must feed the land constantly with the blood of the hunted. If she doesn't, the plants and animals of Valachan grow murderous and howl for von Kharkov's return. So Chakuna continues a cycle of bloodshed, embracing the violence of her peoples' onetime oppressor to ensure her bitter domination of her vicious realm.



#### Chakuna's Domain

Valachan is altered by Chakuna's presence, creating the following effects.

- **Closing the Borders** While in her domain, Chakuna can close or open the borders to Valachan at will. While the borders are closed, shadowy beasts skulk or soar amid the Mists surrounding Valachan. A creature that enters the Mists for the first time on a turn or starts its turn there takes 1d10 Piercing damage.
- **Heightened Senses** Beasts and Monstrosities have *Advantage* on Wisdom checks.
- **Whispering Shadows** Humanoids subtract 1d8 from any ability checks they make when they take the *Hide* action.

If Chakuna dies, these effects end immediately.



#### Chakuna's Lair

Built above the overgrown ruins of von Kharkov's Castle Pantara, the Pantara Lodge is a maze of rope bridges, mighty boughs, and structures built among the branches of gigantic trees. Chakuna leaves those who die in the x without demonstrating skill or honor dangling from the branches of her home.



#### Pantara Lodge

The Pantara Lodge rises 80 feet above the rainforest floor. The site is depicted on Map 2.35: Pantara Lodge and has the following features:

- **Chakuna's Chambers** In her quarters, Chakuna studies lore from other realms, fruitlessly seeking ways to placate her domain without further bloodshed. Secret doors hidden here lead to her meditation chamber and a room where the undying head of Urik von Kharkov spits curses and plots his return.
- **Great Hall and Banquet Room** Chakuna welcomes guests in the lodge's great hall. Prior to the Trial of Hearts every moon, she hosts a lavish meal for her prey.
- **Trophy Gallery** The trophy gallery holds the skulls of deadly beasts, the weapons of those who failed to murder Chakuna, and the stuffed corpses of the Darklord's rivals—animals and people alike.



### Adventures in Valachan

Adventures set in Valachan involve merciless wilderness, predatory animals, and deadly hunts. Use this section to develop horror adventures in this domain.

![Lethal traps and hidden snares threaten participants in the Trial of Hearts](book/RHW/184-18-005.pantara-lodge.webp)



#### Horror in Valachan

Adventures in Valachan often include the following elements.



#### Trial of Hearts Rules

Visitors to Valachan likely are forced to participate in the Trial of Hearts, a dangerous game where the domain's Darklord hunts them. On the night of the full moon, *Chakuna* selects those she considers worthy to participate. At the Pantara Lodge, she shows her guests every courtesy, provides them with a map of the domain, and sets out these rules for the trial:

- Participants can divide into small groups or go it alone.
- Once groups are established at the trial's start, alliances between contenders aren't permitted.
- Participants must reach one of two shrines: either on Kiru Island or between the lakes called the Scars atop Anquara Plateau.
- Participants can leave the Pantara Lodge at dawn. The following dusk, Chakuna pursues the contenders with hunting partners of her choice, attempting to slay any participants she encounters outside a shrine.
- Only one person or group can occupy a shrine.
- Participants can kill one another for any reason—particularly to take a shrine.
- The trial doesn't stop for any reason until Chakuna arrives at both shrines and acknowledges any winners there.
- The Darklord's servants escort winners to the village of Shuaran, and from there, out of Valachan.
- Losers rot where they fall.
- Rule breakers are killed.

Chakuna wants the trial to be challenging. If she catches a competitor too soon, she might release them if they sacrifice an ally, a limb, or a valuable weapon. Anyone who dies in the trial feeds the domain's bloodlust—even those who fall to a threat other than the Darklord herself.



#### Valachan Exploration

Valachan is a dense and deadly wilderness. When creating adventures here, refer to Running Exploration of the Dungeon Master's Guide for details on travel and journeys with stages.

Characters use the rules in the "Travel Pace" section of the Player's Handbook. Valachan's forests prevent a party from traveling at faster than a Normal pace, and their density makes them *Difficult Terrain*, reducing travel pace by half. This means most characters can move through the domain at a Normal pace of 1½ miles per hour and 12 miles per day.



#### Flying

Difficult Terrain slows flying creatures in Valachan, due to the strong winds above the forest canopy. Flying creatures are also easy to spot, attracting the attention of *Chimeras*, *Pteranodons*, and condor-like *Rocs*. Chakuna might stipulate that flight is off-limits during the Trial of Hearts. If she does, the Mists aid in enforcing this rule.



#### Navigation

It's easy to get lost in Valachan's jungles. Unless they use gorges and waterways for guidance, characters must make 15 Wisdom (*Survival*) checks to avoid getting lost. Those who fail spend 1d4 hours wandering and risk encountering deadly creatures (see "x" for suggestions). Characters should make this check once during each stage of a journey, or after dramatic or disorienting encounters.



#### Trial Route: Kiru Island

An approximately 20-mile route from the Pantara Lodge to Kiru Island runs along the gorge south of the lodge to the Eirubamba River, then along the coast to Kiru Island. At a Normal pace, this route takes a day and a half (13 hours) to complete. Roughly 10 miles of this route follows the river. Characters who use a raft can move at Fast pace along the river. Rapids make the river *Difficult Terrain*, but even so, moving at this pace reduces the journey to just over a day (11 hours).



#### Trial Route: The Scars

Participants in the Trial of Hearts who travel from the Pantara Lodge to the Scars on Anquara Plateau have a route of approximately 20 miles if they follow the Shadowtaker Lakes east to the river called Killer's Road, then ascend Anquara Plateau. Characters can follow most of this route at a Normal pace, but 2 miles involve climbing into the mountains—a Slow pace through Difficult Terrain, reducing movement to 1 mile per hour. This route takes over a day and a half (14 hours) to complete.

![Displacer beasts and other deadly feline hunters stalk the bridges of the Pantara Lodge](book/RHW/185-18-005.pantara-lodge.webp)



#### Valachan Campaign Arc

Campaigns set in Valachan often feature the Trial of Hearts and Chakuna's connection to her domain. A campaign here might follow this outline:

- **Levels 1–3** Consider starting this campaign in another domain or world. During their travels, the characters become shipwrecked.
- **Level 4–6** The characters wash up on the shores of Valachan. They must find ways to survive the rainforest and fend off a pack of *Displacer Beasts* that stalks them. They eventually find shelter in Oselo or Shuaran.
- **Levels 7–9** Having heard of their exploits, *Chakuna* invites the characters to the Pantara Lodge, offering to help them leave if they participate in the Trial of Hearts (see the adventure below). Before the trial ensues, the characters might learn secrets from the head of Urik von Kharkov.
- **Levels 10+** If the characters survive the trial, Chakuna helps them leave the domain. As they characters travel out of Valachan, locals from Shuaran or Oselo beg the characters to stay and slay Chakuna. Should the characters kill Chakuna, chaos erupts and Urik von Kharkov strives to retake power in Chakuna's absence.



#### Trial of Hearts

Adventure for Level 8 Characters

- **Situation** To escape Valachan, the characters must participate in the Trial of Hearts.
- **Hook** The hunter *Chakuna* (see earlier in x) invites characters to Pantara Lodge to discuss helping them leave the domain.



#### Encounters

The adventure uses Map 2.35: Pantara Lodge and consists of these encounters.



#### Pantara Lodge

Chakuna seems welcoming and polite, inviting characters to relax before a feast where she'll explain how to leave Valachan. Note the *Indifferent* *Displacer Beasts* that prowl the lodge—Chakuna's guards and hunting companions. The characters receive a comfortable guest room where they can rest before dinner.



#### Chakuna's Guests

The characters aren't Chakuna's only guests. There are three other groups:

- **Lizardfolk** Tolocwa (*Lizardfolk Sovereign*) and three lizardfolk (Medium *Warrior Veterans*) are their tribe's best hunters.
- **Pirates** The human Rakengel (Medium *Pirate Captain*) and three *Pirates* from his crew were recently shipwrecked.
- **Thieves** Aian, Citana, and Lesar are *Weretigers* from Oselo who were caught stealing a rare herb.



#### Trial Rules

After Chakuna's guests have all gathered for a meal of vegetarian dishes and mineral water, Chakuna does the following:

- Explains the trial, outlining the rules from the "x" section.
- Insists this is the only way to leave Valachan.
- Notes that the group could attack her, but they would face her *Displacer Beast* allies. If they want to fight, they should wait for the trial.

The pirate group speaks up in protest, but growls from Chakuna's allies silence them. The Darklord answers questions, then encourages her guests to rest, as the trial starts at dawn. Those who leave before then violate the rules.



#### Cheating

Chakuna catches anyone who tries to leave the lodge early or otherwise cheat. She encourages them to obey the rules and calls on six *Displacer Beasts* to enforce them. She calls the monsters off before anyone dies.



#### Choosing a Route

Have the characters choose a shrine as their destination and determine their route (see "x").



#### Trial Encounters

The trial is divided into three phases, including a night camping in the jungle. As you narrate the characters' journey through the wilderness, roll on the following table for an encounter that happens during each of the first two phases and another that occurs while camping.

**Jungle Events**

| 1d8 | Characters Encounter... |
|---|---|
| 1 | An ambush by the thieves (see above). |
| 2 | Chakuna, who runs past covered in blood; then four *Displacer Beasts* attack. |
| 3 | Flooding or rock falls. A character must succeed on a 15 Wisdom (*Survival*) check or 2 hours are added to the journey. |
| 4 | Four *Swarms of Ravenous Insects*.* |
| 5 | Three *Zombie Plague Spreaders** or a *Relentless Slasher** that survived a previous trial. |
| 6 | A *Hydra* or two *Shambling Mounds*. |
| 7 | A *Tyrannosaurus Rex* or two *Giant Crocodiles*. |
| 8 | A murdered member of another group. Roll a die; if you roll an even number, the corpse has a *Potion of Healing*. |



#### Chakuna During the Trial

Chakuna might appear and menace characters, but don't track her travels or have her fight the characters directly.



#### Kiru Island Event

During the last phase of their journey, groups traveling to Kiru Island must find a way to cross Sangui Cove. While crossing, they are attacked by a *Giant Shark* and a *Giant Crocodile*.



#### Scars Event

During the last phase of their journey, groups traveling to the Scars must climb 120 feet up Anquara Plateau. While they do, a *Giant Ape* attacks them from above.



#### Trial Shrine

At both destinations, the trial shrine is a wooden platform bearing a statue of a panther. It hangs at the end of a 200-foot-long rope bridge suspended 60 feet over a spiked pit. Those who fall into the pit take 21 (6d6) Bludgeoning damage plus 36 (8d8) Piercing damage.



#### Rival

If the characters reached the shrine in less than 15 hours, they are the first ones there. After 2d4 hours, the pirate group arrives at the Kiru Island shrine, and the lizardfolk group arrives at the Scars shrine. Both groups are missing any members who died in previous encounters, but they're *Hostile* and fight the party. If the characters took longer than 15 hours, this rival group arrives first.



#### Conclusion

An hour after the group contends with its rivals, Chakuna arrives. If the characters followed the rules of the Trial of Hearts, she pronounces them victors and upholds her end of the bargain—helping them leave Valachan. If they broke the trial's rules in even the slightest way, Chakuna knows it and fights them. In either case, each character earns a bonus 2,100 XP.



## Other Domains of Dread

None can say how many domains drift through the Mists. This section hints at the multitudes of additional Domains of Dread. Detail and explore them in your adventures, or use them as examples when creating your own domains using 4.



### The Agency

- **Darklord:** Flimira Vhage
- **Hallmarks:** Detective work, memory loss

Everything inside the office of the Agency is a monotone gray. Anyone who passes the frosted glass door into this single-room domain is expected by Flimira "Flintlock" Vhage, the detective agency's owner. From here, Flimira collects cryptic correspondence relating to mysteries across the Domains of Dread. She enlists agents to investigate these cases, then report back to her. However, she never reveals her own past as a detective-turned-criminal, her involvement in every case her agency investigates, or that the Agency exists within her mind.



### Bluetspur

- **Darklord:** The God-Brain
- **Hallmarks:** Abductions, false memories, illithids

The entity that would become the God-Brain of Bluetspur was an illithid elder brain whose existence-violating experiments revealed a malignant truth of the multiverse. This secret manifested in the elder brain's mind as an alien disease. Terrified of learning this pernicious, devouring knowledge themselves, the other illithid elder brains banished their peer from existence. In actuality, the Dark Powers claimed the afflicted elder brain and granted it an alien domain. Now called the God-Brain by the mind flayers and stranger entities that serve it, this elder brain pursues radical methods of saving itself from the thoughts destroying it. Its servants claim trespassers and beings from other domains, violating their minds with their bizarre experiments.



### Carnival

- **Darklords:** Isolde and *Nepenthe*
- **Hallmarks:** Bargains, misfits, wandering exiles

The Carnival is a wandering domain that appears within other Domains of Dread. Before the Carnival appears, mysterious fliers blow into communities near where it's about to arrive. When it arrives, the Carnival sets up a surreal wonderland of entertainment and oddities staffed by performers, outcasts, and cursed individuals from countless lands. Attractions include grand shows at the big top, sideshow performances, and the Hall of Horrors. The Carnival's mysterious leader is Isolde, a good but wrathful warrior of the Feywild who's cursed to lead the Carnival even as she hunts an elusive foe across the Domains of Dread. She carries the bladelike Nepenthe, a weapon that hungers for blood. Although driven by vengeance and painful memories, Isolde protects the Carnival at all costs.



### Cyre 1313, the Mourning Rail

- **Darklord:** The Last Passenger
- **Hallmarks:** Escape from disaster, lightning rail

The disaster known as the Mourning numbers among the greatest tragedies to befall the world of Eberron—a mysterious calamity that killed nearly everyone in the land of Cyre. In the nation's capital of Metrol, some citizens foresaw the coming devastation and sought to escape on lightning rails: elemental-powered engines capable of pulling trains of passenger carts. As scared innocents packed Metrol's last lightning rail, known as Cyre 1313, the evacuation was delayed at the demand of a late-arriving VIP. Hundreds were forced from passenger carts to admit and maintain the secrecy of this last passenger and their retinue. When the lightning rail finally departed, it was too late—the Mourning overtook the train and its escapees. But even as it did so, the Mists claimed Cyre 1313 and all aboard it. Now, the last lightning rail from Metrol hurtles through the Mists as a traveling domain.

Those on board fear the disaster pursuing them, the mysterious passenger seated in the train's foremost cart, and the necrotic energy now infusing the engine's elemental spirit. Yet none of the passengers realizes that their endless quest for escape is pointless, as Cyre 1313 carries only the dead.



### Forlorn

- **Darklord:** Tristen ApBlanc
- **Hallmarks:** Life and death, strange invention

Tristen ApBlanc was born amid tragedy, the son of a vampire father and a human noble. Fearful villagers murdered his parents, leaving the boy to be adopted by druids. But during his teenage years, his *dhampir* nature revealed itself. When the druids discovered the youth's hunger for blood, they cast him out. Tristen grew enraged and slaughtered them, draining them all. The sacred waters of the druids' rituals had infused their blood, though, making it poison to the dhampir. Tristen died with his adopted family, but as the Mists closed in around their sacred stone circle, he rose as a ghost.

Unexpectedly, with the dawn, the Darklord's dhampir body was restored. Now, he lives by day, a perpetually young, charming, invention-obsessed dhampir dwelling in Castle Tristenoira, the smoking fortress his goblin servants built over the druid circle of his onetime family. At night, though, the dhampir dies a painful death, then rises in his spectral form to scour all that is green and vibrant from his land.



### Ghastria

- **Darklord:** Stezen d'Polarno
- **Hallmarks:** Cursed art, dour population

A notorious hedonist, Marquis Stezen d'Polarno enjoyed popularity among his noble peers but craved immortality. A mysterious artist offered him eternity by painting Stezen's portrait on a magical canvas. But the artist didn't mention that the painting would strip Stezen of his love of life and natural charm. Despite his dulled existence, the marquis enjoys one reprieve: Once every season, when he shows his portrait to an audience, it consumes their souls and refreshes his thrill for life. Stezen's artistic predations captured the attention of the Dark Powers, which drew his lands into the Mists. Now, Ghastria is a fertile island that, like its lord, lacks an essential vim—except for once per season, when vigor fleetingly returns.



### G'henna

- **Darklord:** Yagno Petrovna
- **Hallmarks:** Corrupt theocracy, false deity

Born of a Barovian family, Yagno Petrovna went missing on the slopes of Mount Ghakis as a youth. As a violent storm rose, he took shelter in a mysterious ruin and was found weeks later wandering the hills, babbling about an amber idol and the god he'd discovered: Zhakata the Provider and the Devourer. His family sought to help him, but when they learned Yagno had been secretly sacrificing people to his fictitious god, they chased him into the Mists. When he emerged, the domain of G'henna sprawled before him.

Life is hard in G'henna, a rocky land home to fierce, ravenous animals. The domain's starving people worship the bestial god Zhakata and regularly travel to the cathedral-city of Zhukar. There, they offer their crops in sacrifice and hear Zhakata's will through the revered prophet Yagno Petrovna.



### I'Cath

- **Darklord:** Tsien Chiang
- **Hallmarks:** Labyrinth, inescapable dreamworld

In her youth, Tsien Chiang accidentally slew her gold dragon mentor to create a magic, wish-granting bell capable of driving invaders from her homeland. Her scheme worked, and the people made Chiang their queen. Over time, though, the people bristled under Chiang's rule and rose up in revolt. Slaughter and loss on both sides led Chiang to ring her magic bell again, but this time the bell cracked, and the Mists spilled forth. When they faded, Tsien Chiang was the ruler of I'Cath, a labyrinthine, nightmare city where the people sleep endlessly. In their dreams, they toil forever in a fantasy version of the city, working to maintain the perfectionism of their harsh queen.



### Invidia

- **Darklord:** Gabrielle Aderre
- **Hallmarks:** Bad parents, possessed children

Gabrielle Aderre is convinced that her son, Malocchio, is destined for greatness. From her estate outside the village of Karina, she employs an endless string of servants to provide Malocchio with the best possible upbringing. Inevitably, though, every servant flees or vanishes, either as a result of Gabrielle's unreasonable expectations or the deadly tricks and accidents that frequently occur around the child. Gabrielle isn't content to leave her son's grand destiny to chance, though. Using her precious bone spirit board, she calls on supernatural forces to guide and protect her son. Spirits, angels, fiends, and worse answer her summons—but as long as they chart Malocchio's path to glory, the Darklord eagerly accepts their gifts.



### Kalidnay

- **Darklord:** Thakok-An
- **Hallmarks:** Magical apocalypse, obsession

The city of Kalidnay was once the seat of power of Kalid-Ma, one of the monstrous sorcerer-kings of Athas. Thakok-An, the greatest of Kalid-Ma's enforcers, desired the sorcerer-king so greatly that when she learned of a plot against her master, she didn't reveal it. Instead, she performed a magical rite to grant Kalid-Ma even greater power, sacrificing her own family to do so. Her ritual went wrong, though, and life-draining magic washed over Kalidnay, destroying the city and draining life from nearly all its residents. Awaking amid the ruins, Thakok-An found Kalidnay surrounded by an endless sea of silt and mist. Worse, rather than being empowered, Kalid-Ma languished in a cursed torpor, the sorcerer-king's vast magic bleeding away.

Now Thakok-An obsesses over her sleeping king. From Kalidnay's survivors, she's created a new cult of servants. Following Thakok-An's wishes, these templars condemn trespassers in Kalidnay to ritual combat in the arena, where the lives of the slain sustain the secretly withering sorcerer-king.



### Keening

- **Darklord:** Tristessa
- **Hallmarks:** Banshee, silent village

The forbidding land of Keening is dominated by Mount Lament, at whose base lies the village of Anwrtyn. The people of Anwrtyn deafen themselves so they won't hear the shrieking of the banshee Tristessa, a mournful spirit who roams Mount Lament and whose wail carries through the night. In life, Tristessa dwelled under Mount Arak in Tepest (detailed earlier in 2), but she was exiled for crimes against her people. In death, she endlessly seeks to reunite with the family slain by her misdeeds.

![The deadly shrieks of the banshee Tristessa echo through the mountainous domain of Keening](book/RHW/190-19-001.banshee-tristessa.webp)



### Klorr

- **Darklord:** Klorr
- **Hallmarks:** Impending doom, surreal environment

Klorr is the end of worlds. Here, shattered islands drift through a misty netherworld, caught in a swirling, clockwork spiral that ends at the unignorable, burning eye called Klorr. Thirteen stars orbit this sunlike sphere, one winking out every hour. Each time one of the stars dies, one of the domain's ruined islands is drawn into Klorr and consumed by flames. Afterward, each other island wrenches ahead, then halts, one hour closer to the same doom. When all thirteen stars have winked out, they return hourly to the sky.

Those who dwell on the crumbling islands trapped in the domain count the hours until their end. Few know how they came to Klorr or when new islands get added to the cycle, only that the Mists closed in and doomed them. Amid the realm's surreal skies float the ruins of lost domains—among them, a city of skulls, a realm overrun by dogs, and an array of bloody, iron arenas. Echoes of domains that exist elsewhere in the Domains of Dread also drift here, including at least one duplicate of Castle Ravenloft. Those cast away amid this orderly apocalypse grow ever more desperate to defy the doomsday clock and the will of a hidden Darklord, the obsessed clockmaker named Klorr.



### Markovia

- **Darklord:** Frantisek Markov
- **Hallmarks:** Depraved science, sapient animals

Dr. Frantisek Markov is a genius—but less so than yesterday. His Markov Formula grants him unparalleled intellect, but it insidiously steals more than it gives, making him increasingly dull-witted and bestial in form. Despairing, the doctor fled to a tropical island he dubbed Markovia, where he tests new versions of his formula on the local fauna in hopes of recovering his waning genius. As a result of these tests, animals across Markovia now possess sapience and have been deluded into worshipping Markov as their god.



### Nightmare Lands

- **Darklord:** The Nightmare Court
- **Hallmarks:** Nightmares, recurring dreams

Any who sleep might become forever trapped in the Nightmare Lands, a phantasmagoric realm whose features shift endlessly. Those who visit and escape speak of malicious wildernesses; the empty city called Nod; and uncountable drifting spheres, each containing a stranger's unending nightmare. Insidious entities called the Nightmare Court rule the domain. No one knows how many members make up the court, but they include the tragically graceful Ghost Dancer, the tomb-bound Hypnos, the witch Mullonga, the trickster Morpheus, and the embodiment of terror known as the Nightmare Man. These beings, artisans of nightmares, visit terrors on any whose sleeping minds brush against the domain.

The Nightmare Court's members share one commonality: All are the living nightmares of Caroline Dinwiddy, a potent psychic who has repressed memories of her own heartless deeds. These memories torment her sleeping mind, creating the Nightmare Court. Deep within the City of Nod, inside a warped reimagining of the clinic where she once worked, Caroline sleeps without waking, refusing to face the terrors her dreams unleash on innocents across the Domains of Dread and beyond.



### Niranjan

- **Darklord:** Sarthak
- **Hallmarks:** Asceticism, brainwashing, shadows

The Ashram of Niranjan is a vibrant vihara, or monastery, on a misty chain of islands. Here the elderly scholar Niranjan leads ascetics in practicing Ramsana, a way of life prioritizing nonattachment to the material world. In truth, Niranjan is Sarthak, a wicked bronze dragon who sends agents into the Mists bearing his philosophical writings. These works promise escape and peace to any who adopt their teachings and search the Mists for their source. Those who come to the ashram must divest themselves of worldly goods, which become part of Sarthak's hidden hoard. Sarthak then helps his victims enter a trance that causes their souls to slip away from their bodies. Sarthak consumes these souls and replaces them with shadows, leaving the victims' bodies under his control.



### Nova Vaasa

- **Darklord:** Myar Hiregaard
- **Hallmarks:** Nomadic riders, transformation

An unparalleled warrior, Myar Hiregaard united the nomadic tribes of the vast plains of Nova Vaasa. But, while respected as a soldier, Hiregaard made a poor peacetime leader. When brutal games could no longer keep her interest, she incited hostilities between two of her vassal tribes, then led her own forces to crush them. Subtly, she did this again and again.

After Hiregaard's greatest massacre, the Mists enfolded all of Nova Vaasa, splitting the Darklord's personality in two when they did. Now she rules her people with strict fairness—but when her bloodlust is piqued, she transforms into the raging knight called Malkan and sows discord across the plains.



### Odaire

- **Darklord:** Maligno
- **Hallmarks:** Evil toys, village of children

The toymaker Guiseppe had his wish for a family granted when his creation, the marionette Figlio, came to life. A proud father, the toymaker presented his son to all the people of his village, Odaire. The local children loved Figlio, but their skeptical parents said the marionette was nothing but a toy. Over time, this doubt enraged Figlio, and the marionette convinced Guiseppe to craft siblings for him. Then, when the time was right, Guiseppe's creations did away with all the adults in Odaire.

Claimed by the Mists, Odaire is a village populated only by children and ruled by Figlio the *Carrionette* (see x), who now calls himself Maligno.



### Richemulot

- **Darklord:** Jacqueline Renier
- **Hallmarks:** Martial law, plague, wererats

The once-beautiful cities of Richemulot crumble as season after season of the Gnawing Plague afflicts the domain. Countless commoners and aristocrats have died, causing rule to settle with the vain noble Jacqueline Renier. Unbeknownst to the people, Jacqueline is a wererat whose servants create and spread the plague. She loathes what her domain has become but refuses to cede power back to the people by ending the ongoing disaster. Jacqueline's obedient state police, the Casques Silencieux, enforce martial law and quarantines across the domain.



### Rider's Bridge

- **Darklord:** The Headless Rider
- **Hallmarks:** Haunted bridge, murderous legend

Nearly every domain knows some version of the apparition called the Headless Rider. It appears as a mercenary in dark armor in Mordent, a ghostly cataphract in Har'Akir, and a mutated centaur in Lamordia. But in each incarnation, certain details remain true: the rider lacks its head, it appears on a prominent bridge, and it decapitates victims as it endlessly searches for its own head. Anyone who escapes the Headless Rider might find a different domain on the opposite side of the spirit's bridge. (See "x" in 5 for more details.)



### Risibilos

- **Darklord:** Doerdon
- **Hallmarks:** Misdirection, ventriloquism

The Risibilos is a small music hall, similar to those found in any decent-sized city. Its lord, Doerdon, was once a king—one so thoroughly humorless that he forbade his subjects the privilege of laughter, on pain of death. He now finds himself cursed to entertain others—a task he is utterly unqualified for. Fortunately, the Mists delivered him a partner, a ventriloquist's dummy carved in the likeness of *Strahd von Zarovich*. The eerie dummy has a mind of its own, insisting it is the real Strahd and that the creature currently sitting on the throne of Castle Ravenloft is a mere impostor. It rages at the audience and makes audacious promises to any who will help it regain its station. Anyone with the slightest inkling of who Strahd is finds this hilarious. Their peals of laughter are agony to Doerdon's ears.



### Scaena

- **Darklord:** Lemont Sediam Juste
- **Hallmarks:** Reality-manipulating theater

Lemont Sediam Juste fancied himself a serious playwright, and he achieved popular, if not critical, acclaim in 2 for his works of grisly horror. But he craved respectability, and with his new play Apparitions, Lemont believed he would find it. The night of the premiere, when the audience signaled their boredom, the playwright was crestfallen. His supporters wanted blood, so he gave them what they craved.

By the play's end, Lemont had joined the drama and brutally murdered every member of the cast while the crowd roared their approval. As the show ended, the playhouse broke from Dementlieu, and Scaena was formed. Comprising a single playhouse, the domain can create any reality Lemont desires on its stage. The Darklord's immersive performances become somewhat predictable, though, as they always end in slaughter.



### Sea of Sorrows

- **Darklord:** Pietra van Riese
- **Hallmarks:** Island domains, nautical horror

The murderous pirate Pietra van Riese, captain of the Relentless, had an unsavory reputation for attaching her captives to ropes and dragging them through the water until they drowned. She never removed the detritus of her victims, even though some returned to life as zombies. Rival captains ultimately sank the Relentless, but death couldn't keep Pietra. She awoke in the Sea of Sorrows, water in her lungs and sea creatures making their homes in her flesh. Her crew stirred with her, now fish-eaten corpses. When the captain sought to speak with them, her voice emerged from their mouths.

The Relentless sails a domain that can overlap any body of water in any other domain. Some domains border the Sea of Sorrows, while others call these mysterious waters by other names. Those who venture into the Mists by ship might enter the sea's endless debris-choked expanse of eerie beasts and shifting islands, including the following:

- **Blaustein** The island-fortress domain known as Blaustein once was ruled by the notorious Bluebeard, but his spectral wives overthrew him and now endlessly torment him.
- **Dominia** The asylum of the vampire Dr. Daclaud Heinfroth rises up from the stormy island of Dominia. The asylum's patients are all dramatically different versions of Heinfroth, inspired by who he was at various points during his lengthy life.
- **Isle of the Ravens** A storm of ravens surrounds this forested islet. Hidden amid the feathered gale, an impossibly tall tower reaches into the sky. The Isle of Ravens is home to the Lady of Ravens, and any who offend her join her ebon-winged flock.
- **The Lighthouse** Otherworldly light shines from the Lighthouse, a twisted spur of bizarre fossils. Anyone who enters finds that instead of broadcasting a warning across the sea, the light calls down to what lurks in the pit hidden beneath it.
- **Vigilant's Bluff** An undead paladin holds vigil atop Vigilant's Bluff. Weary travelers can find refuge here if they respect the paladin's faith. The bones of those who don't litter the surrounding coral.



### Souragne

- **Darklord:** Anton Misroi
- **Hallmarks:** Imprisonment, swamp magic

In society, Anton Misroi presented himself as an upstanding gentleman who served as a prison warden. But within the walls of the prison, he became a sadist who believed righteousness was on his side. When his torturous punishments finally drove the inmates to rise up, the bloody riot that ensued drew the attentions of the Dark Powers. During the uprising, Anton drowned in the swamps surrounding the prison. But he rose again soon after, an undead warden in search of inmates.

Beyond Anton's prison, alligator-filled swamps cover the domain of Souragne right up to the sinking settlement of Port d'Elhour and Marais d'Tarascon, a village where above-ground crypts outnumber the residences of the living.

![In Souragne, the walking dead rise to terrorize the village of Marais d'Tarascon](book/RHW/193-19-002.marais-dtarascon.webp)



### Staunton Bluffs

- **Darklord:** Teresa Bleysmith
- **Hallmarks:** Endless warfare, repeating history

Eerily faceless mercenary regiments sweep the countryside of Staunton Bluffs. Burning villages and killing helpless residents, they push ever eastward toward Castle Stonecrest, hereditary home of the Bleysmith family. Teresa Bleysmith, spurred by jealousy of her brother, Torrence, gave her family's foes the intelligence they needed to raid Staunton Bluffs. The attack was never supposed to go so far, but the duplicitous mercenaries stormed through the countryside to take Castle Stonecrest within a day. Teresa survived the attack—but when she surveyed the damage done and found her family dead by her own designs, she threw herself from the bluffs. Now she haunts her own domain, where she repeatedly relives the day of her betrayal.



### Tovag

- **Darklord:** Kas the Bloody Handed
- **Hallmarks:** Undead military dictatorship

Notorious across the planes, the vampire Kas was once the champion of the lich Vecna. Wielding the mighty sword that bears his name, he betrayed his master, and the resulting battle supposedly destroyed them both. In truth, Vecna escaped and grew in power over ages and across worlds. Kas, though, was claimed by the Mists, and in his wasteland domain of Tovag, he believes his war with Vecna rages on. Patrols of prisoner-soldiers under undead commanders scour the land, dragooning strangers to serve in Kas's armies and to manufacture bizarre war machines. When Kas deems the time right, he sends his forces into the Mists, believing that Vecna's realm lies just beyond. Invariably, those troops never return, leaving the vampire to rage, rebuild his forces, and continue his search for the *Sword of Kas* (Magic Items A-Z in the Dungeon Master's Guide), which he considers his key to victory.

At least once, the Dark Powers have released Kas from his domain to torment their onetime prisoner Vecna. Inevitably, when Kas fails to defeat his ancient rival, the Mists return him to his domain to rage for another era.



### Zherisia

- **Darklord:** Sodo
- **Hallmarks:** Serial murderers, urban decay

Each day, the city of Paridon in Zherisia erupts in riots over food scarcity, taxation, and the disappearance of dozens of citizens every night. At least one murderer stalks Paridon: the ancient doppelganger Sodo, which has impersonated so many people that it now finds it impossible to hold a form for more than a few days at a time. As Sodo's flesh runs like hot wax, it staves off dissolution by consuming the organs of humanoids. Paridon's streets serve as the Darklord's hunting ground, and those who enter the sewers risk attracting the notice of countless insectile horrors, including *carrion stalkers* (see x) and their monstrous Hive Queen.



### Random Domains

Characters might find themselves in an unexpected domain when the Mists initially carry them to the Domains of Dread or if they aimlessly enter the Mists. When this occurs, roll on or choose a result from the Random Domains of Dread table to determine where the characters emerge. Domains marked with an asterisk (*) are featured domains detailed earlier in this book.

The Random Domains of Dread table also lists what tarokka cards are aligned with and opposed to each domain. Cards marked with a dagger (†) are also aligned with another Domain of Dread. Randomly determine which domain the Mists transport characters to when this card is drawn.

**Random Domains of Dread**

# Chapter 3: Ravenloft Adventures

![Alanik Ray and Arthur Sedgwick investigate the occult art collection of the Marquis Stezen d'Polarno](book/RHW/194-20-001.marquis-stezen-dpolarno.webp)

Drafting frightful encounters, adventures, and campaigns requires deliberate choices that cultivate an atmosphere of dread. This chapter explores how you, the DM, can use the Domains of Dread to create suspense during play and craft terrifying adventures.



## Campaigns in the Mists

The surreal natures of the Domains of Dread, their Darklords, the Mists, and the Dark Powers serve as tools in your frightful adventures. None of them are too important to use, too mysterious to reveal, or too fragile to pit against characters. This section explores how to use the most infamous features of the Domains of Dread to create frightful campaigns.

Before preparing horror adventures, review the "Ensuring Fun for All" section of the Dungeon Master's Guide.



### Creating a Horror Campaign

When planning campaigns in Ravenloft, consider the guidance in 4 of the Dungeon Master's Guide, along with the following topics. Record the answers to the questions in this section to inspire your campaign.



#### Campaign Characters

Characters exploring the Mists are the protagonists of horror stories. 1 provides advice for players creating such characters, but you should also consider the following questions:

- **Character Origins** Do the characters originate from the Domains of Dread, or were they abducted from somewhere else?
- **Context for Surreality** Do the characters realize something is strange about the Domains of Dread, or is the Land of the Mists all they've ever known?
- **Scale of Experience** Do the characters know about a single domain—perhaps one they all call home—or do they have firsthand experience with multiple domains or other settings?
- **Characters' Significance** Why are the characters special? Why did the Dark Powers, a Darklord, or something else take note of them?
- **Consistency of Experience** Do the answers to these questions apply to all of the characters?



#### Campaign Themes

Explore the types of horror adventures you're interested in by considering the following questions:

- **Horror Inspirations** What horror stories or media inspire your campaign?
- **Horror Icons** Is there a classic monster or villain that inspires the foes in your campaign?
- **Horror Genres** What genres of horror—detailed in x or elsewhere—does your campaign focus on?
- **Domains of Dread** Which Domains of Dread or Darklords do you want to focus on? Or do you want to create a new x and x following the methods in chapter 4?



#### Setting Mysteries

The Domains of Dread function in unique ways, but if and how that matters is up to you. "x" later in this chapter details ways to shape the setting to suit your adventures. Review that section and the following questions as you consider how the nature of the Domains of Dread might shape your adventures:

- **Escape** Do you want characters to pursue escape from the Domains of Dread? Do they want to leave even if a domain has been their home?
- **Islands or Regions** Does your campaign focus on a single domain, or are there multiple domains you want to explore?
- **Metaphysical Scale** Do you want your campaign to explore the unusual nature of the Domains of Dread, or is that nature broadly accepted reality?
- **Stories and Secrets** Are tales of other domains or settings treated as facts, lore known only to a few, legends, or nonsense? Is that true for all places beyond a domain's borders?
- **Traveling the Mists** Do people travel between domains? Is travel limited to wanderers such as Vistani, or are tools such as Mist talismans (see the x) common enough to allow for broader travel and trade?
- **Witnesses to the Surreal** How do domain residents react to supernatural events? Are they shocked, do they treat them as commonplace, or do they rationalize (or deny) abject horrors?

The answers to these questions are the ones that inspire you and your players.



#### Darklord Conflicts

Each Domain of Dread is a reflection of and a prison for a Darklord. The tales and torments of those Darklords are fundamental to adventures within their borders. Consider the following questions when developing your campaign:

- **Darklord Plots** Will your campaign involve the history, torment, and potential defeat of a Darklord? Or would you rather keep a Darklord in the background and focus on other stories?
- **Darklord Downfalls** Can a Darklord be defeated, or are they an enduring and recurring threat? What happens when a Darklord dies?
- **Darklord Defiance** What does it mean to best a Darklord? Does it mean slaying them, forcing them to open their domain's borders, undermining their plans, or something else?
- **Darklord Relationships** Does the Darklord want to destroy, conscript, or use the characters? Does the Darklord appear in person or communicate via proxies?
- **Darklord Rivalries** Does your campaign feature interaction between multiple Darklords? If so, how do they know about each other? What do they have to gain from their conflicts?

The "x" section later in this chapter further explores ways to implement Darklords in your campaign.



#### Starting Your Campaign

Start your campaign in a way that establishes an ominous tone or highlights the nature of the Domains of Dread. Consider the following questions:

- **Collective Misfortune** Do the characters gather to mourn the death of a loved one? Does fate bring them together as the survivors of a disaster, such as a shipwreck or massacre?
- **Darklord's Summons** When a Darklord calls, the beckoned answer. Do the characters meet after being hired by a Darklord to perform some task or by attending a social event that turns ominous?
- **Present Terror** Do the characters meet amid terrifying circumstances, such as being prisoners or experiment subjects?
- **Shared Mystery** Do the characters gather due to a shared mystery? Are they led to the same place by an enigmatic message, or do they start cooperating as they flee being accused of murder?
- **Strangers in the Mists** Are the characters united by the Mists? Might they be traveling to other destinations when the Mists unite them?

During character creation, you can work with players to come up with reasons why the characters might be in a grim or unusual situation.

A horrific origin might also unite the party. Players might be interested in their characters sharing a species or a Dark Gift from 1. A group composed entirely of Reborn or of characters who have the Aberrant Anatomy feat can provide ample inspiration for frightful adventures.



#### Campaign Considerations

Think about how you might reinforce a frightful mood over the course of your campaign. Consider the following questions about topics likely to occur during a series of adventures:

- **Allies and Sanctuaries** Is it ever appropriate to harm characters' allies or destroy places they consider safe? Is doing so worth making players feel like they've lost something they've invested in? See "Tragic Limits" in the Dungeon Master's Guide for advice on handling these topics.
- **Altered States** How might characters change during a campaign? Do you want to encourage players to develop character changes resulting from their experiences—such as scars, phobias, or x?
- **Character Secrets** What sorts of secrets might a character have, and are those boons to the game or potential disruptions? You can use the advice in the Dungeon Master's Guide on evil characters to incorporate characters with secrets into your game.
- **Death** What happens when a character dies? How might a character brought back from death be changed?
- **Fear** How do you expect characters to respond to frightful situations? Is fear reflected only by the *Frightened* condition, or would you like players to roleplay shock and revulsion?
- **Hope** How will you give characters hope and ensure they don't feel like the campaign is pointless? What rays of light perforate the darkness?
- **New Characters** If a character dies and isn't raised, how will you add a player's new character to the game? Do the Mists reveal a new hero, or might someone in a domain be inspired to act by another's sacrifice?

When thinking about the answers to these questions, avoid changing the rules of the game—these should remain the stable, agreed-on underpinnings of the game.



#### Ending Your Campaign

Horror stories often don't end well, but yours might be an exception. Have an idea of what makes a satisfying end for your horror campaign. Frame your thoughts on this by considering these questions:

- **Escape** Is the goal of your campaign for the characters to escape a domain or all of the Domains of Dread? Can they achieve this through the defeat of a Darklord, the will of the Dark Powers, or some other magical method?
- **Memorial** If a character dies, can they still contribute to a campaign's culmination? Can an accidental death become a meaningful sacrifice? Is there important work only a spirit can do?
- **Survival** Do you expect any or all of the characters to survive the campaign? Will the players be satisfied if their characters' stories end in defeat, transformation, or willing sacrifice?
- **Worthy Cause** What's the goal the characters might risk everything to achieve? Is this protecting a person or place, or is it keeping something out of a Darklord's hands? Is there a status quo that's vital to restore or a wrong that needs to be undone?

Ensure you and the players agree on what makes a fulfilling end to a campaign. Don't work toward a climax demanding a dramatic sacrifice that no one's interested in making.

![image](book/RHW/195-20-002.raven-on-candle-stick.webp)



#### Further Development

Review your answers to the questions from this section to see what patterns emerge and what answers surprised or excited you. Let those answers develop into ideas for unique horror adventures and arcs for your own campaigns. Next, review the following sections in this chapter. These explore ways to employ elements of the Domains of Dread in your horror adventures and outline whole frightful campaign arcs.



## Using Domains of Dread

Domains of Dread are backdrops to horror tales and the torments of their Darklord. These domains exist to confound and terrify those within. Everything in a Domain of Dread serves frightful ends, and if something seems like it doesn't, you just haven't revealed how yet. While creating horror adventures, consider the following facts about domains.



### Ravenloft Setting Models

What domains compose the Ravenloft setting is up to you. The Domains of Dread have no definitive map or proscribed orientation for how they relate to one another. This allows you to shape the setting however best serves your adventures. Consider the following setting models for how you might use the Domains of Dread or use your favorite elements from multiple domains.



#### Haunted House Domain

In this model, a single domain functions like a haunted house. Characters enter, terrifying forces trap them, and the party struggles to escape. This model features in the adventures I6: Ravenloft (1983) and its descendant Curse of Strahd (2016). This setting model excels if you want to...

- Explore the tale of a single domain or Darklord.
- Highlight a narrow band of horror genres.
- Avoid interacting with multiple domains or traveling the Mists.
- Make a Darklord your adventures' focal villain.



#### Islands of Terror

In this model, the Domains of Dread are isolated realms that characters might reach by braving the Mists. Domains' inhabitants might be aware of each other, but travel is uncommon and dangerous. Characters might be inhabitants of a domain or wayward souls from other realms, and events might lead them through the Mists to other nightmarish lands. This model is broadly used in this book. This setting model excels if you want to...

- Highlight the mystery and surreal nature of the Domains of Dread.
- Feature tours of multiple domains while controlling where the Mists lead.
- Explore stories focused on the nature of the Mists and escaping the Domains of Dread.
- Make Darklords part of a cast of villains.



#### Clusters and Cores

In this model, the Domains of Dread are similar to countries on globe. The Mists mark the edges of the world, rise when Darklords close their domains' borders, and appear as they please, but otherwise domains are separated by geographical and political borders. Domain inhabitants know about one another, travel, and trade, while Darklords are powerful figures that might have political or warlike aspirations. Whether you create a cluster out of a small group of your favorite domains or meld many (or all) the domains into a continent-sized core is up to you. This is the model largely used in earlier explorations of the setting, including Ravenloft: Realm of Terror (1990) and Domains of Dread (1997). This setting model excels if you want to...

- Encourage characters to roam between domains.
- Highlight villains who are infamous in multiple domains or who must be pursued (or evaded).
- Explore large-scale plots, such as wars between or the destruction of the Domains of Dread.
- Obscure Darklords, making them figures that might not be widely known.



#### Gothic Earth

The similarities between x and Dracula, between x and Victor Frankenstein, and between other Ravenloft villains and icons of horror fiction and film are intentional. Because many of Ravenloft's villains and domains have real-world roots, elements from Ravenloft are readily portable into frightful adventures set on a version of Earth steeped in magic and gothic horror. While the details of such historic horror are beyond the scope of this book, consider using the tools herein to pit characters against menaces from your favorite horror tales. This model is explored in Ravenloft: Masque of the Red Death and Other Tales (1994).



### Domain Details

To reinforce the types of horror your adventures explore and give domains their own malicious personalities, consider these setting elements.

![Those who enter the Mists...](book/RHW/196-20-003.entering-the-mist.webp)



#### Darklord Reflections

Every domain can be viewed through the lens of its Darklord, with every part of the domain reflecting some facet of the Darklord's personality, ambition, or torment. You might think about adventures in a domain as explorations of a Darklord's identity.

For example, 2 gothic horror themes include deception, oppression, and predation, all of which are aspects of the domain's Darklord, *Strahd von Zarovich*. While the village of Vallaki leans toward themes of deception, the village of Barovia, in the shadow of Castle Ravenloft, is steeped in oppression. The domain's deadly wildernesses and beasts reinforce themes of predation. When a domain's terrifying forces reflect aspects of its Darklord, that villain becomes a terrifying culmination of the evil in the land and the personification of the domain's terrors.



#### Familiar Ground

Every Domain of Dread takes inspiration from stories within its related genres. Embrace this. Including tropes from your favorite horror stories reinforces expectations about the domain and provides a shorthand to help players understand a location. The Domains of Dread are intentionally filled with gothic castles, haunted manors, and beleaguered villages to hint at the types of characters and adventures you'll find within. Don't worry about recreating familiar stories, as the unpredictable actions of the players' characters will create a unique adventure.



#### Twisted Tropes

Wildly deviating from tropes can create unique locations, but doing so requires more explanation to help players understand the setting. Consider instead featuring familiar horror settings with a twist to make them more appropriate to D&D or to enhance their terror. For example, characters escaping an alien laboratory in x might be stalked by an elusive *displacer beast*, or the ghosts haunting a house in 2 might be desperately trying to keep something worse sealed in the basement. Minor twists help setting elements feel distinct and work better in your game.



#### Isolation

Isolation can take multiple forms in a domain.



#### Character Isolation

In the Domains of Dread, the characters are often the land's only opposition to a domain's evil and their own only hope for survival. While characters might find allies or sanctuaries in a domain, the characters must look to themselves for solutions. Escape is rarely an option.



#### Physical Isolation

Each domain is a complete setting that the Mists might isolate from all other lands. Locations within a domain are often isolated by dark, monster-haunted wildernesses. Even settlements and sanctuaries might have their own grim secrets.

![... might discover nightmares worse than they escaped](book/RHW/197-20-004.nightmares-in-mist.webp)



#### The Locals

The inhabitants of domains endure or ignore the horrors around them. Whether these individuals are oppressed people or soulless pawns of the Dark Powers is up to you, but regardless, they don't effectively resist the horror within their homes. Characters should feel like they're among the only ones who recognize a domain's evil.



#### Incongruous Behavior

Consider treating a domain's inhabitants as part of the strangeness of the setting. Such NPCs might willfully ignore proof of the domain's horrors or passively behave in ways that reinforce a Darklord's will. In more surreal cases, NPCs might forget the characters or even reappear after dying.



#### Nightmare Nature

To any question regarding the natural world within a domain, the scariest answer is likely true.
