Use details of a domain to create a beat of small, unsettling moments to support the percussion of unignorable terrors in your adventures. If you highlight the strange nature of a domain often, the land feels surreal and haunted. If you do so more rarely, the domain feels more realistic. You might even change the pace of how often you reinforce the strange nature of a domain, perhaps doing so more the farther characters are from civilization or safety.

For examples of frightful details you might highlight in a domain, roll on or choose a result from the Dread Details table.

**Dread Details**

| 1d8 | In a Quiet Moment, a Character Witnesses... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Bestial eyes glaring from the shadows. |
| 2 | Clouds briefly take on frightful shapes. |
| 3 | A door unlatch and open on its own. |
| 4 | A farm animal or pet curse under its breath. |
| 5 | Flowers turn black, then wither. |
| 6 | A shadow or reflection move on its own. |
| 7 | A spectral orb drift through a wall or door. |
| 8 | A tree branch move like a grasping claw. |

You can customize these suggestions to reinforce the themes of a domain or its Darklord. For example, in 2, a statue might momentarily resemble a rotting zombie, while in 2, Darklord Ankhtepot's visage might appear in a sandstorm. Strive to make such elements feel like moments of strangeness—harmless oddities that a character can dismiss as their eyes deceiving them, rather than suggestions of an immediate threat.



## Using Darklords

Second only to the characters, Darklords are the most important inhabitants of the Domains of Dread. This section provides details and options for using Darklords in horror campaigns.



### Darklords in Your Adventures

Most Darklords are important, recurring villains. Take time to understand these characters' origins and develop details that you can consistently express as characters repeatedly encounter them, their agents, and evidence of their deeds. The Dungeon Master's Guide provides details on developing villains as well as an NPC Tracker. Use the guidance there and in the following sections to develop Darklords into infamous villains your players will be excited to learn about and oppose.



#### Roleplaying a Darklord

Most Darklords are irredeemably evil villains, obsessed with their own drives and desires. Many delude themselves into believing they're heroes or beings beyond morality. When preparing to roleplay a Darklord, review the Darklord's origin story and consider what traits are core to the Darklord. Aim to roleplay the Darklord in a way that makes sense with the villain's origins and that makes you excited to play them as a recurring character.

Then consider the following questions:

- What do you like most about the Darklord and want to highlight?
- What are the Darklord's three most positive traits?
- What are the Darklord's three most negative traits?
- Why do others fear the Darklord?
- What makes the Darklord effective in their role?
- Does the Darklord think they're a hero or better than others? Why?
- Does the Darklord always lie or never lie?
- How is the Darklord a reflection of one or more of the adventurers?
- What does the Darklord want more than anything?
- When would the Darklord be gracious or heroic?

Record your answers to these questions, then create a short list of characteristics you want to convey to the players over encounters with the Darklord.



#### Darklord Goals

In the adventure Curse of Strahd, the Darklord's goals are stated as follows:

- Transform and possess a victim
- Torment and slay a rival
- Test or toy with the characters

These goals guide Strahd's interactions with the characters through an entire campaign, allowing for the villain's consistent representation.

Recurring Darklords (or other prominent villains) should have similar, simple-to-understand goals. While you might know the finer details of a Darklord's motivations, players engage with villains only a limited number of times—likely with significant amounts of time between interactions. Choose one to three objectives for a Darklord that you can reinforce during character interactions or that you can hint at with other evidence. This helps the players understand what the Darklord wants and how to act against them.

Use the goals presented above and on the list below to inspire your Darklord's objectives:

- Change society
- Claim a new role
- Continue a tradition
- Correct a tragic event
- Defend the status quo
- Enforce order
- Escape their prison
- Find a missing person
- Maintain a lie
- Prevent the inevitable
- Recover a lost treasure
- Relieve their boredom
- Seek a revelation
- Suppress a secret



#### Darklord's Tale

A Darklord's villainy informs their goals and the torments they suffer. As characters adventure in a Darklord's domain, they learn about the Darklord, hear reports of the Darklord's infamy, and eventually discover secrets to frustrate or undermine the villain. Consider these ways of revealing details about a Darklord:

- **Rumors and Legends** Domain inhabitants typically know of a Darklord or the results of the villain's evil. They can provide consistent reports of the Darklord's depredations, what little they know of the villain's origins, and examples of how their lives are affected by the Darklord's evil.
- **Evidence** Show the characters examples of the Darklord's evil, the suffering of the villain's victims, the crimes of the Darklord's servants, and how the domain is scarred by the Darklord's wickedness.
- **Lies** The Darklord or their servants provide flattering but false details of the villain's origins, personality, or objectives. Within such lies are truths commoners don't know.
- **Primary Sources** The truth of a Darklord's past might come from the villain's family, longtime servants or rivals, or historic records—such as journals, correspondence, or neglected artwork. Magical sources, such as mirrors that reflect the past or methods to enter the Darklord's memories, might also reveal secrets. Such truths might be hidden, but the Dark Powers ensure they survive to torment the Darklord.

![The Tome of Strahd recounts the tale of Strahd von Zarovich. Other Darklords might keep similar records](book/RHW/198-20-005.tome-of-strahd.webp)



#### Darklord's Menace

Not every Darklord is a threat in combat to every party, but a Darklord's menace isn't rooted in their stat block. Rather, it's built over adventures where evidence of the Darklord's wickedness is established and reinforced. Consider the following questions to develop a Darklord's reputation, adding them as features of adventures:

- **Demonstrations** When the characters offend the Darklord, how does the villain express displeasure? Do they take it out on the domain's inhabitants? Do they dub the characters criminals or heretics and execute innocent people who helped the characters?
- **Law and Superstition** What do the domain's inhabitants do or refuse to do out of fear of the Darklord or the situation the Darklord has created? Have these habits become local traditions?
- **Servants** What serves the Darklord? Are they soldiers and servants? Are they monsters or strangely behaving animals? Is it the weather or environment itself? How do such servants make it clear they're extensions of the Darklord's will?
- **Signature Evidence** How does the Darklord prey or experiment on the domain's inhabitants and what evidence does that leave? If the Darklord executes or sacrifices foes, what is their signature form of slaughter?
- **Strangers** Do domain inhabitants believe strangers are agents of the Darklord or likely to attract the Darklord's attention? Do they avoid strangers or spy on them for the Darklord?
- **Titles** What is the Darklord's title? Is it a royal or religious title, or is it an epithet the domain's inhabitants call them?



#### Meeting a Darklord

Your players' first encounter with a Darklord should be memorable. Prior to this encounter, the characters might have heard rumors of the Darklord and witnessed their depravity. Reinforce this by planning how the characters will meet the Darklord and what the villain will be doing. Consider whether the Darklord is...

- Attempting to hire the characters.
- Commanding the Darklord's servants.
- Committing a signature crime.
- Engaged in an experiment.
- Having a decadent or horrible meal.
- Impatient with the characters' interruption.
- Pretending to be heroic.
- Trying to lure a victim.

Pay attention to the Darklord's first words to the characters. 2 presents greetings along with many Darklords' portraits. Take inspiration from these greetings, and have the Darklord's first words reflect their self-obsessed personalities and how they perceive strangers.

In future meetings, the Darklord should behave consistently. You might develop a signature way of speaking, turns of phrase, or an in-character voice for a Darklord, but keep these simple so the villain doesn't feel like a caricature or comedic figure.



#### Darklord Allies

Determine who serves the Darklord. A Darklord's servants should feel like facets of the Darklord's nature or goals. Characters should overcome these foes during adventures wherein they learn more about the Darklord. Defeating lesser villains gives characters a sense of progress while maintaining a Darklord's menace. Make a Darklord's allies exciting, but don't lose sight of the Darklord as the most important villain.

When developing allies for a Darklord, consider the following types of allies:

- **Advisers** Advisers grant the villain insights or control they wouldn't otherwise possess.
- **Copies** Some servants are lesser versions of the Darklord. They do the same things as the Darklord to a lesser extent, or they're a weaker version of the same creature as the Darklord.
- **Creations** A Darklord might be served by their creations, such as Construct or Undead servants. A relic or ritual might maintain the Darklord's control of such creatures.
- **Devotees** Devotees of a Darklord follow them without question. They might be whole organizations of soldiers or worshippers.
- **Grudging Allies** Some servants obey because they must. They might serve the Darklord to keep loved ones safe or out of a sense of duty.
- **Incidental Allies** Some allies don't directly serve the Darklord, but they and the Darklord both gain benefits from their partnership. A monster the Darklord keeps fed with sacrifices would be such an ally.
- **Majordomo** A majordomo is likely the Darklord's most powerful servant—the one who knows the most about them and, potentially, the one most likely to betray the Darklord.
- **Mini Darklords** Some servants control their own portions of a domain and embody the Darklord's will in that region.

Individual allies can occupy multiple roles.

![The Holy Symbol of Ravenkind is one example of a relic used to defeat a Darklord](book/RHW/199-20-006.holy-symbol-of-ravenkind.webp)



#### Defeating a Darklord

Slaying a villain isn't in itself a heroic goal, but the death of a villain generally means an end to its evil and its ability to affect others. Such isn't true of Darklords.

Typically, when a Darklord is defeated in combat, their domain doesn't change, and fear of the Darklord doesn't fade. Moreover, the Darklord returns after a short time. While a Darklord is sidelined, their domain-affecting powers end, their servants go without orders, and the domains' borders open. Characters might enter the Mists and find their threats reduced, but this doesn't mean the Mists allow travel to other lands.

Thwarting a Darklord and escaping their clutches ultimately means delivering the villain a dramatic defeat—one that sends them into such a state of rage, desolation, or uncertainty that their grip on their domain is undermined. Such a defeat might involve a climactic battle following a series of heroic accomplishments. If you plan a climactic confrontation with a Darklord—after which the characters escape the Darklord's domain—determine how the characters must subvert the villain. These requirements should develop from the Darklord's origins and as counters to the goals you've developed for the villain (see "x" earlier in this chapter). Take inspiration for additional goals for the characters from the suggestions here:

- **Destruction** Destroy what the Darklord draws their power from, what they've been working to create, or their sanctuary.
- **Escape** Help a victim or captive of the Darklord escape the domain, or ensure they can't be part of the Darklord's plans.
- **Isolation** Disrupt those who empower the Darklord—like their soldiers, cultists, creations, or other allies—forcing the Darklord to spend years to make more.
- **Relic** Recover a symbol, icon, or weapon that is anathema to the Darklord.
- **Rivals** Empower foes of the Darklord, resurrect storied heroes, restore bastions of opposition, or reawaken sites of good magic within the domain.
- **Truth** Reveal the Darklord as a fraud or pretender to their position.

Characters should achieve these goals over the course of multiple adventures, culminating in a climactic encounter where the Darklord discovers the full extent of the characters' successes.



#### Unexpected Ends

It's fine if characters defeat a Darklord in combat before you intend. A Darklord loses control only after extraordinary events during an adventure's climax. Until then, any defeat is an inconvenience or was part of a Darklord's plans—in any case, it's an opportunity for adventures. Don't rob characters of the accomplishment of a victory, but don't let them think they've won for long. Use the suggestions below to reinforce a Darklord's threat even after an unexpected defeat.



#### Familiar Death

This isn't Darklord's first death. As they die, a Darklord might be amused, blasé, cocky, or fascinated, but not angry or fearful. As it departs, a Darklord might congratulate the characters or narrate their own end. Before dying, the Darklord should make it clear that the characters now have the Darklord's full attention.



#### No Remains

Darklords don't usually leave corpses. When a Darklord is defeated, the Mists claim their body, or the corpse dissolves in an unsettling or thematically appropriate effect.



#### Deadly in Defeat

With the Darklord's defeat, what contingencies take effect? Perhaps the Darklord left a letter or a gift to be delivered on the event of their death. Maybe their servants have orders about what to do on the event of the Darklord's disappearance—like commencing an attack or making a sacrifice. Perhaps threats the Darklord was restraining—such as hidden monsters or volatile servants—run wild, making the domain's inhabitants desire the Darklord's return. In any case, use a Darklord's defeat to demonstrate that the villain is just the face of a much larger, evil system.



#### The Cat's Away

Use a Darklord's defeat to allow characters to have an adventure they couldn't have had otherwise. Perhaps new allies feel emboldened to share information or the guardians of the Darklord's lair are distracted. Use the Darklord's absence as a chance to reveal more about the villain and provide the characters with the tools they need to defeat the Darklord once and for all.



#### The Darklord's Shadows

The Darklord might be temporarily gone, but their evil isn't. During the Darklord's absence, consider ways the domain might focus more on the characters. Perhaps everyone in the domain whispers about them, wolves are curious about them, zombies flee from them, or the Mists seem to follow them. Cultivate the idea that the Darklord is still watching them or that the characters have violated a taboo.



#### The Darklord's Return

Determine how the Darklord returns and what they do once they're back. Does the Darklord seek revenge against the party? Is the Darklord more curious about—or obsessed with—the characters (see "Darklord Patrons" below)? Does the Darklord invite the characters to their home, devise a trap for them, or seek to involve them in some broader plot? Or was the Darklord's defeat truly inconsequential, with the characters learning of the villain's return only well afterward?



### Darklord Patrons

Most Darklords have lost track of how long they've been prisoners of their domains. Countless times they've failed to achieve their goals, and countless times the Dark Powers have tempted them with hope and opportunity again. Darklords seek new factors that might finally allow them to achieve their desires. And few factors hold more potential to further Darklords' plots—or simply distract them for a time—than the characters.

Darklords might become fascinated by characters, viewing them as potential allies, protégés, tools, or challenges to overcome. In such cases, the Darklord might patronize or test the characters, sending them on quests throughout the Darklord's domain or into the domains of rival Darklords. In return for the characters' aid, the Darklord might offer the characters escape, secrets, or treasures, or the villain might promise not to harm innocents or the characters' allies.

Darklords might serve as typical quest givers, but they tend to be more possessive of their allies. At your discretion, a Darklord's magic might grant all the characters a Dark Gift from those presented in x. Alternatively, the Darklord might grant characters a sinister supernatural gift.



#### Darklord Gifts

Darklords might bestow a supernatural gift on characters they've allied with (see "Supernatural Gifts" in the Dungeon Master's Guide for details). These sinister Blessings might be a symbol of a promise made between the Darklord and the recipient, or they might be a reward for the characters' service. A character must accept a Darklord's Blessing to receive it. The Blessing can be removed by the *Remove Curse* spell, or the Darklord might revoke it anytime.

The following Blessings are examples of those a Darklord might bestow upon a character. Customize them to create gifts appropriate to specific Darklords.



#### Mark of Beasts

Supernatural Gift (Blessing)

On granting this Blessing, the Darklord chooses a Beast associated with themself. While you are in the same domain as the Darklord, Beasts of that kind are *Friendly* toward you. Additionally, you can use this Blessing to cast *Speak with Animals* to communicate with this kind of Beast only. Once you cast this spell in this way, you can't cast it again until you finish a Long Rest.



#### Mark of the Dread Lord

Supernatural Gift (Blessing)

While in the same domain as the Darklord who gave you this Blessing, you can cast *Fear*. Once you cast this spell in this way, you can't cast it again until you finish a Long Rest.

So long as you possess this Blessing, your face is veiled by shadows.



#### Mark of Obsession

Supernatural Gift (Blessing)

Immediately after you take damage from a creature you can see within 10 feet of yourself, you can take a Reaction to force the creature to make a 14 Wisdom saving throw. On a failed save, the creature has the *Frightened* condition until the end of your next turn. Once you use this Blessing, you can't use it again until you finish a Long Rest.

While you have this Blessing, the Darklord who gave it to you can contact you once every 24 hours. This might take the form of a magical message, such as a *Sending* spell, or a short letter delivered by mysterious means.



#### Mark of Sacrifice

Supernatural Gift (Blessing)

You can use this Blessing to cast *Protection from Evil and Good*. Once you cast this spell in this way, you can't cast it again until you finish a Long Rest.

If this Blessing is removed, the Darklord who gave it to you knows your whereabouts, and you have *Disadvantage* on Wisdom saving throws for 24 hours.



## Escaping Ravenloft

The Domains of Dread are as escapable as you please. The Mists might claim characters for a single adventure, then return them home. The characters might be residents of the Lands of the Mists, making escape meaningless. Or escape from Ravenloft might motivate an entire campaign. If you make escape a focus of your campaign, consider the following questions:

- **Possibility** Is it possible to escape the Domains of Dread against the will of the Dark Powers?
- **Experts** Who might have knowledge regarding the nature of Ravenloft? What might the characters do to convince them to share their knowledge?
- **Methods** What methods might allow the characters to escape? Is powerful magic enough, or does the nature of Ravenloft need to be altered? What costs might such methods have?
- **Ramifications** Will the characters' escape only affect them, or will it have ramifications across the Domains of Dread (or the entire multiverse)?
- **Will** Do the Dark Powers have a role in the characters' escape? Must characters win these mysterious entities' favor or find ways to defy them?

Roll on or choose a result from Escape Adventure Seeds table to inspire adventure or campaign plots involving escape from the Domains of Dread.

**Escape Adventure Seeds**

| 1d6 | To Escape, the Characters Must... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Activate the Rift Spanner, a device fueled by souls stolen by the night hag Styrix. |
| 2 | Free x, allowing it to escape into the multiverse. |
| 3 | Find x and discover how he escaped 2. |
| 4 | Journey into the past and prevent x from becoming the first Darklord. |
| 5 | Sever a Darklord's tie to their domain, freeing the land back into the multiverse. |
| 6 | Use the device called the x to transport their souls into other bodies. |

![Darklord Ivan Dilisnya invites the objects of his obsessions to share in bizarre diversions at his estate, Degravo](book/RHW/200-20-007.degravo-estate.webp)



## Enemies and Allies

This section presents individuals and groups who might appear anywhere in the Lands of the Mists. Such individuals and organizations might create continuity between domains, facilitate travel through the Mists, or provide support to characters. Alternatively, they might serve as opponents capable of confounding characters in multiple domains.



### Mist Wanderers

Individuals who travel the Mists might ally with characters or share mysteries that lead to adventures elsewhere in the Domains of Dread.



#### Alanik Ray

The Great Detective

Alanik Ray is a peerless, elf investigator renowned in multiple domains as a master sleuth and solver of confounding mysteries. Alanik resides in Port-a-Lucine in 2 with his husband, Arthur Sedgwick, but he investigates mysteries and aids sleuths across the Domains of Dread.



#### Arthur Sedgwick

Pragmatic Investigator

Together with his husband, Alanik Ray, the physician Arthur Sedgwick investigates criminal cases and paranormal mysteries. The practical half of the detective duo, Arthur chronicles their adventures, having published two volumes: The Life of Alanik Ray and The Casebook of Alanik Ray.



#### Ez d'Avenir

Fearless Adventurer

As a former pupil of x, *Ez d'Avenir* (detailed in x) is no stranger to the dangers haunting the Mists. Since venturing out on her own, Ez has gained a reputation as a skilled monster hunter and foe of evil. She often allies herself with other adventurers to put an end to evils.



#### Firan Zal'honan

Scholar of Sinister Secrets

The arrogant scholar Firan Zal'honan seeks the secrets underpinning the Domains of Dread. He plots to use his discoveries to escape the Mists into the "true realities" beyond. Firan hires agents to aid in his expeditions or to ferry him through the Mists—which he claims want to disrupt his efforts. Secretly Firan has ties to x, the missing Darklord of Darkon, or might be the Darklord in disguise (see 2 for details).



#### Larissa Snowmane

Domain-Traveling Riverboat Captain

Larissa Snowmane ferries travelers between the Domains of Dread aboard her riverboat, River Dancer. Larissa protects those traveling with her. In the most dire circumstance, she uses her mysterious magic, the Dance of the Dead, which can control the dead at the risk of slaying the living. Larissa learned her magic in part from Anton Misroi, Darklord of x. She avoids that swampy domain at all costs.

![Larissa Snowmane's ship, River Dancer, navigates the waterways of the Domains of Dread](book/RHW/201-20-008.river-dancer.webp)



#### Savra Sunstar

Dhampir Vampire Hunter

Savra Sunstar is a monster hunter and the dhampir daughter of Jander Sunstar, a vampire hero who saved Savra's mother from an early demise. For her part, Savra despises her father and seeks to slay him. She has devoted her life to hunting vampires and allies herself with like-minded adventurers.



#### Weathermay-Foxgrove Twins

Paranormal Investigators

The twins *Gennifer* and *Laurie Weathermay-Foxgrove* (detailed in x) are tenacious adventurers who follow their family's tradition of slaying monsters and defending the innocent. They reside in Mordent and have learned much from their surrogate uncle, x.



### Organizations

These organizations span multiple domains.



#### Church of Ezra

- **Goal:** Seek mercy from an ambivalent god
- **Adventure Themes:** Apathetic congregations, superstitions, witch hunting

Pious souls in multiple domains pray to Ezra, an aloof god who personifies the Mists. Ezra's worshippers appear in congregations with varied (and sometimes conflicting) practices. The church serves largely as a formalization of local superstitions, whether in modest rural temples or urban cathedrals. When common folk give voice to their hopes or seek to ward off evil, they often pray to Ezra.



#### The Circle

- **Goal:** Vanquish evil through acts of self-sacrifice
- **Adventure Themes:** Bravery, hubris, proof of heroism, quests against evil, tragedy

Bold knights of the Circle quest from the 2 in search of evil. More often than not, though, they find tragic fates. Even successful knights often venture back to the Shadowlands with evidence of their victories, potentially carrying evil back to their homeland. The knights of the Circle provide bold but reckless assistance to other would-be heroes, endlessly seeking to prove their valor.



#### Keepers of the Feather

- **Goal:** Discover the paranormal and dispel evil
- **Adventure Themes:** Paranormal investigations, occult mysteries, mysticism

The founding members of the Keepers of the Feather are *wereravens* (see x) in 2 who oppose Strahd and whose reach extends to other domains. These Keepers are cautious, hiding their nature and guiding others so as not to jeopardize themselves or the mystical secrets they've gathered over generations. Many aided by these wereravens aren't ever aware of their assistance.

In other realms, mysteries and talismans of the Keepers of the Feather have fallen into the hands of socialites and spiritualists. In social clubs, curious occultists pursue the mysteries of séances, fortune telling, metaphysical theories, and tales of the macabre. Such dabbling is as likely to cause catastrophes as it is to help those in need. These Keepers identify themselves with amulets that mimic the shape of a Barovian relic known as the *Holy Symbol of Ravenkind*.

Both factions maintain a network of trained ravens that send messages between group members in different domains.



#### Order of the Guardians

- **Goal:** Destroy or contain cursed items and phenomena
- **Adventure Themes:** Ending curses, exorcisms, supernatural investigations, vault defense

A network of monastic occultists, the Order of the Guardians hunts and destroys dangerous supernatural objects, cursed items, and stranger anomalies. If the Guardians can't destroy dangerous relics, they contain them within hidden, heavily warded vault-monasteries. The Guardians might share goals with characters trying to prevent supernatural dangers, but they might also consider characters who employ dangerous magic to be threats.



#### Priests of Osybus

- **Goal:** Release x
- **Adventure Themes:** Cult rituals, necromancy, secrets of the Domains of Dread

The *Priests of Osybus* follow the teachings of a depraved lich and steal souls to transcend death. With their foul immortality, they seek to free Strahd von Zarovich from the Mists, an act they believe will cause the dissolution of the Domains of Dread. This inspires the priests to learn all they can about the deepest mysteries of the Mists. In shadowy cults, they conduct rituals aimed at escaping the Mists. These priests are detailed further in x.



#### Ulmist Inquisition

- **Goal:** Destroy the evil that dwells in wicked hearts
- **Adventure Themes:** Ends justifying the means, hunting evil, psionic interrogation

The three branches of the Ulmist Inquisition employ psionic powers to stamp out evil, but their zeal and willingness to peer into others' minds cause people to fear the inquisitors as much as the villains they oppose. Cells of the Ulmist Inquisition often ally with the Church of Ezra and oppose the priests of Osybus. Ulmist inquisitors might side with adventurers against evil, but they often test the virtue of their allies' souls. These inquisitors are detailed further in x.



#### Vistani

- **Goal:** Find a way home, preserve age-old traditions, predict and avoid dangers in the Mists
- **Adventure Themes:** Reliable guides, stories from various lands, travel between domains

Known throughout the Land of the Mists, Vistani (singular: Vistana) have a unique understanding of the Domains of Dread and the hidden paths between them. Following itinerant traditions, many Vistani and their adopted family members travel between domains, learning of distant lands, the many faces of evil, and strange wonders. Vistani never linger in one domain for long, as they endlessly seek a path to their legendary homeland.



## Horror Atmosphere

![Light, music, and props all contribute to a frightful atmosphere](book/RHW/202-20-009.frightful-atmosphere.webp)

Frightful D&D adventures benefit from a game atmosphere that reinforces the horrifying plot. Consider these elements to influence your game's atmosphere, customizing what you can and not fretting about what you can't:

- **Location** Strive to play in an area with minimal distractions that all players are comfortable in. Reduce distracting stimuli by turning off unnecessary screens and removing nongame materials.
- **Lighting** Dimming the lights can cause distractions to fade and create an eerie ambiance in your game space. You can also adjust the lighting to reflect a setting's light level, if it's easy for you to do so. However, always ensure the players have enough light to read by.
- **Music** You can use music to reinforce an adventure's mood. Create playlists in advance, choosing options without lyrics and that aren't recognizably tied to popular media. If you can subtly control volume, slowly raise it when you want attention and lower it when players are talking. Experiment with how volume and tempo influence the mood of a scene.
- **Props** Props and handouts are useful but shouldn't become chores or distractions. They might be as simple as a whiteboard for notes or a handwritten letter from a Darklord. Ravenloft has a history of featuring props in its adventures, such as the tarokka deck (see 6).



## Horror Roleplaying

Consider the following methods to develop a sense of dread during your horror adventurers.



### Describing Horror

Rather than just naming a threat, inspire your players' imaginations by describing the horror indirectly using the following techniques:

- **Before It Arrives** Foreshadow the horror's approach. How do the environment, nearby animals, the weather, or shadows react to it?
- **Approaches** What sounds does the horror make as it moves? What parts do characters see before the whole comes into view?
- **Up Close** What does the horror smell like? How does it breathe? Does the air around it grow cold?
- **Attacks** How does the horror attack? What does damage from it feel like? When it grabs a character, what does it feel like? Does it have physical weapons, or is it a supernatural force that warps other life?
- **Wounded** When the horror is wounded, how does it react? What does its blood look like? What is inside it?



### Horror Pacing

Not everything can be scary, and continuous terror is unsustainable. Before players grow numb to endless tension, create opportunities for them to catch their breath and regain a feeling of calm. The best horror adventures are like roller coasters, ratcheting up suspense and releasing it before building toward the next harrowing moment.



### Idle Uneasiness

Occasionally slow your adventure's pace to draw out tension. Linger on describing details. Ask players to describe what their characters are thinking or feeling, or ask what the players think is the worst possible thing that could happen right now. Describe feelings of being watched. Let characters respond to these stray thoughts. Sometimes these impressions should just be their nervousness getting to them. But sometimes it's the calm before a threat strikes.



### Let Players Fill Gaps

Invite players to turn their imaginations against themselves. Ask players to fill in details with questions like these: What does the way it moves remind you of? It emits the worst smell—what is it? Something on the shelf reminds you of a nightmare—what is it? Players' responses don't need to control the narrative; it's up to you whether these responses are true or just the characters' perceptions.



### Mood Modeling

Model the behaviors you want players to emulate by focusing on the game, letting others speak in turn, heading off encroachment on boundaries, and complimenting exciting choices. Stand or pace during intense moments. Speak faster or anxiously when something scary is happening. Raise your voice during pitched battles, and whisper during tense or conspiratorial moments. Allow yourself to sound uncertain, correct yourself, or pause as if you heard something outside. Ask players, "Are you sure?" By engaging with the suspenseful atmosphere you want to create, you bring it into being at the table.



### Out of Time

When the time for action comes, make your narration urgent. Speak quickly and in short bursts. Focus less on senses and more on descriptions—a splash of crimson, who knows where it came from? Politely demand players react quickly: "There's no time to debate—what do you do?"



### Reliability and Trust

Reliability and trust are just as important to your horror adventures as lurid shocks. Frequent betrayals can make players hesitant, so emphasize that certain people and locations are trustworthy through repeated positive encounters.



### End on Cliffhangers

Leave players excited to play again. When ending a session, implement one of the following to conclude on a cliffhanger: Hint at a new threat, impose a complication on existing plans, increase the stakes, introduce a new mystery, have a foe appear, have the world change, or otherwise shock the characters. Then call for a break before players can react.



## Haunted Bastions

The rules for 10 in the Dungeon Master's Guide allow characters to establish sanctuaries to rest and accrue resources between adventures, but these redoubts aren't outside the grasp of the Mists.



### Bastions in the Mists

Bastions in the Domains of Dread work well in campaigns that focus on a single domain or where Darklords aren't likely to seal their domains' borders and cut characters off from their Bastions.

Characters can create Bastions in any domain. The domains of 2, 2, 2, 2, and the 2 are well suited to hosting Bastions due to their large size or aloof Darklords. Consider having characters inherit one or more existing structures—such as a ruined fortress, secluded tower, or house recently scoured of ghosts. Should characters adopt such a structure, they can refurbish it to their specifications.

How Darklords respond to Bastions is up to you, but don't create plots that are hostile to Bastions. Darklords might ignore a Bastion, be curious about it, or use it as one more way to bind characters within their domains.

![The Dark Powers might intrude on any sanctuary, even characters' personal Bastions](book/RHW/203-20-010.dark-powers-in-bastion.webp)



### Haunted Bastions

Haunted Bastions are afflicted by unusual supernatural events. These might be unpredictable annoyances at first, but clever characters might turn hauntings to their advantage.

If you use this system, the first special facility characters create in their Bastion is Haunted. A Haunted special facility has the following rules:

- **Irreplaceable** A Haunted special facility can't be replaced until it is no longer Haunted.
- **Repeating** While there is at least one Haunted special facility in a Bastion, whenever a character gains a new special facility or replaces a special facility with a different one, roll any die; on an even result, that new facility is Haunted.

When a character issues an order to a Haunted special facility or a Maintain order to their whole Bastion, roll 1d6; on a 1, roll on the Bastion Hauntings table and refer to the "x" section to see what happens. A Bastion can experience only one haunting per Bastion turn.

**Bastion Hauntings**

| 1d100 | Haunting |
|---|---|
| 01–07 | Cursed Hireling |
| 08–15 | Free-Roaming Spirit |
| 16–22 | Friendly Ghost |
| 23–29 | Hidden Room |
| 30–38 | Lightning Storm |
| 39–47 | Living Dead |
| 48–55 | Mist Wanderers |
| 56–63 | Mysterious Priest |
| 64–71 | Ill Luck |
| 72–79 | Poltergeist |
| 80–86 | Spacial Warp |
| 87–93 | Spectral Vision |
| 94–100 | Vistani Visitors |



#### Haunting Descriptions

The hauntings from the Bastion Hauntings table are detailed here in alphabetical order.



#### Cursed Hireling

One of your Bastion's hirelings is cursed. As long as the hireling remains cursed, it won't leave the special facility it manages, and any work conducted in that facility takes twice as long to complete.



#### Free-Roaming Spirit

A random special facility in your Bastion becomes Haunted. If all the special facilities in the Bastion are already Haunted, the DM rolls again on the Bastion Hauntings.



#### Friendly Ghost

A benevolent spirit possesses a hireling of the DM's choice. If the special facility where the hireling works produces items or Gold Pieces, it produces twice as much as usual as long as the hireling remains possessed. The spirit departs after 14 days.



#### Hidden Room

The spirits reveal a hidden closet within your Bastion. Add a 5-foot-square space to your Bastion. Something might lie inside, at the DM's discretion.



#### Lightning Storm

Trade orders issued this turn have no effect (including one that triggered this haunting, if applicable). If you have a Lightning Generator special facility, this Bastion Haunting has no effect.



#### Living Dead

A group of mindless undead shamble from the Mists. The Attack Bastion event occurs, but roll 3d6 for that event rather than 6d6.



#### Mist Wanderers

The Mists rise and 1d4 strangers emerge, seeking shelter. If there is room in your Bastion, they join as hirelings. Otherwise, they linger for 1d4 days before vanishing into the Mists.



#### Mysterious Priest

A hooded priest appears at the Bastion, attracted by its haunting. Roll any die. One of the following occurs based on whether you rolled an even or an odd number on the die:

- **Inquisitor (Even)** The priest is a witch hunter. If you have an Ancient Altar, Arcane Study, Cabinet of Curiosities, or Séance Parlor in your Bastion, the priest destroys it and you must replace it with a different special facility. If your Bastion has none of these facilities, the Extraordinary Opportunity Bastion event occurs.
- **Exorcist (Odd)** The priest is an exorcist. If you have a Reliquary, Sacristy, Sanctuary, or Sanctum in your Bastion, the priest offers to remove a haunting from one facility. If you agree, choose one Haunted facility; that facility is no longer Haunted.



#### Ill Luck

Accidents and bad luck plague your Bastion. Harvest orders issued this turn have no effect (including one that triggered this haunting, if applicable).



#### Poltergeist

Disruptive happenings plague the Bastion. Empower and Research orders issued this turn have no effect (including one that triggered this haunting, if applicable).



#### Spatial Warp

The nature of a Bastion special facility changes. Roll 1d4. On a 4, replace one of your Bastion's special facilities with another for which you qualify; otherwise, increase the Facility Space of a Cramped special facility in your Bastion to Roomy or a Roomy one to Vast, at no cost.



#### Spectral Vision

A ghostly vision of a past event plays out. You gain some insight into the spirits that haunt your Bastion or the history of the surrounding land, as though affected by the *Legend Lore* spell.



#### Vistani Visitors

Vistani travelers visit your Bastion, drawn by tales of the spirits that inhabit it. In return for a night's shelter, they offer to reveal your fate via a casting of the *Augury* spell or through a tarokka reading (see x). If you turn them away, they depart, but the highest-level special facility in your Bastion that isn't already Haunted becomes Haunted.



### Special Facilities

Characters can create the following special facilities in addition to those in the Dungeon Master's Guide. These facilities are summarized on the Special Facilities table.

**Special Facilities**

| Level | Special Facility | Prerequisite | Order |
|---|---|---|---|
| 5 | Rookery | None | Craft |
| 5 | Séance Parlor | None | Research |
| 9 | Ancient Altar | None | Empower |
| 9 | Cabinet of Curiosities | None | Trade |
| 9 | Infirmary | Proficiency in the *Medicine* skill | Craft |
| 13 | Lightning Generator | None | Empower |
| 13 | Spirit Vault | None | Research |
| 17 | Liminal Space | None | Recruit |

![Spirits and grim secrets haunt Bastions in the Demiplanes of Dread](book/RHW/204-20-011.demiplanes-of-dread-bastion.webp)




# Chapter 4: Creating Domains of Dread

![A hexblood witch in the domain of Tepest conjures visions of adventurers' fatal fates](book/RHW/206-21-001.hexblood-witch.webp)

Any fear might find terrible life amid the Domains of Dread. Each domain highlights its own distinctive terror or flavor of the macabre. 2 presents numerous Domains of Dread and their respective Darklords, but you can blend legendary evils, unexpected monstrosities, and grim settings into your own horrifying creations.

This chapter explores how to create a Domain of Dread, starting with defining its Darklord, the villain at the domain's heart. Descriptions of various genres of horror also provide details to guide and inspire your creations.

**Tarokka and Random Tables**

This section provides random tables compatible with the tarokka deck (see 6). Here's how to use the tarokka deck—or playing cards—instead of a d10 to generate random results:

- **1: Remove the High Deck** Remove all high deck cards, leaving only cards numbered one through nine plus the master of the suit.
- **2: Draw a Card** Ensure the deck is well shuffled, then draw from the top.
- **3: Consult a Table** Reference the card's number to find your result on a table; in the tarokka deck, the master of a suit counts as a ten.

When using the tarokka deck, you can let the card's suit add extra dimension to your results. The four of coins might encourage you to link that aspect of the Darklord to wealth, while the four of swords could provide an interpretation rooted in violence. Appendix A details interpretations of the tarokka deck's cards.



## Creating a Darklord

Domains are reflections of and prisons for the Darklords they confine. To devise a Domain of Dread, first consider its central antagonist and prisoner: its Darklord. The following sections detail how to develop a Darklord as a focal antagonist in your horror adventures.



### Building Your Darklord

A Darklord's memories, desires, mistakes, and evil deeds shape a domain and its inhabitants. This chapter presents tables with suggested questions and motifs related to a Darklord's past and personality. Choose or randomly generate prompts to develop your Darklord further, or use the table entries as inspiration.

To build a Darklord, follow these steps:

- **Step 1:** Choose Genres. What horror genres does your Darklord fit into? Use those genres' principles to help develop your Darklord.
- **Step 2:** Determine Their Past. Who was the Darklord before they turned to irredeemable evil? What ambitions and flaws drove them to commit heinous acts? How did the Darklord first attract the attention of the Dark Powers? The "x" section provides a multitude of prompts to inspire your Darklord's origin story.
- **Step 3:** Determine Their Identity. What monstrous form does your Darklord's evil take? Turn to each genre chosen in step 1, then consult that genre's respective "Villain Identities" and "Villain Torments" sections. Feel free to mix and match the tables from different genres to achieve your desired feel.



### Genres of Horror

Horror stories span a wide variety of genres. One tale might explore the grotesque, warping flesh and bone into perversions of the living; another might be fantastical and philosophical, using restless ghosts to examine the nature of the soul.

Before you begin building a Darklord, consider which genres of horror you'd like to explore. The Genres of Horror table describes the six major genres of horror explored later in this chapter and their common motifs. If you're uncertain where to start, use the table to identify which motifs interest, excite, or inspire fear in you. The sections later in the chapter also detail each genre's core principles, which drive how you develop the Darklord, the domain, and the adventures within.

These genres aren't mutually exclusive. Feel free to blend themes from different genres to create a unique and terrifying story. The end of this chapter briefly describes a handful of additional genres for consideration.

**Genres of Horror**

| Genre | Characters in Stories of This Genre... | Common Motifs |
|---|---|---|
| x | Explore the unpredictability of flesh. | Gore, loss of bodily autonomy, parasitic infestations |
| x | Face incomprehensible insignificance. | Faceless terrors, infinite voids, unblinking eyes |
| x | Battle grim evils and wicked magic. | Antiheroes, evil witchcraft, misty forests |
| x | Unmask ancient taboos and traditions. | Cryptic legends, masked cults, secluded towns |
| x | Examine mortality and tragic histories. | Decrepit mansions, incorporeal haunts, old ruins |
| x | Confront passions and evils within. | Ancient castles, strong emotions, tarnished splendor |



### Darklord's Past

Every Darklord has committed irredeemable acts that attract the attention of the Dark Powers. Yet Darklords are still individuals who, at one point, had a home, childhood, and family. The following sections each examine a different aspect of the Darklord's life prior to imprisonment.



#### Past Life

What circumstances and choices pushed the Darklord down their twisted path? Choose or randomly generate at least three questions from the Past Life table to answer. If you generate the same question again, use the question one above or below the entry instead.

**Past Life**

| 1d10 | Question |
|---|---|
| 1 | Does the Darklord feel that they have any hope of redemption? Do they want it? |
| 2 | How did the Darklord react when challenged? |
| 3 | What ideal or philosophy governs the Darklord's greater actions? |
| 4 | What locations and circumstances shaped the Darklord's adolescence? |
| 5 | What pushed the Darklord to continue committing heinous acts? |
| 6 | What person, place, or object does the Darklord desire most? |
| 7 | What was the first depraved act the Darklord committed? |
| 8 | Whose respect did the Darklord crave? |
| 9 | Who hurt the Darklord? |
| 10 | Who loved the Darklord? |



#### Dark Catalyst

Negative emotions can twist one's ideals into something sinister. Choose or randomly generate at least one prompt from the Dark Catalyst table to develop what encouraged the Darklord's corruption.

**Dark Catalyst**

| 1d10 | Something in the Darklord's Past... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Caused them to obsess over control. |
| 2 | Celebrated the Darklord's heinous activities. |
| 3 | Drove them toward bloodthirsty revenge. |
| 4 | Enabled their indulgence and vices. |
| 5 | Escalated their violent tendencies. |
| 6 | Fueled an all-consuming fear of loss. |
| 7 | Pushed them to turn to a greater power. |
| 8 | Removed their empathy for others. |
| 9 | Sowed paranoia, encouraging them to constantly test their allies' loyalty. |
| 10 | Spurred them to pursue perfection. |



#### Wicked Ambitions

All Darklords have a core ambition or goal that drives them to commit evil acts. These unobtainable goals fueled their corruption and motivate the Darklords' conflicts with adventurers in their domains. Choose or randomly generate such a goal from the Wicked Ambitions table.

**Wicked Ambitions**

| 1d10 | The Darklord... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Seeks an apprentice or inheritor. |
| 2 | Explores ways to forget the past. |
| 3 | Longs for divine or otherworldly power. |
| 4 | Pursues ways to relieve themself of loneliness. |
| 5 | Relentlessly pursues the reincarnation of a loved one. |
| 6 | Searches for an object or artifact. |
| 7 | Seeks vengeance against a person or ideal. |
| 8 | Struggles to cheat death. |
| 9 | Wants to be a hero—but one who is twisted to the extreme. |
| 10 | Wishes to be beautiful and admired. |



#### Intervention of the Dark Powers

Consider how the Darklord attracted the attention of the Dark Powers. On the completion of an act of remarkable depravity, the Mists claim the Darklord—and perhaps their home—imprisoning them in a new Domain of Dread. The deed that ultimately causes a villain to be claimed by the Mists needn't be devastating, but it should represent an evil novel enough for the Dark Powers to take note. Use the Darklords' tales from 2 to inspire how a Darklord might be claimed by the Mists.



### Birth of a Darklord

Now trapped in a domain tailor-made to be their prison, the Darklord is immortal, and their greatest desire is just out of reach. At this point, you should have an idea of who the Darklord is, what they did, what form their evil takes, and how they came to the attention of the Dark Powers.

Now consider how the Darklord's evil manifests in their domain and how it brings them into conflict with the adventurers and the domain's inhabitants.



#### Monstrous Identities

Some Darklords undergo harrowing transformations on their imprisonment, as the Dark Powers warp those Darklords' forms to reflect their evil. Alternatively, the Darklord might have been a monster to begin with, or perhaps they gained their form and powers through their deeds or a curse.

Consider how your Darklord is viewed by inhabitants of their domain. Reference the genres of horror that your Darklord fits into (later in x), and use a genre's "Villain Identities" and "Villain Torments" sections to shape the Darklord's monstrousness. The "Villain Identities" sections provide options for the Darklord's primary identity or form while within their domain, while the "Villain Torments" sections provide torturous twists that the Dark Powers might employ to torment the Darklord and reflect their evil.



#### Finishing Touches

The story of a Darklord entwines with those of the adventurers and the domain itself. As you finish fleshing out your Darklord's details, consider the following options to further connect the Darklord to their domain and the adventures within it.



#### Endless Torment

In every domain, its Darklord's greatest desire remains in view but ever out of reach. How does your Darklord's torment remain central to and unignorable in the story?



#### Misty Borders

The x surround each Domain of Dread. The Dark Powers afford Darklords some control over the Mists bordering their domains. Does your Darklord allow the Mists to function undisturbed, or do the Mists also reflect the Darklord's nature, perpetuating the cycle of torment?



#### Supporting Cast

Consider what NPC types support the Darklord, exacerbate their threat, or oppose them. How do the inhabitants of the domain play into the Dark Powers' plans, taking the Darklord's situation from bad to worse?



## Creating a Domain

![Domains of Dread might be any size or shape and can draw inspiration from any horror genre](book/RHW/207-21-002.different-domains-of-dread.webp)

Once you've developed a terrifying Darklord, start shaping that Darklord's unique Domain of Dread. Everything in this realm is inspired by the Darklord's torment or personalized to it.

This section provides guidelines to help you create a suitably terrifying and tragic Domain of Dread.



### Building a Domain

Similar to building a Darklord, you can choose or randomly generate prompts from the tables below to flesh out the domain's details.

To build a Domain of Dread, follow these steps:

- **Step 1:** Choose Genres. Most Domains of Dread are inspired by the same horror genres that shape their imprisoned Darklord, but feel free to mix in new genre elements.
- **Step 2:** Develop Details. What are the distinctive elements of the domain? How do these elements reflect and twist the Darklord's past, furthering the Darklord's torment? The "Dread Details" section contains several tables with prompts to tailor your domain to its central prisoner.
- **Step 3:** Create Adventures. What adventures will the characters have in this domain? Turn to the genres chosen in step 1, and consult their "Adventure Hooks" and "Adventure Settings" sections to inspire your adventures.
- **Step 4:** Choose Monsters. The genres later in x each include a table suggesting a plethora of monsters that suit the genre's sensibilities. Consult those monster tables, and choose which terrifying creatures will haunt the characters in the domain. If none of the suggested monsters fit your ideas, you can reskin or alter the suggested monsters or choose ones that do.



### Dread Details

The domain's buildings, natural elements, landmarks, and creatures reflect the Darklord's vile past. This section provides prompts for developing elements of your domain and connecting those specifics to the imprisoned Darklord.

Don't get bogged down with the particulars of a working society. Things like weather, ecosystems, and agriculture needn't follow logic in a domain. Mundane details can fade into the background as your adventures focus on the domain's threats.



#### Domain Elements

Above all else, a domain is a torturous prison for its Darklord. Visceral sights, sounds, and smells within the domain should hint at the Darklord's past villainy or serve as a means for the Dark Powers to torment the domain's central prisoner.

Choose or randomly generate at least three questions from the Domain Elements table to answer. If you generate the same question again, use the question one above or below the entry instead. Don't be afraid to combine details in unexpected ways—the more unnatural or off-putting, the better.

**Domain Elements**

| 1d10 | Question |
|---|---|
| 1 | What sounds, smells, colors, or symbols pervade the domain? |
| 2 | Where do the Mists appear besides the domain's borders? What shapes and sounds haunt the Mists in and near the domain? |
| 3 | What is visible in the sky? Is there a day-and-night cycle? What's the weather like? |
| 4 | What is the domain culture's general attitude toward the Darklord? |
| 5 | What does the domain culture fear or consider taboo? |
| 6 | What does the domain culture celebrate? |
| 7 | What is scarce in the domain, and how do the inhabitants compensate for this? |
| 8 | What do buildings in the domain look like? Are they new or old? |
| 9 | What biome is the domain's environment (e.g., arctic, desert, forest)? |
| 10 | What justifications do the inhabitants use, if any, to pretend nothing is wrong in the domain? |



#### Darklord's Shadows

A domain's features are constant, painful, and symbolic reminders of the Darklord's wicked past. Choose or randomly generate at least one prompt from the Darklord's Shadows table to develop how the domain reflects the Darklord's history. Consider connecting the results to your answers to the questions in "Domain Elements."

**Darklord's Shadows**

| 1d10 | The Domain Reflects... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A taboo the Darklord broke. |
| 2 | Someone the Darklord killed. |
| 3 | Someone or something the Darklord loved—and lost. |
| 4 | Esoteric knowledge the Darklord sought but couldn't obtain. |
| 5 | A tradition sacred to the Darklord's home. |
| 6 | An act of extreme violence the Darklord committed. |
| 7 | The Darklord's greatest temptation. |
| 8 | Someone the Darklord betrayed. |
| 9 | The Darklord's greatest fear. |
| 10 | Evidence of the Darklord's vilest act. |



## Unleash Your Horror

At this point, you should have a wealth of information about your Darklord and their domain. Review your notes, connect elements, establish recurring themes, and consider ways to foreshadow circumstances that adventures might focus on. You don't need to have answers for every question now; you can define many details during adventures or by focusing on elements your players gravitate toward. For examples of fully detailed Darklords and domains, see 2.



## Genres of Horror

The following sections provide overviews of several genres of horror. Use these to inspire adventures, Darklords, and Domains of Dread of your own creation or to further detail the domains presented in 2. Mix and match elements from different genres to create your own uniquely terrifying combinations.



### Body Horror

![image](book/RHW/208-21-003.body-horror.webp)

Body horror examines the fear of our failing anatomies. Tales in this genre explore the unpredictability of flesh—that robust health might be an illusion and that we might be incubating what will devour us. Examples include Alien and The Fly.



#### Body Horror Principles

Consider the following principles when creating Darklords and domains with body horror themes:

- **Depth of Transformation** Physical transformations are common and might affect more than bodies. Objects, architecture, and the natural world might be also anthropomorphized.
- **Flesh Aberrations** Characters suffer aberrant or excessive growth, whether of organs, discordant appendages, or unnatural materials.
- **Gore Is a Byproduct** Though gore might take center stage in body horror stories, it's often a side effect of stories about fear of change, difference, mortality, physical harm, or disease.
- **Gore Isn't Required** Body horror doesn't need to be messy. Swapping bodies, turning to stone, or gaining one's ideal form might feature in this genre.
- **Real Disabilities Aren't Horrifying** Body horror has a history of portraying disability as monstrous. Avoid this trope.



#### Body Horror Villains

A physical transformation doesn't make someone a villain. Villains in body horror adventures cultivate evil in tandem with the aberrant transformations afflicting their form and surroundings.



#### Villain Identities

Villains of this genre are often tragic figures, whether they're cultists enduring forced metamorphosis or scientists trying to extend their lives. Choose from or roll on the Body Horror Villains table to inspire villains appropriate to this genre.

**Body Horror Villains**

| 1d10 | The Villain Is... |
|---|---|
| 1 | An abandoned homunculus made in the image of its creator's child. |
| 2 | A scientist who, hoping to keep their spouse alive, grafts their spouse to their own body. |
| 3 | A fungal mass that grows more intelligent with every sapient life it engulfs. |
| 4 | A guardian angel possessed by the vile blood of the demons it has slain. |
| 5 | A dying ruler obsessed with creating a new body so they can continue their reign. |
| 6 | A cancer possessed by the mind of a dead mage that seeks to regrow their body. |
| 7 | A monarch who feeds their cannibal children, no matter the cost. |
| 8 | The priests of a forgotten god, who try to raise their deity from the faithful's flesh. |
| 9 | A house that remembers its tenants and will do anything to regain them. |
| 10 | A grieving mortician who sculpts every face they encounter into that of their lost love. |



#### Villain Torments

Villains in this genre simultaneously draw power from and are tormented by supernatural and physiological aberrance. Choose from or roll on the Body Horror Torments table to determine what abhorrent affliction plagues the villain.

**Body Horror Torments**

| 1d10 | The Villain... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Possesses a bestial mouth in their torso. |
| 2 | Is pockmarked with eyes that never close. |
| 3 | Grows tooth-filled cysts on their limbs. |
| 4 | Is plagued by an ever-growing fungal mass sprouting from their extremities. |
| 5 | Restitches their body together. |
| 6 | Has parasites writhing beneath their skin. |
| 7 | Can dissolve their physical form at will. |
| 8 | Is gravid with bulbous egg sacs. |
| 9 | Aches with a ceaseless hunger. |
| 10 | Can't control their transformation into a beast and back. |



#### Body Horror Adventures

Adventures in body horror realms often become tests of endurance, whether characters are attempting to hold out until rescue arrives or endeavoring to mount a rescue themselves. Alternatively, adventures might have an investigative feel, requiring the heroes to uncover the dark secret that lies beneath the mundane.



#### Adventure Hooks

Body horror plots often explore the unpredictability of life and discordance between mind and body. Choose from or roll on the Body Horror Plots table to inspire your body horror adventures.

**Body Horror Plots**

| 1d10 | Adventure Plots |
|---|---|
| 1 | A malevolent curse is transforming the village's children into misshapen statues. |
| 2 | Guests of a popular local dinner party keep succumbing to autophagia. |
| 3 | Corpses of beasts—mutated and halfway human—are left at the forest's edge. |
| 4 | Every night, one townsperson melts. |
| 5 | Fiends have infiltrated a community by wearing the corpses of the deceased. |
| 6 | Fleshy catacombs open beneath a town. |
| 7 | A neighborhood is filled with derelict houses composed entirely of mimics. |
| 8 | The corpse of a monstrous leviathan has washed ashore, entrails still moving. |
| 9 | A virulent infestation uses the townsfolk as incubators for giant insects. |
| 10 | Something is stealing the tongues of the city guards. |



#### Adventure Settings

Body horror can occur anywhere, from mundane settings to unsettling locales. Choose from or roll on the Body Horror Settings table to inspire locations for your adventures.

**Body Horror Settings**

| 1d10 | The Adventure Takes Place In... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A vine-covered, ostensibly abandoned prison or asylum. |
| 2 | The cavernous gut of a dead behemoth. |
| 3 | A sprawling university, older than the town surrounding it. |
| 4 | A city of red muscle, with bleeding eyes embedded in hair-strangled buildings. |
| 5 | A forest of burnt pines draped in gore. |
| 6 | A derelict laboratory with old experiments floating in containment tubes. |
| 7 | A slaughterhouse, larger than it appears on the outside and full of victims. |
| 8 | A suddenly empty mortuary. |
| 9 | An old church sitting astride a warren of ancient tunnels. |
| 10 | A vibrant garden sprouting from a mound of putrid corpses. |



#### Body Horror Monsters

Any monster might become the focus of a body horror plot. Know what your players anticipate so you can distort those expectations. A poised elf revealed to be a husk puppeted by sapient worms can prove as frightening as any eldritch horror. The Body Horror Monsters table presents monsters particularly appropriate to such adventures. Unless otherwise noted, creatures in this table appear in the Monster Manual.

**Body Horror Monsters**

| CR | Creature |
|---|---|
| 1/8 | *Slaad Tadpole* |
| 1/2 | *Bodytaker Podling** |
| 1 | *Carrionette** |
| 2 | *Gibbering Mouther*, *Intellect Devourer* |
| 3 | *Carrion Stalker*,* *Doppelganger*, *Grell* |
| 4 | *Black Pudding*, *Strigoi** |
| 5 | *Flesh Golem*, *Red Slaad* |
| 6 | *Medusa*, *Zombie Clot** |
| 7 | *Blue Slaad*, *Bodytaker Plant*,* *Necrichor*,* *Violet Fungus Necrohulk* |
| 8 | *Chain Devil* |
| 10 | *Aboleth* |
| 15 | *Yithian** |
| 19 | *Lesser Star Spawn Emissary** |
| 21 | *Greater Star Spawn Emissary** |



### Cosmic Horror

![image](book/RHW/209-21-004.cosmic-horror.webp)

Cosmic horror revolves around the fear of personal insignificance. The genre, inspired by stories of the Cthulhu Mythos, is predicated on the idea of entities so vast and so genuinely beyond our comprehension that we can't fathom their simplest motivations. To see them is to become lost in their magnitude and the evidence that we have never and could never matter to the cosmos at large. Examples include Annihilation and Stalker.



#### Cosmic Horror Principles

Consider the following principles when creating Darklords and domains with cosmic horror themes:

- **Fear the Unknown** Be vague. Cosmic horror emerges through imagination and the indescribable, not through details.
- **Iconography** Cults, forbidden books, and strange symbols form the cornerstones of cosmic horror.
- **Inscrutable Forces** Cosmic horror is about alien forces driven by motivations humans can't understand. There is no good or evil, no law or chaos.
- **Marginalization Isn't Horror** The genre has a history of framing marginalized demographics as monstrous and stigmatizing mental illness. Avoid those tropes.
- **Remove the Familiar** Cosmic horror makes characters feel gradually unmoored from reality.



#### Cosmic Horror Villains

Despite the genre's grand magnitude, villains of cosmic horror are still often individual beings. Godlike terrors and inscrutable forces might pull the strings with their unknowable goals, but the antagonists the characters face are concrete, fallible people.



#### Villain Identities

Cosmic horror villains often perpetrate horrors as they strive for outcomes they can't articulate. Choose from or roll on the Cosmic Horror Villains table to inspire villains appropriate to this genre.

**Cosmic Horror Villains**

| 1d10 | The Villain Is... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A smiling minstrel whose music drives listeners to murder. |
| 2 | A priest obsessed with creating a shelter safe from the coming apocalypse. |
| 3 | A mayor who will do anything to ensure citizens finish a sacred transformation. |
| 4 | An astronomer broken and enraptured by what they saw in the stars. |
| 5 | A scientist striving to make their body the perfect host for an ageless being. |
| 6 | A coroner who believes the bodies they autopsy contain secret messages. |
| 7 | The head librarian of an ancient sect, who seeks secrets hidden within their peers. |
| 8 | A spoiled noble who intends to raise a cult to feed to residents of an alien dimension. |
| 9 | A researcher knowingly incubating a powerful entity within themself. |
| 10 | A hierophant seeking a doorway to an alien realm to bring about a new world. |



#### Villain Torments

Villains in this genre are endowed with unnatural powers stemming from their studies or granted by alien forces. Choose from or roll on the Cosmic Horror Torments table to determine what alien or psychological torment plagues the villain.

**Cosmic Horror Torments**

| 1d10 | The Villain... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Is haunted by otherworldly masters that whisper from reflective surfaces. |
| 2 | Sees multiple dimensions at once. |
| 3 | Is transforming into a long-extinct being. |
| 4 | Screams messages from the far-flung future. |
| 5 | Absorbs the words out of books. |
| 6 | Drains any object they focus on of all but one portentous color. |
| 7 | Finds their body warped to match that of the last person they talked with. |
| 8 | Incubates an alien symbiote in their brain. |
| 9 | Sleepwalks, drawing the same symbol on every surface they come across. |
| 10 | Obsesses over music, shifting their form to embody whatever song they hear. |



#### Cosmic Horror Adventures

Adventures in cosmic horror realms are bleak, desperate affairs, where the best one can hope for is to survive relatively intact. There is no stopping the ultimate evil, but characters might aspire to seal it away temporarily.



#### Adventure Hooks

Cosmic horror adventures often deal with how alien forces might alter us, perverting our expectations and separating us from what makes us human. Choose from or roll on the Cosmic Horror Plots table to inspire your cosmic horror adventures.

**Cosmic Horror Plots**

| 1d10 | Adventure Hook |
|---|---|
| 1 | A child has gone missing in the impossibly vast space beneath their bed. |
| 2 | Something drags a coastal town's inhabitants out in the night, garbs them in silver, and leads them to the surf to drown. |
| 3 | A wandering minstrel plays music that robs entire cities of sleep. |
| 4 | Local bakers have started making pies filled with a delicious, luminescent, alien, blue goo. |
| 5 | A sapient, unholy tome will do anything to reach a group of cultists. |
| 6 | The inheritors of an ancient sect are transforming into astral horrors. |
| 7 | Animals in the local forest have started going to a specific charred grove to die. |
| 8 | Colossal statues surrounding the city move only during dusk and dawn. |
| 9 | The characters must survive an evening in a sinking ancestral home. |
| 10 | A new wing in the academy's library has appeared, filled with blank books. |



#### Adventure Settings

Cosmic horror frequently takes place in settings that imply access to hidden knowledge or in unnatural, logic-defying dimensions far removed from reality. Choose from or roll on Cosmic Horror Settings table to inspire locations for your adventures.

**Cosmic Horror Settings**

| 1d10 | The Adventure Takes Place In... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A lavish manor devoid of people—save for staff who swear the lord is busy. |
| 2 | A narrow chapel in the woods, whose bell rings ceaselessly. |
| 3 | A hidden ward of a decrepit university. |
| 4 | A dimension of featureless white, broken up only by staring eyes. |
| 5 | The ninth basement beneath an otherwise normal family home. |
| 6 | A small inn in the mountains that smells perpetually of brine. |
| 7 | An ambulatory forest riddled with carvings of unblinking eyes. |
| 8 | A sewage system that predates its city. |
| 9 | A coastline slowly being consumed by an obsidian sea. |
| 10 | A decrepit lighthouse whose light flickers on at strange intervals. |



#### Cosmic Horror Monsters

Monsters in cosmic horror adventures are often strange beings that enact bizarre changes on their victims. The Cosmic Horror Monsters table presents monsters particularly appropriate to such adventures. Unless otherwise noted, creatures in this table appear in the Monster Manual.

**Cosmic Horror Monsters**

| CR | Creature |
|---|---|
| 1/4 | *Kuo-toa* |

### Dark Fantasy

![image](book/RHW/210-21-005.dark-fantasy.webp)

The dark fantasy genre features fantasy worlds where grim themes, nihilistic plots, or horrifying elements inform their stories. Any tale featuring both supernatural elements and horror themes might constitute dark fantasy, whether it's a fantasy story steeped in dread or an otherwise realistic world that features a supernatural terror. Examples include The Dark Tower and Pan's Labyrinth.



#### Dark Fantasy Principles

Consider the following principles when creating Darklords and domains with dark fantasy themes:

- **Evil Sometimes Triumphs** Good doesn't always win. Evil individuals with great power and unopposed schemes might prosper.
- **Low Magic** Magic and magic items might be rarer or require a bargain or sacrifice to use.
- **Morally Gray** The lines between good and evil are blurred. Choices involve deciding on the least bad outcome available.
- **Nefarious Deeds** Corruption and suspicion flourish among organizations and individuals.
- **Reluctant Heroes** Antiheroes are common—characters tainted by the world's evil or those who refuse to be considered heroes.



#### Dark Fantasy Villains

Sinister individuals leave their marks on dark fantasy domains, whether with oppressive architecture, unavoidable propaganda, or scars on an exploited environment.



#### Villain Identities

Villains occupy places of influence in dark fantasy domains. Choose from or roll on the Dark Fantasy Villains table to inspire villains appropriate to this genre.

**Dark Fantasy Villains**

| 1d10 | The Villain Is... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A machine that believes it's a resurrected tyrant and seeks to rebuild its empire. |
| 2 | The leader of a subterranean people who plots to blot out the sun's searing light. |
| 3 | A high priest intent on shifting an entire nation into their god's realm. |
| 4 | A desperate general who unleashes otherworldly war machines. |
| 5 | A massive treant who has allied with raiders and seeks to fell every forest. |
| 6 | A sage who solves an endless war by preventing anyone from dying. |
| 7 | An eternal royal whose immortality relies on the blood of angels. |
| 8 | A criminal kingpin who burns opponents into psychoactive spirit dust. |
| 9 | An ancient dragon whose godlike magic drains the domain of life. |
| 10 | A god who killed all their peers and now rules the mortal realm. |



#### Villain Torments

In dark fantasy adventures, a villain's power is often rooted in the villain's own suffering. Choose from or roll on the Dark Fantasy Torments table to determine how this power tragically works against the villain.

**Dark Fantasy Torments**

| 1d10 | The Villain... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Uncontrollably damages everything they care about. |
| 2 | Manufactures catastrophes to distract from their own ineptitude. |
| 3 | Is surrounded by power-hungry spies and saboteurs, fueling the villain's paranoia. |
| 4 | Seeks the pleasure of lost glories. |
| 5 | Is surrounded by sycophants whose constant praise makes every success feel hollow. |
| 6 | Is plagued by a cursed family legacy. |
| 7 | Is hounded by rivals and baseless mockery. |
| 8 | Must sacrifice those they love to maintain their facade of power. |
| 9 | Is praised by society for a deed they never truly accomplished. |
| 10 | Elicits excessive fear and reverence, resulting in their isolation. |



#### Dark Fantasy Adventures

Adventures in dark fantasy domains involve desperate or reluctant heroes resisting evil. Even in the grimmest settings, desperation and hope fan the flames of resistance.



#### Adventure Hooks

Plots in dark fantasy adventures range from street-level depravity to world-ruining conspiracies. Choose from or roll on the Dark Fantasy Plots table to inspire your dark fantasy adventures.

**Dark Fantasy Plots**

| 1d10 | Adventure Hook |
|---|---|
| 1 | A beholder-shaped statue has come to life and begun terrorizing the city. |
| 2 | A portal to a demonic realm has opened in the mouth of an innocent acolyte. |
| 3 | A sapient virus is turning the inhabitants of a village into shadows. |
| 4 | Giant spiders have declared war on all bipedal creatures. |
| 5 | A coven plans to use a volcano as a massive cauldron for a catastrophic spell. |
| 6 | The nation's beloved monarch was recently revealed to be a lich. |
| 7 | A malevolent phantom haunts the moon, raising corpses bathed in its light as undead. |
| 8 | A sentient weapon transforms its surroundings into a mockery of the war it last fought in. |
| 9 | A factory distills souls into a powerful wish-granting elixir. |
| 10 | An expanding labyrinth has just swallowed another neighborhood. |



#### Adventure Settings

Evil is entrenched in dark fantasy domains, reflected by their grandiose adventure locales. Choose from or roll on the Dark Fantasy Settings table to inspire locations for your adventures.

**Dark Fantasy Settings**

| 1d10 | The Adventure Takes Place In... |
|---|---|
| 1 | The floating and fallen ruins of a magical megastructure. |
| 2 | A blood-soaked swamp. |
| 3 | A tower that pierces a magical ley line, draining its power. |
| 4 | A criminal consortium's lavish academy. |
| 5 | A forest where every tree grows from the body of a mummified hero. |
| 6 | An empire covered in the watchful religious symbols of an all-seeing deity. |
| 7 | A fortress with seven locked gates that seal off the underworld. |
| 8 | A country devastated by the fallout of weapons used in an age-old war. |
| 9 | A town threatened by an unstoppable, slowly encroaching infection. |
| 10 | A city adrift on a sea full of primeval predators. |



#### Dark Fantasy Monsters

Any monster can find a place in a dark fantasy plot. D&D's most iconic threats—such as dragons and beholders—are particularly appropriate to horror-tinged tales, as are any other supernatural foes. The Dark Fantasy Monsters table presents monsters particularly appropriate to such adventures. Unless otherwise noted, creatures in this table appear in the Monster Manual.

|---|---|
