### Folk Horror

![image](book/RHW/211-21-006.folk-horror.webp)

Folk horror adventures involve traditions, beliefs, and perceptions that are passed down through generations and take terrifying twists. For those who ascribe to hidden traditions, sacrifices to strange gods or placations to lurking monsters are everyday events. For outsiders, though, these practices reveal the subjectivity of normalcy and societal truth. Examples include Midsommar and The Wicker Man.



#### Folk Horror Principles

Consider the following principles when creating Darklords and domains with folk horror themes:

- **Isolation Begets Weirdness** Strange and potentially dangerous traditions flourish in isolated or private communities.
- **Perversion of Community** Communities in folk horror stories often are a grim mirror of an aspect of accepted society. They often dramatically use outsiders or purge nonbelievers.
- **Relative Truth** Beliefs highlighted in folk horror stories might not be true.
- **Secret Traditions** Community members typically hide their beliefs, perhaps by physically obscuring them or manipulating others in power.
- **Strangeness in Specificity** Art, symbols, tools, celebrations, and other trappings of belief make a community's traditions more specific and eerie.



#### Folk Horror Villains

Antagonistic forces in folk horror usually are community leaders—paragons of the strange beliefs central to the horror's narrative. Outsiders might have a chance to adopt the community's ways, but otherwise locals consider them heretics or corrupting elements.



#### Villain Identities

Folk horror villains are manipulative, leading others to follow inscrutable traditions. Choose from or roll on the Folk Horror Villains table to inspire villains appropriate to this genre.

**Folk Horror Villains**

| 1d10 | The Villain Is... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A secluded temple's high priest who needs to find the perfect sacrifice. |
| 2 | An erinyes that appears when youngsters speak a rhyme into a darkened mirror. |
| 3 | A night hag that dwells in the dreams of those who drink a special ergot tea. |
| 4 | A shape-shifter that takes on the appearance of the last person it fed on. |
| 5 | A wicker giant that animates during the new moon, punishing the unwary. |
| 6 | A mayor who behaves in archaic ways so villagers don't enrage an ancient ghost. |
| 7 | A treant who demands corpses to replace trees cleared by a town's construction. |
| 8 | A mysterious robed figure who wears a horned mask and leads a silent cult. |
| 9 | A bloodthirsty forest guardian that resembles a deer with two heads. |
| 10 | A shadow that appears only when individuals look away from the woods' tree line. |



#### Villain Torments

Folk horror villains have been consumed by the traditions or land they embody, causing them to fail in their duties or their rites to spin out of control. Choose from or roll on the Folk Horror Torments to determine how these twisted traditions torment the villain.

**Folk Horror Torments**

| 1d10 | The Villain... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Knows the beliefs are false but keeps up the facade to maintain power. |
| 2 | Adheres to an ancient faith and desperately works to convert nonbelievers. |
| 3 | Seeks to transform their body into a vessel or gate for the subject of their belief. |
| 4 | Now appears as a bloodthirsty amalgamation of various forest creatures. |
| 5 | Uncontrollably utters prophecies. |
| 6 | Is haunted by judgmental ancestral spirits. |
| 7 | Can appear only at dawn and dusk. |
| 8 | Has partially melded into a hallowed tree. |
| 9 | Is being consumed by fungi. |
| 10 | Can no longer commune with their deity, driving them to ever bloodier sacrifices. |



#### Folk Horror Adventures

In folk horror tales, characters often discover that their beliefs aren't as universally held as they assumed—and provide no defense against those who reject those beliefs.



#### Adventure Hooks

Folk horror plots often involve outsiders to a group discovering unsettling practices or traditions. Choose from or roll on the Folk Horror Plots to inspire your folk horror adventures.

**Folk Horror Plots**

| 1d10 | Adventure Hook |
|---|---|
| 1 | Anyone entering the city on horseback is imprisoned and sentenced to death. |
| 2 | A cult requests help summoning a demonic force to combat a greater evil. |
| 3 | The townspeople protect a violent hag, whom they call "grandmother." |
| 4 | After an estate party, the residents adopt the characters, refusing to let them leave. |
| 5 | The characters bear an uncanny resemblance to the founders of a secret village. |
| 6 | Townsfolk disappear for days before reappearing with missing memories. |
| 7 | Strangers hand out wax earplugs to protect others from "the choir." |
| 8 | Every night, parents let their children follow floating lights into the forest. |
| 9 | Villagers physically can't stop smiling. |
| 10 | Anyone who stays in the village overnight loses their shadow to the looming woods. |



#### Adventure Settings

Folk horror stories often take place in isolated or rural areas, but they could be set anywhere insular communities thrive or traditions stagnate. Choose from or roll on the Folk Horror Settings to inspire locations for your adventures.

**Folk Horror Settings**

| 1d10 | The Adventure Takes Place In... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A copse of dense, blackened woods. |
| 2 | A mansion built around a stone circle. |
| 3 | A field where paths grow in corridor-like patterns leading to a ruin at the center. |
| 4 | A telepathic collective that townsfolk join by ingesting a rare fungus. |
| 5 | A hag's hut that stands atop a growing hill of rotten sweets. |
| 6 | A glacier that residents never leave. |
| 7 | A cavern where the glowing bones of an otherworldly being jut from the walls. |
| 8 | A countryside with stretches of hayfields and colorful barns. |
| 9 | Rival villages engaged in an age-old war. |
| 10 | A deserted chapel that has been burned down and rebuilt a thousand times. |



#### Folk Horror Monsters

Eerie traditions and unnatural alliances with monsters fill folk horror tales. When certain behaviors have taken hold over generations, even the strangest practices and most dangerous beings might be accepted as part of society. The Folk Horror Monsters table presents monsters particularly appropriate to such adventures. Unless otherwise noted, creatures in this table appear in the Monster Manual.

**Folk Horror Monsters**

| CR | Creature |
|---|---|
| 1/2 | *Myconid Adult*, *Vine Blight* |
| 1 | *Scarecrow* |
| 2 | *Awakened Tree* |
| 2 | *Cultist Fanatic*, *Will-o'-Wisp* |
| 3 | *Green Hag*, *Mist Horror*,* *Werewolf* |
| 4 | *Death's Head Tree** |
| 5 | *Shambling Mound* |
| 7 | *Tree Blight* |
| 8 | *Death Cultist*, *Fiend Cultist* |
| 9 | *Jiangshi** |
| 10 | *Cultist Hierophant*, *Dullahan** |
| 13 | *Loup Garou** |
| 16 | *Gulthias Blight* |
| 21 | *Arch-hag* |



### Ghost Stories

![image](book/RHW/212-21-007.ghost-stories.webp)

Ghost stories number among the more psychologically elaborate genres of horror. Only by revealing tales of tragedy and past wrongs can heroes bring peace to forces that share their suffering with the living. Examples include The Woman in Black and The Haunting of Hill House.



#### Ghost Story Principles

Consider the following principles when creating Darklords and domains inspired by ghost stories:

- **Mirror of Humanity** Ghosts are a way to examine the nature of the soul, mortality, and history.
- **Naive Heroes** Heroes are purehearted or unsuspecting individuals whose resolve is shaken by the story's events. Look for ways to test heroes' psychology with your hauntings.
- **Resolving a Haunt** Heroes need a way to put spirits to rest. Once you reveal the story, ensure the way to combat the haunting is clear.
- **Specificity** Even the smallest details can reveal a haunting's story. A simple locket or portrait might contain clues that explain a haunting.
- **Ties to the Living** Personal ties give ghost stories weight. Consider connecting the heroes to spirits in ways they won't predict, such as making a phantasmal villain a hero's ancestor.



#### Ghost Story Villains

In ghost stories, spirits often represent instruments of supernatural justice, causing those responsible for their deaths to suffer. Spirits also can represent grief and the need for closure.



#### Villain Identities

While the villains in ghost stories are often spirits or haunted places, they also could be the individuals who provoked a haunting to begin with. Choose from or roll on the Ghost Story Villains table to inspire villains appropriate to this genre.

**Ghost Story Villains**

| 1d10 | The Villain Is... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A medium who gains power over spirits by feeding victims to them. |
| 2 | The spirit of a long-dead murderer who continues to kill in death. |
| 3 | A ghostly ancestor who refuses to relinquish control of their kin. |
| 4 | A priest who marks the unworthy for sacrifice to the cathedral's hungry spirits |
| 5 | A phantom rider who sweeps through the village, stealing away the living. |
| 6 | An unbound spirit that repeatedly manifests in victims' nightmares. |
| 7 | The capricious phantasm of an amoral accident victim who torments the living. |
| 8 | The spirit of a former tyrant who demands sacrifices from their old domain. |
| 9 | A ghost hunter who inflicts hauntings on clients—then charges to remove the spirits. |
| 10 | The spirit of an evil captain who lurks near their wrecked vessel, sabotaging passing ships. |



#### Villain Torments

Whether they're living monsters or ghosts, villains in ghost stories are the architects of their own tragedies. Choose from or roll on the Ghost Story Torments table to determine how the villain's past painfully manifests.

**Ghost Story Torments**

| 1d10 | The Villain... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Can't touch anyone without stealing a precious memory. |
| 2 | Can temporarily release spirits from the villain's elaborate scars. |
| 3 | Is hounded by spirits that each represent an emotion the villain can no longer feel. |
| 4 | Drains the life from any animal they see. |
| 5 | Has lost the ability to feel physical sensation. |
| 6 | Can be seen only in reflective surfaces. |
| 7 | Is bound within a building; leaving would permanently destroy them. |
| 8 | Turns to ash in sunlight. |
| 9 | Can communicate only through music and writing. |
| 10 | Siphons the color from objects they possess. |



#### Ghost Story Adventures

Ghost story adventures deal with learning the story behind a haunting and ultimately resolving it. They benefit from preserving the mystery behind a spirit's motivations until the heroes discover the truth.



#### Adventure Hooks

Though the structure—learn about a haunting and resolve it—might seem straightforward, ghost story plots can explore philosophical issues like the burden of ancestry and the nature of the soul. Choose from or roll on the Ghost Story Plots table to inspire your ghost stories.

**Ghost Story Plots**

| 1d10 | Adventure Hook |
|---|---|
| 1 | Murder victims linger as ghosts until someone solves their murders. |
| 2 | Bloody graffiti keeps appearing on the city's walls. |
| 3 | A stubborn miser must visit their haunted family home to put their family to rest. |
| 4 | A mob of angry spirits besieges the local temple on the winter solstice each year. |
| 5 | The adventurers must solve the murder of a ghost who can say only three words. |
| 6 | A ship—with the same name as a vessel lost at sea decades prior—arrives at port. |
| 7 | Rumors abound of a ritual allowing a living individual to trade places with the dead. |
| 8 | The ghosts of an actor's rivals haunt the local theater. |
| 9 | A noble accidentally broke a family urn, unleashing their cruel ancestral spirits. |
| 10 | Every full moon, spirits in a graveyard rise to seek vengeance for a mass crime. |



#### Adventure Settings

Ghost stories are intensely personal, and adventures within this genre take place in a setting dripping with tragic history. Choose from or roll on the Ghost Story Settings table to inspire locations for your adventures.

**Ghost Story Settings**

| 1d10 | The Adventure Takes Place In... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A decrepit mansion where, for years, nobles killed the staff to keep their secrets. |
| 2 | A graveyard city-state where all living residents are grave keepers. |
| 3 | An opulent yet abandoned library, filled with haunted artifacts. |
| 4 | The site of an ancient battle that permanently devastated the land. |
| 5 | A nation where the residents observe grueling rituals to appease the angry dead. |
| 6 | An expansive forest in which a cruel noble once hunted the poor for sport. |
| 7 | A ruined barn where dozens of remarkable animals lost their lives in a fire. |
| 8 | A picturesque cliff where visiting couples often mysteriously fall to their deaths. |
| 9 | An attic in which a hateful spirit has been sealed for decades. |
| 10 | A dilapidated lighthouse overlooking a black-sand beach. |



#### Ghost Story Monsters

Creatures that embody or serve as a response to past tragedies often feature in ghost stories. Don't limit yourself to incorporeal Undead when creating your own hauntings. The Ghost Story Monsters table presents monsters particularly appropriate to such adventures. Unless otherwise noted, creatures in this table appear in the Monster Manual.

**Ghost Story Monsters**

| CR | Creature |
|---|---|
| 1/2 | *Death's Head*,* *Shadow* |
| 1 | *Animated Armor*, *Death Dog*, *Specter* |
| 2 | *Animated Rug of Smothering*, *Poltergeist* |

### Gothic Horror

![image](book/RHW/213-21-008.gothic-horror.webp)

Gothic horror deals with the terror within. It shatters the illusion of humanity by holding a mirror up to us and forcing us to examine what we truly are and what we pretend to be. In gothic horror, we—not some distant entity—are the architects of our destruction. Examples include Dracula and Frankenstein.



#### Gothic Horror Principles

Consider the following principles when creating Darklords and domains with gothic horror themes:

- **Brave Heroes** Gothic heroes are often virtuous, deeply passionate, or courageous. Adventures should test characters' beliefs and morality.
- **Foreboding** Atmosphere and a sense of dread are key. Locations are often decrepit or foreboding.
- **High Emotions** Gothic stories include intense, exaggerated emotions. Romances, rivalries, and life-changing events are common.
- **Sacrifice** Sacrifices feature prominently in gothic stories. Give characters heart-wrenching choices.
- **Unassuming, Unrepentant Villains** Gothic villains are unrepentantly evil, but this shouldn't be immediately obvious. Drop hints about your villain's awful secrets before revealing them fully.



#### Gothic Horror Villains

Though thoroughly wicked, villains in gothic horror tales act reserved or unassuming until they reveal their true nature. Any intriguing figure with a dark secret can serve as a gothic horror villain.



#### Villain Identities

Gothic villains are most effective when they are slowly revealed as shockingly cruel, immoral, or the antithesis of good. Choose from or roll on the Gothic Horror Villains table to inspire villains appropriate to this genre.

**Gothic Horror Villains**

| 1d10 | The Villain Is... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A reclusive noble who uses their vampiric reputation to terrorize their vassals. |
| 2 | A vain socialite who made a bargain with a fell power to retain their youth. |
| 3 | A scientist obsessed with creating the perfect poison, machine, or life-form. |
| 4 | A beloved magnate who abducts commoners to use in beauty rituals. |
| 5 | A celebrity who murders openly but uses their charm to avoid repercussions. |
| 6 | Someone who loves a monstrous creature and does anything to keep it safe. |
| 7 | A wealthy heir who manipulates the ambitious into committing terrible deeds. |
| 8 | A poisoner who seeks to manipulate history through targeted killings. |
| 9 | An artist who concocts terrible accidents to inspire their art. |
| 10 | A monster hunter who accuses those they consider sinful of being monsters. |



#### Villain Torments

Self-debasement and self-loathing lurk at the heart of gothic villains' evil, whether they indulge in vices or are consumed with misanthropy. Choose from or roll on the Gothic Horror Torments table to determine how temptation and dramatic emotions torment the villain.

**Gothic Horror Torments**

| 1d10 | The Villain... |
|---|---|
| 1 | Inherited unlimited wealth, but all finery they wear turns into ash. |
| 2 | Endlessly cries tears of blood. |
| 3 | Is covered in tattoos, which magically update to illustrate all their sins. |
| 4 | Turns into a lead statue when the sun rises. |
| 5 | Is incomparably beautiful, but locals perceive them as a beast. |
| 6 | Sees evidence of their impending doom everywhere. |
| 7 | Extinguishes any light shone on them. |
| 8 | Can't taste food. |
| 9 | Curses anyone they dance with. |
| 10 | Craves company but is cursed to forever wear a mask and obscure their identity. |



#### Gothic Horror Adventures

The themes of gothic horror adventures center around shattering the lies we trick ourselves into believing. Ominous history, poetic tragedy, and supernatural forces are staples of gothic horror.



#### Adventure Hooks

The dichotomy between goodness and evil, reckonings for wicked deeds, and dire choices are strong themes in gothic horror plots. Choose from or roll on the Gothic Horror Plots table to inspire your gothic horror adventures.

**Gothic Horror Plots**

| 1d10 | Adventure Hook |
|---|---|
| 1 | The city's rulers secretly are warring hags, wererats, and vampires. |
| 2 | A scientist, never seen and known only through their writing, has disappeared. |
| 3 | A repentant immortal requests help in losing centuries of painful memories. |
| 4 | A beloved social figure turns into a murderous living doll every night. |
| 5 | A pair of spirits brings unspeakable tragedy to any romantic couple in town. |
| 6 | A generational curse forces villagers to sacrifice themselves. |
| 7 | Every night, one random guest of an opulent inn chokes on their own blood. |
| 8 | A serial killer impales victims on a certain monument in a cruel mockery of art. |
| 9 | Terrible noises sound from a dilapidated mansion; those who visit are never seen again. |
| 10 | As the result of abhorrent experiments, blood-drained creatures roam the streets. |



#### Adventure Settings

Gothic horror settings have an underlying sinister air, and encounters often take place in forlorn structures where depravity runs rampant. Choose from or roll on the Gothic Horror Settings table to inspire locations for your adventures.

**Gothic Horror Settings**

| 1d10 | The Adventure Takes Place In... |
|---|---|
| 1 | A lavish garden that siphons life from visitors to maintain its beauty. |
| 2 | A ruined cathedral devoted to transforming a prophesied being. |
| 3 | A laboratory where preserved body parts carry the minds of their former owners. |
| 4 | A forest of eternal night where bloodthirsty creatures live in fragile peace. |
| 5 | A rectory where the stained glass windows hold the trapped souls of the pious. |
| 6 | A city where all who die are cast in plaster and used to adorn the streets. |
| 7 | An island where the inhabitants make sacrifices to avoid eerie transformations. |
| 8 | An artist's paradise where cruelties are elevated to terrible and beautiful art forms. |
| 9 | A castle in which visitors are transformed into objects or animals. |
| 10 | A ruined fortress haunted by a monstrous yet docile creature. |



#### Gothic Horror Monsters

Creatures imbued with tragedy or abominable origins work well in gothic horror adventures. The Gothic Horror Monsters table presents monsters particularly appropriate to such adventures. Unless otherwise noted, creatures in this table appear in the Monster Manual.

**Gothic Horror Monsters**

| CR | Creature |
|---|---|

### Disaster Horror

![image](book/RHW/214-21-009.disaster-horror.webp)

In disaster horror, the world has fallen to ruin or it's getting there fast. The unthinkable has happened, and society is collapsing. In these tales, you might replace a monster or villain with cascading catastrophes like those brought about by a meteorite strike or volcanic eruption. Regardless of a hero's power, the best-timed strike or the most powerful spell might not fix a city ruined by an earthquake or a world ravaged by plagues.



#### Disaster Horror Features

Consider the following principles when creating adventures with disaster horror themes:

- **Nature of Disaster** The disasters in your horror adventures need not be natural. Magical disruptions, temporal shifts, and violent interplanar rifts might sow supernatural chaos. Wars and relentless monster hordes—including legions of zombies or demons—also can cause domain-changing ruin.
- **Society's Downfall** In disaster horror, society breaks down. Inns are closed, healers are few or overtaxed, and anarchy rises as governments crumble.
- **What It Takes to Survive** Scared innocents, opportunistic scavengers, and leaderless institutions (military or otherwise) seek to survive. The hopeless acts of others might prove more horrifying than the disaster.



### Occult Detective Stories

![image](book/RHW/215-21-010.occult-detective-stories.webp)

Occult detective stories straddle the line between fantasy, mystery, and horror. For the occult detective, solving paranormal mysteries is part of the job. In these adventures, supernatural criminals or monsters pursue nefarious ends while the characters act as detectives: interpreting events, seeking patterns, deducing goals, and ultimately putting an end to the threat. Investigation and cleverness take center stage in these adventures, although—as in the noir stories that inspire the genre—there's plenty of room for action.



#### Occult Detective Story Features

Consider the following principles when creating adventures with occult detective themes:

- **Lighter Frights** Occult detective adventures can be just as terrifying as other horror adventures but might be lighter in tone. Adventurers might encounter the results of horrific deeds rather than experiencing them firsthand and might face a foe only once they're prepared.
- **Supernatural Twists** Consider how monsters, magic, or other supernatural forces might lend a thrilling twist to criminal enterprises. How will the characters catch an invisible assassin or a thief who pilfers extradimensional spaces?
- **Threading Hints** Once you know the villain's mode of operation, consider how the villain might give themself away. Even if you're not sure, listen to the characters' plans and give them opportunities to feel brilliant in the course of their investigations.



### Psychological Horror

![image](book/RHW/216-21-011.psychological-horror.webp)

Psychological horror stories create suspense by heightening or calling into question characters' states of mind, emotions, and perceptions. These tales often highlight the difference between what characters think and how they behave.



#### Psychological Horror Features

Consider the following principles when creating adventures with psychological horror themes:

- **Fears as Metaphors** Common anxieties and fears can become metaphors for antagonists in psychological horror. Fear of judgment by one's peers might manifest as a jury of nothics, while fear of change could be represented by a medusa that petrifies those who threaten the status quo.
- **Mental Illness Isn't Horror** Some classic psychological horror tales stigmatize mental illness. Avoid this trope in your adventures.
- **Unreliable Information** Uncertainty and paranoia shape psychological horror stories. Characters might experience a deadly encounter only to wake up at the end, not having realized they were asleep. Before undermining characters' senses, identify what's driving these skewed perceptions and how characters might overcome them.



### Slasher Horror

![image](book/RHW/217-21-012.slasher-horror.webp)

Slasher horror contends with relentless killers, which might be people or monsters. These adventures revel in grisly details, the suspense of an impending showdown with a powerful foe, and the fear that death waits right around the corner.



#### Slasher Horror Features

Consider the following principles when creating adventures with slasher horror themes:

- **Solo Antagonist** Slasher horror stories typically include one major antagonist that threatens a group. This might be a particularly large or cunning beast, a murderer who terrorizes a neighborhood, a monster stalking a town, or a supernatural menace that spreads a signature cause of death.
- **Targets** Consider who the villain's targets are and why the villain is preying on that group. Is it out of hunger or for revenge, or does the creature have a deep-seated need to kill?
- **Violence and Infamy** Antagonists in slasher horror are often infamous, akin to urban legends, with numerous victims. Consider how the killer avoids capture and what makes the killer's actions warrant their infamy.




# Chapter 5: Denizens of the Mists

![A grim dullahan strikes down its victim, claiming another grisly death's head as a follower](book/RHW/218-22-001.grim-dullahan.webp)

Terrors haunt the Mists. This chapter begins with advice to help you, the DM, use monsters to create frightful encounters. Following this is a collection of horrifying monsters and stalwart monster hunters for your adventures in the Domains of Dread.



## Horror Monsters

Cultivating mystery and menace around the monstrous foes in your adventures can be a simple matter. Here are techniques you can use to transform any monster into a horror to haunt characters' nightmares.



### Monstrous Origins

Unique monsters are singularly terrifying. Consider presenting the monster central to your adventures as a one-of-a-kind terror. Such a creature might be a fluke of nature, the product of insidious magic, a purposefully terrifying creation of the Dark Powers, or a being with an even more unsettling background. Use the tips for creating Darklords and drawing inspiration from different genres of horror in x to create unique origins for the most important threats in your adventures.

Different origin stories suggest diverse paths for adventurers to follow when investigating these creatures, learning their weaknesses, and ensuring nothing like them ever menaces again.



### Terrifying Language

Describe monsters in vivid ways. A terror chasing characters could just "follow" them, but instead it might "wriggle," "surge," or "galumph" after them. Descriptive language underscores how a creature behaves and conjures a visceral description of the monster. Unexpected descriptions can emphasize a creature's bizarre nature and unsettle the players. For example, it's one thing to say a snake "slithers," but another to say a sinister shadow or cruel witch does.

Use unsettling descriptions and similes. For example, a vine blight's constricting vines might resemble "noose-like cords" or "oily digits." Try less literal descriptions—even nonsensical ones. For example, a flesh golem might howl like "an earthquake in a mortuary" or "a charnel pit that's learned to sob."



### Notorious Monsters

Treat creatures central to your horror adventures as infamous threats. The more you foreshadow their menace or reveal that they have threatened others before, the larger such creatures loom. Build dread by giving monsters reputations that suggest the monsters' form, deeds, or peculiarities while letting players' imaginations embellish details.

For example, tales might describe a skeletal horror that whistles cheerfully while committing brutal acts. Characters might hear rumors of the Whistling Fiend's melodies becoming haunting earworms for survivors of the fiend's attacks. A party seeking the monster might hear it whistling in the Mists long before they confront it. All that time, characters can speculate about their enemy's nature, but ultimately the Whistling Fiend might be any threat you choose.



### Mysterious Monsters

Use conflicting descriptions and strange behaviors to cultivate mystery around your monster. The less characters know about a creature, the more they'll speculate about terrifying possibilities.

You can develop uncertainty about a creature even after it appears. Keep players guessing about an adventure's threat by referring to a monster by a flavorful description rather than the name of its stat block. A "zombie" doesn't sound like much of a threat, but a "stumbling mass of fetid skin and shattered bones" might be something else entirely.



### Weird Traits

By adding unexpected traits to monster stat blocks, you can undermine players' expectations of what a monster is and what it can do. Consider how you can use the Creature Traits list in the "Creating a Creature" section of the Dungeon Master's Guide to give familiar monsters horrifying twists.



### Putting It All Together

Combine the techniques in this section to create a unique terror. If you have ideas about what you want your monster to do, write them down. Then develop stories that connect those pieces or reinforce the type of horror you want to create.

![A zombie beholder's terror is transformed when the monster is recast as a flesh-stitched horror](book/RHW/219-22-002.zombie-beholder.webp)

For example, perhaps you've got an idea for an arrogant mage who sought to prove he didn't need his adventuring companions' protection by constructing a suit of living armor. Considering the bizarre, magical whims of such a character, you choose a *Zombie Beholder* as the foundation for the mage's animate armor. To reinforce its nature as a magical creation, you change the monster's creature type from Undead to Construct and describe it as being made of stitched-together animal parts. Then you give it the Berserk and Magic Resistance traits of a *Flesh Golem*. The characters' surprise at unexpectedly facing a beholder might be startling enough, but you add to your story that the mage has become trapped within his living armor as it hunts his former companions. Only by defeating the horror might the characters free what remains of the mage within, represented by the Emissary of Juiblex creature trait from the "Creating a Creature" section of the Dungeon Master's Guide.

### Bodytaker Plants


##### Bodytaker Plants

*statblock*

![A new bodytaker podling emerges from a bodytaker plant](book/RHW/221-22-004.bodytaker-podling-and-plant.webp)


##### Bodytaker Podling

*S,M • plant • N E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 16 | 11 | 14 | 10 | 10 | 10 |

**Skills** 

**Senses** Blindsight 30 ft.

**Languages** Deep Speech plus one other language

**Challenge** 1/2

**Traits**

**Semblance of Life.** The podling is a physical copy of a creature digested by a Bodytaker Plant. The podling has *Advantage* on Charisma (*Deception*) checks made to pass as the digested creature. The podling melts into a slurry when it dies.

**Actions**

**Slam.** m 5, reach 5 ft. {@h}6 (1d6 + 3) Bludgeoning damage.


##### Bodytaker Plant

*H • plant • N E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 18 | 8 | 20 | 14 | 14 | 18 |

**Senses** Blindsight 120 ft.

**Languages** telepathy 120 ft.

**Challenge** 7

**Traits**

**Podling Link.** The plant can see through and communicate telepathically with any of its podlings within 10 miles of it. When the plant dies, its podlings also die.

**Rejuvenation.** If the plant dies, it revives with all its *Hit Points* in 1d10 days. This trait doesn't function if the plant is reduced to 0 *Hit Points* by Poison damage or its remains are sprinkled with salt.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The plant makes three Vine attacks. It can replace one attack with a use of Entrapping Pod.

**Vine.** m 7, reach 20 ft. {@h}17 (3d8 + 4) Slashing damage. If the target is a Large or smaller creature, it has the *Grappled* condition (escape 14) from one of four vines.

**Entrapping Pod.** str 15, one Large or smaller creature the plant is grappling. {@actSaveFail} The target is pulled into the plant's space, is no longer *Grappled*, and is trapped in the plant's pod. While trapped, the target has the *Blinded* and *Paralyzed* conditions, and it has *Total Cover* against attacks and other effects outside the pod. After 2d4 hours, the trapped target dies, and if it was a Humanoid, a Bodytaker Podling resembling it emerges from the pod. A creature outside the pod and within 5 feet of the plant can take an action to make a 14 Strength (*Athletics*) check. On a successful check, the target is removed from the pod, falls in a space within 5 feet of the plant, and has the *Prone* condition. If the plant dies, the trapped target is no longer *Blinded* or *Paralyzed* and can escape from the pod using 5 feet of movement, exiting *Prone*.

**Reactions**

**Transfer Harm.** {@actTrigger} An attack roll hits the plant while a podling is within 5 feet of the plant. {@actResponse} The plant halves the damage it takes from that attack, and the podling takes the other half of the damage.



### Boneless


##### Boneless

*M • undead • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 15 | 14 | 12 | 1 | 10 | 1 |

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Languages** understands Common but can't speak

**Challenge** 1

**Traits**

**Abduct.** The boneless needn't spend extra movement to move a creature it is grappling.

**Compression.** The boneless can move through a space as narrow as 1 inch without expending extra movement to do so.

**Actions**

**Smother.** m 4, reach 5 ft. {@h}7 (2d4 + 2) Bludgeoning damage. If the target is a Medium or smaller creature, it has the *Grappled* condition (escape 12). Until the grapple ends, the target has the *Blinded* and *Restrained* conditions, is suffocating, and takes 7 (2d4 + 2) Bludgeoning damage at the start of each of the boneless's turns. The boneless can smother only one creature at a time. While grappling a target, the boneless can't take this action again.

**Bonus Actions**

**Unraveling Flesh (1/Day).** wis 11, each creature within 30 feet that can see the boneless. {@actSaveFail} The target has the *Frightened* condition. {@actSaveSuccessOrFail} The boneless moves up to its *Speed* without provoking *Opportunity Attacks*.

### Brain in a Jar


##### Brain in a Jar

*S • undead • L E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | 3 | 15 | 19 | 10 | 15 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Senses** Blindsight 120 ft.

**Languages** telepathy 60 ft. understands Common plus three other languages but can't speak; telepathy 60 ft.

**Challenge** 3

**Traits**

**Detect Intelligence.** The brain magically senses the location of any creature within 300 feet of itself that has an Intelligence score of 3 or higher, regardless of interposing barriers.

**Magic Resistance.** The brain has *Advantage* on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The brain makes two Disrupting Burst attacks.

**Disrupting Burst.** m,r 6, reach 5 ft. or range 120 ft. {@h}11 (2d6 + 4) Psychic damage. The target can't take Reactions until the end of its next turn, and it has *Disadvantage* on saving throws to maintain *Concentration* until the end of its next turn.

**Mind Blast 5.** int 14, each creature in a 60-foot *Cone*. {@actSaveFail} 14 (4d6) Psychic damage, and the target has the *Incapacitated* condition until the end of the brain's next turn. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage only.

### Carrion Stalker


##### Carrion Stalker

*T • aberration • U • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 6 | 17 | 16 | 2 | 13 | 6 |

**Senses** Tremorsense 60 ft.

**Challenge** 3

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The carrion stalker makes two Tentacle attacks and one Stinger attack.

**Tentacle.** m 5, reach 5 ft. {@h}8 (2d4 + 3) Piercing damage, and the carrion stalker attaches to the target. While attached, the carrion stalker can't make Tentacle attacks against other targets. The carrion stalker can detach itself by spending 5 feet of movement. The target or a creature within 5 feet of it can detach the carrion stalker as an action.

**Stinger.** m 5 (with *Advantage* if the carrion stalker is attached to the target), reach 5 ft. {@h}7 (2d6) Poison damage, and the target is subjected to the following effect. con 13. {@actSaveFail} The target has the *Poisoned* condition. While *Poisoned* in this way, the target is infested with a carrion stalker larva. If the target is still *Poisoned* in this way after 24 hours, the effect ends as the larva becomes a fully grown Carrion Stalker, which bursts from the target's chest and kills it.

### Carrionette


##### Carrionette

*T • construct • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 8 | 15 | 12 | 8 | 14 | 14 |

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Languages** Common plus one other language

**Challenge** 1

**Actions**

**Silver Needle.** m 4, reach 5 ft. {@h}1 Piercing damage plus 3 (1d6) Necrotic damage. If the target is a Humanoid not cursed by a carrionette, it is subjected to the following effect. cha 11. {@actSaveFail} The target is cursed for 1 minute. Until the curse ends, the target has the *Poisoned* condition, and its *Speed* is reduced by 10 feet.

**Soul Swap 5.** cha 11, one Humanoid the carrionette can see within 15 feet that is cursed by its Silver Needle. {@actSaveFail} The carrionette possesses the target's body, and the target possesses the carrionette's body and has the *Unconscious* condition for 1 hour. While possessing another body, the carrionette and target retain their alignments; personalities; Intelligence, Wisdom, and Charisma scores; and languages known. They otherwise adopt the other creature's game statistics, though the target can't use this Soul Swap action. The possession is undone if the target (while in the carrionette's body) deals damage to the carrionette (in the target's original body) with its Silver Needle. If either body is destroyed, both the carrionette and the target die.

**Bonus Actions**

**Head Fruits.** Each Undead ally in the tree's space can immediately take a *Reaction* to gain 5 *Temporary Hit Points*.



### Dullahan


##### Dullahan

*M • undead • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 18 | 14 | 16 | 11 | 15 | 16 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Skills** 

**Senses** Truesight 120 ft.

**Languages** understands Common plus one other language but can't speak

**Challenge** 10

**Traits**

**Mounted Adept.** While mounted and without the *Incapacitated* condition, the dullahan and its mount have *Advantage* on Dexterity saving throws, and the dullahan can force an attack targeted at its mount to target the dullahan instead.

**Terrorizer.** The dullahan has *Advantage* on attack rolls against targets that have the *Frightened* condition.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The dullahan makes two attacks, using Beheading Blade or Fiery Skull in any combination, and uses Headless Wail.

**Beheading Blade.** m 8, reach 5 ft. {@h}9 (1d10 + 4) Slashing damage plus 11 (2d10) Necrotic damage. If the target is reduced to 0 *Hit Points* by this attack, it dies and its head is lopped off. The head rises as a Death's Head in the space of the target's corpse or in the nearest unoccupied space. The head is under the dullahan's control. The dullahan can control no more than seven heads at a time.

**Fiery Skull.** r 7, range 120 ft. {@h}18 (4d8) Fire damage.

**Headless Wail.** con 15, up to three creatures within 120 feet of the dullahan that aren't Constructs or Undead. {@actSaveFail} 13 (2d12) Psychic damage, and the target has the *Frightened* condition until the start of the dullahan's next turn. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage only.

**Fiery Bolt.** r 7, range 120 ft. {@h}19 (3d10 + 3) Fire damage.

**Bonus Actions**

**Bolster Allies.** Ez chooses up to six allies within 60 feet. Each target that can hear her has Ez's choice of (A) *Advantage* on the next attack roll it makes before the end of its next turn or (B) *Resistance* to Acid, Necrotic, and Poison damage until the end of its next turn.

**Curse of the All-Seeing Eye (1/Day).** Ez chooses a damage type. wis 15, one target within 30 feet that Ez can see. {@actSaveFail} The target is cursed. Until the curse ends, the target has *Vulnerability* to the chosen damage type. The curse ends early if Ez uses this action again. If the target drops to 0 *Hit Points* before the curse ends, Ez can take a *Bonus Action* on a later turn to curse a new creature.

**Inspiring Rally.** Ez chooses up to six allies within 60 feet. Each target that can hear her can take a *Reaction* to move up to its *Speed* without provoking *Opportunity Attacks*.

### Gug


##### Gug

*H • aberration • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 22 | 15 | 23 | 7 | 16 | 11 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** understands Deep Speech but can't speak

**Challenge** 12

**Traits**

**Pack Tactics.** The gug has *Advantage* on an attack roll against a creature if at least one of the gug's allies is within 5 feet of the creature and the ally doesn't have the *Incapacitated* condition.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The gug makes two Claw attacks and uses Chew.

**Claw.** m 10, reach 10 ft. {@h}22 (3d10 + 6) Slashing damage. If the target is a Medium or smaller creature, it has the *Grappled* condition (escape 16) from one of two claws.

**Chew.** dex 18, up to two Medium or smaller creatures *Grappled* by the gug. {@actSaveFail} The gug places the target in its mouth and chews. A chewed creature is no longer *Grappled* but has the *Restrained* condition. While *Restrained* in this way, a target has *Half Cover* against attacks and other effects not originating from the gug and takes 10 (3d6) Piercing damage at the start of each of the gug's turns. A gug can have a maximum of four creatures in its mouth at a time. A creature in the gug's mouth can take an action to make a 16 Strength (*Athletics*) check. On a successful check, the target is no longer *Restrained* and moves to an unoccupied space within 5 feet of the gug. If the gug dies, a target is no longer *Restrained* and can escape from the gug using 5 feet of movement, exiting with the *Prone* condition.

![image](book/RHW/233-22-016.gug.webp)


##### Gug

*H • aberration • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 22 | 15 | 23 | 7 | 16 | 11 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** understands Deep Speech but can't speak

**Challenge** 12

**Traits**

**Pack Tactics.** The gug has *Advantage* on an attack roll against a creature if at least one of the gug's allies is within 5 feet of the creature and the ally doesn't have the *Incapacitated* condition.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The gug makes two Claw attacks and uses Chew.

**Claw.** m 10, reach 10 ft. {@h}22 (3d10 + 6) Slashing damage. If the target is a Medium or smaller creature, it has the *Grappled* condition (escape 16) from one of two claws.

**Chew.** dex 18, up to two Medium or smaller creatures *Grappled* by the gug. {@actSaveFail} The gug places the target in its mouth and chews. A chewed creature is no longer *Grappled* but has the *Restrained* condition. While *Restrained* in this way, a target has *Half Cover* against attacks and other effects not originating from the gug and takes 10 (3d6) Piercing damage at the start of each of the gug's turns. A gug can have a maximum of four creatures in its mouth at a time. A creature in the gug's mouth can take an action to make a 16 Strength (*Athletics*) check. On a successful check, the target is no longer *Restrained* and moves to an unoccupied space within 5 feet of the gug. If the gug dies, a target is no longer *Restrained* and can escape from the gug using 5 feet of movement, exiting with the *Prone* condition.



### Jiangshi


##### Jiangshi

*M • undead • L E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 18 | 3 | 18 | 17 | 14 | 12 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** Common plus three other languages

**Challenge** 9

**Traits**

**Jiangshi Weaknesses.** The jiangshi has these weaknesses: If the jiangshi sees its reflection, it immediately takes its *Reaction*, if available, to move as far from the reflection as possible., While the jiangshi is wearing or touching a *Holy Symbol*, it loses its *Immunity* to the *Frightened* condition and automatically fails saving throws to avoid or end the *Frightened* condition.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The jiangshi makes three Slam attacks and uses Consume Energy.

**Slam.** m 8, reach 5 ft. {@h}13 (2d8 + 4) Bludgeoning damage.

**Consume Energy.** con 16, one creature the jiangshi can see within 30 feet. {@actSaveFail} 18 (4d8) Necrotic damage. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage. {@actSaveSuccessOrFail} The jiangshi regains *Hit Points* equal to the Necrotic damage taken, the jiangshi's *Fly Speed* increases to 20 feet until the end of its next turn, and it can take its Hungering Stride *Bonus Action*. A Humanoid reduced to 0 *Hit Points* by this damage rises at the end of the jiangshi's turn as a Wight under the jiangshi's control. If this wight kills a Humanoid with its Life Drain action, the wight transforms into an independent Jiangshi 5 days later.

**Bonus Actions**

**Hungering Stride (Requires Consume Energy).** The jiangshi takes the *Dash* action.

**Shape-Shift.** The jiangshi shape-shifts into a Medium or Small Beast, Humanoid, or Undead creature, or it returns to its true form. Its game statistics, other than its size, are the same in each form. Any equipment it is wearing or carrying isn't transformed.

### Loup Garou


##### Loup Garou

*S,M • monstrosity • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 24 | 18 | 21 | 14 | 16 | 16 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** Common (can't speak in dire wolf form)

**Challenge** 13

**Traits**

**Legendary Resistance (3/Day).** If the loup garou fails a saving throw, it can choose to succeed instead.

**Legendary Actions**

**Mauling Charge.** The loup garou moves up to half its *Speed* without provoking *Opportunity Attacks* and makes one Longsword or Rend attack.

**Surprise Bite.** The loup garou uses Shape-Shift, turning into its hybrid or dire wolf form, then makes one Bite attack. The loup garou can't take this action again until the start of its next turn.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The loup garou makes two attacks, using Longsword or Rend in any combination. It can replace one attack with a Bite attack.

**Bite (Dire Wolf or Hybrid Form Only).** m 12, reach 5 ft. {@h}16 (2d8 + 7) Piercing damage plus 14 (4d6) Necrotic damage. If the target is a Humanoid, it is subjected to the following effect. con 18. {@actSaveFail} The target is cursed. If the cursed target drops to 0 *Hit Points*, it instead becomes a Werewolf under the DM's control and has 10 *Hit Points*. The curse can't be removed until this loup garou dies. {@actSaveSuccess} The target is immune to this loup garou's curse for 24 hours.

**Longsword (Humanoid or Hybrid Form Only).** m 12, reach 5 ft. {@h}18 (2d10 + 7) Slashing damage plus 3 (1d6) Necrotic damage.

**Rend (Dire Wolf or Hybrid Form Only).** m 12, reach 5 ft. {@h}16 (2d8 + 7) Slashing damage. If the target is a Medium or smaller creature, it has the *Prone* condition.

**Bonus Actions**

**Shape-Shift.** The loup garou shape-shifts into a Large dire wolf-humanoid hybrid or a Large dire wolf, or it returns to its true humanoid form. Its game statistics, other than its size, are the same in each form. Any equipment it is wearing or carrying isn't transformed.

##### Mi-Go

*M • aberration • N E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 20 | 15 | 16 | 21 | 15 | 12 |

**Saving Throws**

**Languages** all; telepathy 120 ft.

**Challenge** 9

**Traits**

**Magic Resistance.** The mi-go has *Advantage* on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.

**Silver Canister.** The mi-go has a silver canister. While holding or carrying the canister, the mi-go can use its Extract Brain action. The canister has AC 15, HP 40, and *Resistance* to all damage. The canister breaks if reduced to 0 *Hit Points*. If the canister is broken, any brains inside it are destroyed. The mi-go can create a new canister after 7 days.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The mi-go makes two Pincer attacks. It can replace one attack with a use of Dazing Ray if available.

**Pincer.** m 9, reach 5 ft. {@h}23 (4d8 + 5) Slashing damage plus 16 (3d10) Acid damage. If the target is a Medium or smaller creature, it has the *Grappled* condition (escape 15) from one of two pincers.

**Dazing Ray 4.** dex 17, one creature the mi-go can see within 60 feet. {@actSaveFail} 22 (4d10) Lightning damage plus 10 (3d6) Force damage, and the target has the *Stunned* condition until the end of the mi-go's next turn.

**Extract Brain (Requires Silver Canister).** con 17, one creature that is *Grappled* by the mi-go or that has the *Stunned* condition. {@actSaveFail} 77 (14d10) Piercing damage. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage. {@actSaveSuccessOrFail} If this damage reduces the target to 0 *Hit Points*, the mi-go kills it, removes its brain, and places the brain in its silver canister.

**Throw.** The monster throws a creature *Grappled* by it to a space it can see within 30 feet of itself that isn't in the air. dex 18, the creature thrown and each creature in the destination space. {@actSaveFail} 13 (2d6 + 6) Bludgeoning damage, and the target has the *Prone* condition. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage only.

### Necrichor


##### Necrichor

*M • undead • L E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 8 | 16 | 18 | 17 | 13 | 10 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Senses** Blindsight 120 ft.

**Languages** telepathy 120 ft. Common plus two other languages

**Challenge** 7

**Traits**

**Amorphous.** The necrichor can move through a space as narrow as 1 inch without expending extra movement to do so.

**Legendary Resistance (2/Day).** If the necrichor fails a saving throw, it can choose to succeed instead.

**Reborn by Blood.** If destroyed, the necrichor revives with all its *Hit Points* in 1d10 days in the nearest unoccupied space next to a creature of its choice that it has previously possessed with its Blood Puppeteering action. This trait doesn't function if the destroyed necrichor's remains are in a vessel affected by the *Hallow* spell or if all the necrichor's previous Blood Puppeteering targets are dead.

**Spider Climb.** The necrichor can climb difficult surfaces, including along ceilings, without needing to make an ability check.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The necrichor makes two Necrotic Burst attacks.

**Necrotic Burst.** m,r 6, reach 5 ft. or range 120 ft. {@h}12 (2d8 + 3) Force damage plus 11 (2d10) Necrotic damage, and the target has the *Poisoned* condition until the start of the necrichor's next turn. While *Poisoned*, the target can't regain *Hit Points*.

**Blood Puppeteering {@recharge}.** con 15, one *Bloodied* creature within 5 feet. Constructs and Undead automatically succeed on this save. {@actSaveFail} The target is possessed by the necrichor; the necrichor disappears, and the target has the *Incapacitated* condition and loses control of its body. The necrichor now controls the target's body, but the target retains awareness. The necrichor can't be targeted by any attack, spell, or other effect except ones that specifically target Undead. The necrichor's game statistics are the same, except it uses the possessed target's *Speed* and Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution scores. The possession lasts until the target drops to 0 *Hit Points* or the necrichor leaves it as a *Bonus Action*. When the possession ends, the necrichor appears in an unoccupied space within 5 feet of the target, and the target is immune to this necrichor's Blood Puppeteering for 24 hours. {@actSaveSuccess} The target is immune to this necrichor's Blood Puppeteering for 24 hours.

![image](book/RHW/241-22-024.necrichor.webp)

The necrichor now controls the target's body, but the target retains awareness. The necrichor can't be targeted by any attack, spell, or other effect except ones that specifically target Undead. The necrichor's game statistics are the same, except it uses the possessed target's *Speed* and Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution scores. The possession lasts until the target drops to 0 *Hit Points* or the necrichor leaves it as a *Bonus Action*. When the possession ends, the necrichor appears in an unoccupied space within 5 feet of the target, and the target is immune to this necrichor's Blood Puppeteering for 24 hours. {@actSaveSuccess} The target is immune to this necrichor's Blood Puppeteering for 24 hours.



### Nightgaunt


##### Nightgaunt

*L • aberration • C E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 17 | 20 | 16 | 13 | 16 | 10 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Senses** Blindsight 60 ft.

**Languages** understands Deep Speech but can't speak

**Challenge** 8

**Traits**

**Flyby.** The nightgaunt doesn't provoke an *Opportunity Attack* when it flies out of an enemy's reach.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The nightgaunt makes two attacks, using Claw or Barb in any combination. It can replace one attack with a use of Ascend.

**Claw.** m 8, reach 5 ft. {@h}14 (2d8 + 5) Slashing damage plus 10 (3d6) Poison damage. If the target is a Medium or smaller creature, it has the *Grappled* condition (escape 13).

**Barb.** r 8, range 60 ft. {@h}21 (6d6) Piercing damage, and the target has the *Poisoned* condition until the end of its next turn.

**Ascend.** The nightgaunt flies upward in a straight line, moving up to its *Fly Speed*. If the nightgaunt is grappling a creature, it ignores the extra movement cost to carry the creature with it.

**Bonus Actions**

**Tickle.** wis 16, one creature *Grappled* by the nightgaunt. {@actSaveFail} The target has the *Incapacitated* condition until the start of the nightgaunt's next turn.

### Priest of Osybus


##### Priest of Osybus

*S,M • humanoid • N E • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 10 | 14 | 16 | 18 | 17 | 11 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** Common plus two other languages

**Challenge** 6

**Traits**

**Tattoo of Osybus.** If damage reduces the priest to 0 *Hit Points*, it receives a random boon. Roll 1d6 to determine the boon the priest receives. The priest revives at the start of its next turn with half its *Hit Points*, and its creature type is now Undead.

**1: Dread Boon.** An aura of dread fills a 15-foot *Emanation* originating from the priest. wis 15, each non-Undead creature that starts its turn in the *Emanation*. {@actSaveFail} The target has the *Frightened* condition until the start of its next turn

**2: Ectoplasmic Boon.** Sticky ectoplasm slows creatures in a 15-foot *Emanation* originating from the priest. str 15, each creature that starts its turn in the *Emanation*. {@actSaveFail} The target's *Speed* is reduced by 10 feet until the start of its next turn.

**3: Vampiric Boon.** When the priest deals Necrotic damage to a creature, the priest gains *Temporary Hit Points* equal to the damage dealt.

**4: Blazing Boon.** The priest has a *Fly Speed* of 30 feet and *Immunity* to Fire damage.

**5: Spectral Boon.** The priest has *Resistance* to Bludgeoning, Piercing, and Slashing damage, and it has *Vulnerability* to Radiant damage. Additionally, the priest can move through other creatures and objects as if they were *Difficult Terrain*. It takes 5 (1d10) Force damage if it ends its turn inside an object.

**6: Deathly Boon.** When the priest revives with this boon, all corpses of Small or Medium Humanoids in a 30-foot *Emanation* originating from the priest rise as Skeletons under the priest's control. Additionally, at the end of each of the priest's turns, each non-Undead creature in a 5-foot *Emanation* originating from the priest takes 5 (1d10) Necrotic damage. The priest dies and this trait doesn't function if the priest receives a boon it already has or the priest's tattoo of Osybus is destroyed. The tattoo is destroyed only if the priest takes 15 damage or more on a single turn while the priest has 0 *Hit Points*.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The priest makes two attacks, using Soul Blade or Necrotic Bolt in any combination.

**Soul Blade.** m 7, reach 5 ft. {@h}9 (2d4 + 4) Piercing damage. If the target is a creature, it has the *Paralyzed* condition until the start of the priest's next turn. If this damage reduces a Medium or smaller creature to 0 *Hit Points*, the creature dies, and its soul becomes trapped in a soul tattoo on the priest's body. The soul is freed if the priest dies.

**Necrotic Bolt.** r 7, range 120 ft. {@h}30 (4d12 + 4) Necrotic damage, and the target can't regain *Hit Points* until the start of the priest's next turn.

**Bonus Actions**

**Soul Tattoo 5.** The priest magically animates a soul tattoo on its body that becomes a Shadow in an unoccupied space within 5 feet of the priest. The shadow takes its turn immediately after the priest on the same *Initiative* count, and it obeys the priest. The shadow remains animate until it is destroyed, it is more than 120 feet from the priest, the priest dies, or the priest uses this *Bonus Action* again.

**Exhausting Gaze.** wis 16, one creature the nightmare can see within 60 feet. {@actSaveFail} 14 (4d6) Psychic damage, and the target gains 1 *Exhaustion* level.

**Susceptible to Charm.** The shoggoth has *Disadvantage* on saving throws to avoid or end the *Charmed* condition.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The shoggoth makes three Pseudopod attacks. It can replace one attack with a use of Suction Burst if available.

The target no longer has the *Grappled* condition, is pushed up to 30 feet straight away from the shoggoth, and has the *Deafened* and *Stunned* conditions until the end of its next turn. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage only.

**Reactions**

**Cold Sprint.** {@actTrigger} The shoggoth is subjected to Cold damage. {@actResponse} The shoggoth moves up to its *Speed* and can make one Pseudopod attack with *Advantage*.

|---|---|---|---|---|---|

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 60 ft.

**Languages** Common

**Traits**

**Stirge Telepathy.** The strigoi can magically control stirges within 120 feet of itself using a special telepathy.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The strigoi makes two Claw attacks and one Proboscis attack.

**Claw.** m 5, reach 5 ft. {@h}10 (2d6 + 3) Slashing damage.

**Proboscis.** m 5, reach 5 ft. {@h}5 (1d4 + 3) Piercing damage plus 7 (2d6) Necrotic damage. The target's *Hit Point* maximum decreases by an amount equal to the Necrotic damage taken, and the strigoi regains *Hit Points* equal to that amount. A creature reduced to 0 *Hit Points* by this attack dies, leaving behind nothing except its skin and equipment.

**Bonus Actions**

**Protective Swarm {@recharge}.** The strigoi summons a swarm of bloodthirsty mosquitoes in a 10-foot *Emanation* originating from itself, which lasts for 1 minute or until the strigoi's *Concentration* on it ends. Whenever the swarm enters a creature's space or a creature enters the swarm or ends its turn there, that creature is subjected to the following effect (a creature makes this save only once per turn, and strigoi and stirges are unaffected). con 13. {@actSaveFail} 3 (1d6) Necrotic damage, and the target has the *Poisoned* condition until the end of its next turn.

**Actions**

**Infestation.** m 4, reach 5 ft. {@h}12 (4d4 + 2) Poison damage, or 7 (2d4 + 2) Poison damage if the swarm is *Bloodied*, and the target has the *Poisoned* condition. If the target remains *Poisoned* in this way after 1 hour, it is subjected to the following effect. con 11. {@actSaveFail} Roll 1d6: on a 1-2, the target has the *Blinded* condition; on a 3-4, the target's *Hit Point* maximum decreases by 5 (1d10); on a 5-6, the target gains 1 *Exhaustion* level. The effect lasts until the *Poisoned* condition ends. {@actSaveSuccess} The *Poisoned* condition ends.


##### Swarm of Ravenous Insects

*M • beast • U • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 3 | 15 | 14 | 1 | 12 | 1 |

**Swarm.** The swarm can occupy another creature's space and vice versa, and the swarm can move through any opening large enough for a Tiny creature. The swarm can't regain *Hit Points* or gain *Temporary Hit Points*.

**Actions**

**Ravenous Bites.** m 4, reach 5 ft. {@h}20 (4d8 + 2) Piercing damage, or 11 (2d8 + 2) Piercing damage if the swarm is *Bloodied*, and the target has the *Poisoned* condition for 1 minute as insects burrow inside it. The condition ends early if a spell or effect restores *Hit Points* to the target. While *Poisoned*, the target takes 4 (1d8) Piercing damage at the start of each of its turns. A creature reduced to 0 *Hit Points* by this damage dies.

##### Vampire Nosferatu

|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 20 | 18 | 21 | 6 | 17 | 14 |

**Skills** 

**Senses** Darkvision 120 ft.

**Languages** Common plus one other language

**Challenge** 8

**Traits**

**Blood Frenzy.** The nosferatu has *Advantage* on attack rolls against any creature that doesn't have all its *Hit Points*.

**Regeneration.** The nosferatu regains 10 *Hit Points* at the start of each of its turns if it has at least 1 *Hit Point*. If the nosferatu takes Radiant damage, this trait doesn't function on the nosferatu's next turn.

**Spider Climb.** The nosferatu can climb difficult surfaces, including along ceilings, without needing to make an ability check.

**Sunlight Hypersensitivity.** The nosferatu takes 20 Radiant damage if it starts its turn in sunlight. While in sunlight, it has *Disadvantage* on attack rolls and ability checks.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The nosferatu makes one Bite attack and two Claw attacks.

**Bite.** m 8, reach 5 ft. {@h}9 (1d8 + 5) Piercing damage plus 11 (2d10) Necrotic damage. The target's *Hit Point* maximum decreases by an amount equal to the Necrotic damage taken, and the nosferatu regains *Hit Points* equal to that amount.

**Claw.** m 8, reach 5 ft. {@h}9 (1d8 + 5) Slashing damage.

**Blood Spew 5.** con 16, each creature in a 15-foot *Cone*. {@actSaveFail} 27 (6d8) Necrotic damage, and the creature can't regain *Hit Points* for 1 minute. {@actSaveSuccess} Half damage only.

**Reactions**

**Bloodthirsty Slash.** {@actTrigger} A *Bloodied* creature the nosferatu can see within 40 feet takes damage. {@actResponse} The nosferatu moves up to its *Speed* without provoking *Opportunity Attacks* and makes a Claw attack against the triggering creature.

### Yithian


##### Yithian

*L • aberration • C N • AC  • HP  • Speed *

| STR | DEX | CON | INT | WIS | CHA |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 18 | 10 | 18 | 21 | 18 | 19 |

**Saving Throws** 

**Senses** Truesight 60 ft.

**Languages** Deep Speech; telepathy 120 ft.

**Challenge** 15

**Traits**

**Magic Resistance.** The yithian has *Advantage* on saving throws against spells and other magical effects.

**Shielded Mind.** The yithian's thoughts can't be read by any means, and other creatures can communicate with it telepathically only if it allows them.

**Actions**

**Multiattack.** The yithian makes three Pincer attacks. It can replace one attack with a use of Sup.

**Pincer.** m 9, reach 10 ft. {@h}18 (4d6 + 4) Piercing damage and the creature has the *Grappled* condition (escape 14).

**Sup.** int 18, one creature within 10 feet that has the *Grappled*, *Incapacitated*, or *Restrained* condition. {@actSaveFail} 15 (3d6 + 5) Psychic damage. The target's *Hit Points* maximum decreases by an amount equal to the damage taken, and the yithian regains *Hit Points* equal to that amount.

**Bonus Actions**

**Mind Swap {@recharge}.** int 18, one Humanoid the yithian can see within 5 feet. {@actSaveFail} The target is possessed by the yithian; the yithian disappears, and the target has the *Incapacitated* condition and loses control of its body. The yithian now controls the body; the target has no awareness of the yithian's actions. The yithian can't be targeted by any attack, spell, or other effect. The yithian's game statistics are the same, except it uses the possessed target's *Speed* and Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution modifiers. It knows everything the target knew. The possession lasts until the body drops to 0 *Hit Points* or the yithian leaves as a *Bonus Action*. When the possession ends, the yithian returns to its body, which appears within 5 feet of the target. The target is *Stunned* for 1 minute by alien memories, and it is immune to this yithian's Mind Swap for 24 hours. {@actSaveSuccess} The target is immune to Mind Swap for 24 hours.

The yithian's game statistics are the same, except it uses the possessed target's *Speed* and Strength, Dexterity, and Constitution modifiers. It knows everything the target knew. The possession lasts until the body drops to 0 *Hit Points* or the yithian leaves as a *Bonus Action*. When the possession ends, the yithian returns to its body, which appears within 5 feet of the target. The target is *Stunned* for 1 minute by alien memories, and it is immune to this yithian's Mind Swap for 24 hours. {@actSaveSuccess} The target is immune to Mind Swap for 24 hours.

# Appendix: Tarokka Deck

Tarokka fortune-telling cards originated among Vistani, who created these cards to guide their travels. Since Vistani entered the Mists, their cards have spread and gained renown as tools for divining the future and charting paths between the Domains of Dread. Now, diviners across many lands seek glimpses of what's to come and answers to unknowable questions from the tarokka. Such diviners have a saying: "No secret is safe from the tarokka."

The tarokka deck is a prop for creating mood-rich fortune-telling scenes in your adventures. It features prominently in the adventure Curse of Strahd, but you can use it to influence adventures of your own design as well.



## Composition

A tarokka deck has fifty-four cards, each of which has its own name. Forty of them compose the common deck, which is divided into four suits: coins, glyphs, stars, and swords.

Each suit contains cards numbered one through nine, plus a tenth card called the master of that suit. One can refer to a card by its suit designation or by its name. For instance, the six of stars is also known as the evoker, and the master of coins is the rogue.

The remaining fourteen cards make up the high deck and symbolize powerful and enigmatic forces.

All cards in the tarokka deck and what they represent are detailed at the end of x.



### High Deck

The cards that make up the high deck aren't considered one suit, although they all have a crown icon to mark their importance. Each card represents an important power. If one of these cards appears during a reading and contradicts the prediction of an earlier card, Vistani always assume this card takes precedence.



### Common Deck

The four suits of the common deck are described below.



#### Coins

The suit of coins symbolizes desire for personal and material gain. It also represents gluttony, lust, and obsession. On the side of good, this suit can suggest the accumulation of wealth to benefit a charity or a just cause. On the side of evil, it embodies the worst aspects of greed.



#### Glyphs

The suit of glyphs symbolizes faith, spirituality, and inner strength. It is the suit of priests and those who devote themselves to the service of a deity, a higher power, or a heightened philosophy. It symbolizes health and healing, as well as illness and disease. On the side of good, this suit represents willpower and dedication. On the side of evil, it signifies weakness of character, self-doubt, and betrayal of one's ideals or beliefs.



#### Stars

The suit of stars symbolizes the desire for personal power and control over things beyond mortal ken. It is the suit of mages, sages, and intellectuals. It also represents the triumph of magic, science, and reason over religion, mysticism, and superstition.



#### Swords

The suit of swords symbolizes aggression and violence. It is the suit of warriors, be they paladins, soldiers, or mercenaries. It also symbolizes the power of governments and leaders, whether noble or corrupt.

**Prop Tarokka Decks**

Tarokka decks for use in your game are available separately, with each card featuring imagery to aid you in creating portentous fortunes. If you don't have a tarokka deck, you can use a regular deck of playing cards instead. To do so, separate the numbered cards from the face cards and jokers, and treat them as two separate decks: the common deck (the numbered cards) and the high deck (the face cards and jokers).



#### Common Deck

Each suit in a regular deck of playing cards corresponds to a suit in the tarokka deck.

- Hearts = Glyphs
- Spades = Swords
- Diamonds = Coins
- Clubs = Stars

An ace represents a one in the tarokka deck, while a ten in a regular deck represents a master card in the tarokka deck.



#### High Deck

Each jack, queen, king, and joker corresponds to a card in the tarokka high deck.

| Playing Card | Tarokka Card |
|---|---|
| King of hearts | *RHW* |
| Queen of hearts | *RHW* |
| Jack of hearts | *RHW* |
| King of spades | *RHW* |
| Queen of spades | *RHW* |
| Jack of spades | *RHW* |
| King of diamonds | *RHW* |
| Queen of diamonds | *RHW* |
| Jack of diamonds | *RHW* |
| King of clubs | *RHW* |
| Queen of clubs | *RHW* |
| Jack of clubs | *RHW* |
| Joker 1 | *RHW* |
| Joker 2 | *RHW* |



## Tarokka Readings

Tarokka decks aid fortune tellers in revealing information about specific individuals. The focus of a tarokka reading might be the individual having their fortune told or someone else. A fortune teller randomly selects or invites another to choose what tarokka card best represents the focus of the reading. To begin the tarokka reading, this card is laid face up in position 1 in the pattern below.

![image](book/RHW/263-23-003.tarokka-positions.webp)

The fortune teller then draws four additional cards, laying one face down in each of the other numbered positions in the pattern. These positions each represent something about the focus:

- **Position 1** The focus of the reading and the lens through which the other cards are interpreted
- **Position 2** The past, something that might or might not be apparent to those other than the focus
- **Position 3** What opposes the focus, whether literal opponents or obstructing fortunes
- **Position 4** The future, an omen of what's to come and a fate that might still be changed
- **Position 5** What aids the focus, whether literal allies or advantageous events

The reading proceeds with the fortune teller revealing the significance of each card's position and what the card represents, as guided by the descriptions later in x. After a card is interpreted, the card in the next position is revealed. This continues until all five cards have been interpreted. The fortune teller might reveal more details (see the following section) or claim that the cards remain silent on certain points. The fortune teller and characters then might speculate about the reading's broader meanings. Once you're satisfied with what's revealed, the reading ends.



## Tarokka Techniques

The tarokka deck is a prop for inspiring adventures and creating dramatic fortune-telling scenes. Through a mix of creative interpretation and card manipulation, a DM can influence what the tarokka reveals and the accuracy of its revelations. Consider the following techniques during tarokka readings.



### Stacking the Deck

You can use sleight of hand tricks to ensure tarokka cards appear where you desire during a reading. Select the desired cards before the tarokka reading and put them in the order you want to draw them so you can produce them effortlessly and place them in the desired positions. Cards might be stacked on the top of the deck or drawn from the bottom. Stacking the deck is useful for ensuring specific results or creating patterns that appear repeatedly between readings. Avoid letting players notice you're stacking the deck, as it undermines the mystery of that and future tarokka readings.



### Dramatic Interpretations

![Orphir Brindletop, a member of the Keepers of the Feather, consults the tarokka](book/RHW/264-23-004.orphir-brindletop.webp)

When interpreting tarokka cards, you can elaborate on the card descriptions in x, reframing those details and adjusting them to better suit your adventure. Use these techniques to add onto and adjust the meanings of tarokka cards:

- **Broad Interpretation** Highlight broader card details, like the meanings of suits and the generalities they encompass, over card specifics.
- **Card Imagery** Focus on specifics in a card's art, like the numbers of objects or the positions of figures, to suggest a deeper meaning.
- **Contextual Meanings** Suggest that multiple cards of the same suit or in specific relation to one another have greater or lesser meaning.
- **Diviner Experience** Reveal that a card arrangement has a specific meaning, or that the fortune teller has seen it in an ominous instance before.
- **Foreshadowing** Highlight details that align with impending events of which only you are aware.
- **Leading Questions** Have a fortune teller ask questions that lead characters to connect the reading with past events or their existing knowledge.



### Manipulating Fate

You control fate in your adventures. If you don't know what a tarokka card means during a reading, note that and fulfill its prophecy in the future. For example, if the four of glyphs appears in a reading, its imagery might appear later as a shepherd NPC, a hooked staff, a wandering sheep, four runes, or the like. You can then tell the players about the connection between the image and the reading.

Additionally, listen in on players' speculations about the meaning of tarokka readings, then use those suggestions to influence future revelations in your adventures.

**High Deck**

| Name | Meaning |
|---|---|
| *RHW* | The importance of some physical object that must be obtained, protected, or destroyed at all costs |
| *RHW* | Great rage or passion; something bestial or malevolent hiding in plain sight or lurking just below the surface |
| *RHW* | Defeat, failure, and despair; the loss of something or someone important, without which one feels incomplete |

| *RHW* | The looming past; the return of an old enemy or the discovery of a secret buried long ago |
| *RHW* | The imminent death of one rightly or wrongly convicted of a crime; false accusations and unjust prosecution |
| *RHW* | Death; disastrous loss of wealth or property, a horrible defeat, or the end of a bloodline |
| *RHW* | A being of great importance whose life is in danger (who might be helpless or simply unaware of the peril) |
| *RHW* | The presence of a spy or a minion of some greater power; an encounter with a puppet or an underling |
| *RHW* | Something unexpected or mysterious that can't be avoided; a great quest or journey that will try one's spirit |
| *RHW* | A hidden source of information; a fortunate turn of events; a secret potential for good |
| *RHW* | Inspiration and keen intellect; a future event, the outcome of which will hinge on a clever mind |
| *RHW* | One who has been compromised or led astray by temptation or foolishness; one who tempts others for evil ends |

|---|---|---|

| Eight of swords | *RHW* | All that is wrong with leadership; those who rule through fear and violence |
